Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
8 min
Nass Overrides Qiyas: The Case of Hayd and Nifas
Usul rule: nass on khilaf qiyas and its limitation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a nass that overrides qiyas and apply the Hanafi principle that such nass does not extend beyond its specific case.

Core Idea
A nass contradicting qiyas is confined to its text; it cannot be extended by analogy.

This lesson examines a key Hanafi usul principle: when a nass (explicit text) overrides qiyas (analogy), the resulting ruling is limited to the specific case mentioned. The example of purity as a condition for fasting during menstruation illustrates this. We will see how this principle guides the distinction between making up missed prayers and fasts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the underlying qiyas
Determine what the ruling would be by analogy in the absence of text. Fasting is valid despite minor impurity and janaba, so by analogy it should be valid during hayd and nifas.
Qiyas would make purity unnecessary for fasting.
2
Identify the nass that overrides qiyas
Find the explicit textual evidence. The hadith from Aisha (ra) shows the Prophet commanded women to make up fasts but not prayers, establishing purity as a condition for fasting.
This is a nass on khilaf qiyas.
3
State the Hanafi rule: nass on khilaf qiyas la yata'adda
The rule states that a textual ruling that contradicts analogy does not extend beyond its specific context. It is restricted to the cases explicitly mentioned.
This is a well-established usul principle.
4
Apply the rule to the qada distinction
The condition of purity for fasting is not extended to making up (qada) of prayers because that would extend the nass beyond its scope. The hadith only mentions the obligation to make up fasts, not prayers.
The nass does not imply a condition for qada of prayers.
5
Note the role of hardship (haraj)
The text also mentions hardship as a reason: making up many prayers in a short period is burdensome, especially with long nifas, while making up fasts over months is easier. This supports not extending the condition to qada of prayer.
Hardship (haraj) is a subsidiary consideration, not the primary principle.

بيان المرض
وهذا مما وافق فيه القياس النقل، وقد جعلت الطهارة عنهما شرطا لصحة الصوم نصا،
الحيض والنفاس
بخلاف القياس؛ إذ الصوم يتأدّى بالحدث والجنابة فينبغي أن يتأدّى بالحيض والنفاس لو لا النص، وقد تقرّر من ههنا أن لا تُؤدّي الصلاة والصوم في حالة الحيض والنفاس،
فإِذَنْ لا بد أن يفرّق بين قضائهما، وهو أن شرط الطهارة فيه خلاف القياس.
أي الفرق
الصوم
فلم يتعد إلى القضاء مع أنه أنه لا حرج في قضائه؛ إذ قضاء صوم عشرة أيام في ما بين أحد عشر شهرًا مما لا يضيق وإن فرض أن يستوعب النفاس شهر رمضان كاملة فمع أنه نادر لا يُناط به أحكام الشرع أيضًا لا حرج فيه؛ إذ قضاء صوم شهر واحد في أحد عشر شهراً مما لا حرج فيه. بخلاف الصلاة فإن في قضاء صلاة عشرة أيام في كل عشرين يوما مما يفضي إلى الحرج
غالبًا، فلهذا نعفى ،والموت، عطف على ما قبله وهو آخر الأمور المعترضة السماوية، وأنه ينافي الأهلية
أي قوله: الصغر
النقل: وهو ما روى البخاري ومسلم أن فاطمة بنت قيس قالت: يا رسول الله، إني امرأة أُستحاض فلا أطهر أفَأَدَعُ الصلاة؟ فقال: "لا، إنما ذلك عرق وليس بحيض، فإذا أقبلت حيضتك فدعي الصلاة، وإذا أدبرت فاغسلي عنك الدم ثم صلّي" إلخ. (السنبلي) نصا : فإنه منع النبي الحائض عن الصوم، وثبت منه منع النفساء أيضا عنه دلالة، في "المشكاة" عن عدي بن ثابت عن أبيه عن جده عن النبي النبي أنه قال في المستحاضة: "تدع الصلاة أيام أقرائها التي كانت تحيض فيها، ثم تغتسل وتتوضأ عند كل صلاة وتصوم وتصلي". (رواه أبوداود) (القمر) نصا المراد به ما رواه الترمذي عن عائشة لالها قالت: كنا نحيض عند رسول الله ، ثم نطهر، فيأمرنا بقضاء ، الصيام ولا يأمرنا بقضاء الصلاة إلخ، فعلم منه : أن النساء ما كن يَصُمن في عهد النبي ، وأنه لا قضاء للصلاة وللصوم قضاء، فثبت أن الطهارة من الحيض شرط للصوم. (السنبلي) فلم يتعد أي هذا الاشتراط إلى القضاء، فإن النصوص الواردة على خلاف القياس لا تتعدّى عن مورد النص. (القمر) في قضاء صلاة إلخ والنفاس في العادة أكثر من مدة الحيض، فتضاعف الواجبات فيه أيضًا، وهو مستلزم للحرج، وهو مدفوع.(السنبلي) إلى الحرج غالبًا والنفاس عادةً أكثر من مدة الحيض، فيتصوّر الحرج في قضاء صلوات حالة النفاس أيضًا. (القمر) وأنه ينافي إلخ فإن الموت هادم لأساس التكليف.

أحكام الدنيا ممّا فيه تكليف حتى بطلت الزكاة وسائر القرب عنه، وإنما حَصّ بيان للأحكام الزكاة أوّلاً دفعًا لوهم من يتوهم أنها عبادة مالية لا تتعلق بفعل الميت، فيؤدي بها الولي
الزكاة
كما زعم الشافعي دون المال فهي تساوي الصلاة والصوم في البطلان. وإنما يبقى عليه المأثم لا غير، فإن شاء الله عفا عنه بفضله وكرمه، وإن شاء عذبه بعدله وحكمته، وهذا هو حال حق الله تعالى وأما حق العباد فلا يخلو إما أن يكون حقا للغير عليه، أو حقا له على الغير، وأشار إلى الأول بقوله : وما شرع عليه لحاجة غيره، فإن كان
وذلك ؛ لأنها عبادة لا بد لها من الاختيار، والمقصود منها الأداء،

الميت
حقا متعلقا بالعين يبقى ببقائه كالمرهون يتعلّق به حق المرتهن، والمستأجر يتعلّق به حق
أي لا بفعل الميت
العين
المستأجر، والمبيع يتعلق به حق المشتري، والوديعة يتعلّق بها حق المودع، فإن هذه الأعيان يأخذها صاحب الحق أوّلاً من غير أن تدخل في التركة، وتقسم على الغرماء أو الورثة.
وإن كان دينًا لم يبق بمجرد الذمة حتى يضم إليها، أي إلى الذمة.
مال أو ما يؤكد به الذمم، وهو ذمّة الكفيل يعني ما لم يترك مالاً
مما فيه تكليف إلخ لأن الموت هادم لأساس التكليف؛ لأنه عجز كله عن إتيان العبادات أداءً وقضاء، ولأنه ذهب من دار الابتلاء إلى دار الجزاء. (السنبلي) حتى بطلت أي سقطت الزكاة عن الميت ولا يجب أداؤها من تركته، وسائر القرب أي العبادات كالصلاة والحج والصوم القمر وذلك أي الدفع؛ لأنها أي الزكاة عبادة كالصلاة والصوم. (القمر) والمقصود منها إلخ : ألا ترى أنه لو ظفر الفقير بمال الزكاة ليس له أخذها ولا تسقط به.(القمر) فهي: أي الزكاة تساوي الصلاة والصوم في البطلان وقال بحر العلوم مولانا عبد العلي يه: هذا إذا كان لم يوص، وأما لو أوصى فالعبادات المالية كالزكاة وفدية الصوم والصلاة تؤدّى من المأثم أي إثم الواجبات المتروكة (القمر) فإن كان حقا إلخ أي هذا القسم الثاني من أقسام أحكام الدنيا ينقسم إلى عدة أقسام: الأول منها هذا والثاني ما بينه بقوله : وإن كان دينًا إلخ، وترك البعض الذي بينه في الكتب الأخرى
ثلث ماله. (القمر)
من الأصول. (السنبلي وإن كان أي حق الغير دينًا لم يبق إلخ فإن ذمة الوجوب قد بطلت بالموت. (القمر)
Statement of legal capacity. Statement of illness. This is where analogy aligns with transmitted text. And the requirement of purity from them (menstruation and postpartum bleeding) as a condition for the validity of fasting is established by text, contrary to analogy; for fasting is performed despite minor impurity and janaba, so it should be performed during menstruation and postpartum bleeding if not for the text. And it is established here that prayer and fasting are not performed during menstruation and postpartum bleeding. Therefore, there must be a distinction between making them up, which is that the condition of purity in it is contrary to analogy. (Meaning: the distinction is for fasting.) So it (the condition) does not extend to making up, because there is no hardship in making it up; for making up ten days of fasting within eleven months is not constraining, even if it is supposed that postpartum bleeding covers the entire month of Ramadan, though rare and not used as a basis for legal rulings, also there is no hardship; for making up one month of fasting in eleven months involves no hardship. Unlike prayer, for making up ten days of prayers within every twenty days generally leads to hardship. Thus we exempt it. And death, conjoined to what precedes, and it is the last of the celestial interrupting matters, and it negates legal capacity. That is his statement: childhood. The transmitted evidence is what al-Bukhari and Muslim narrated that Fatima bint Qais said: O Messenger of Allah, I am a woman who experiences istihadah (irregular bleeding) and I do not become pure, should I abandon prayer? He said: "No, that is a vein and not menstruation. When your menstruation comes, leave prayer, and when it ends, wash the blood from yourself and then pray" etc. (al-Sanbali) Textually: for the Prophet forbade the menstruating woman from fasting, and it is established that he forbade the postpartum woman by indication. In al-Mishkat from Adi ibn Thabit from his father from his grandfather from the Prophet that he said regarding the mustahadah: "She leaves prayer during the days of her menses which she used to menstruate, then she takes a bath and performs wudu for every prayer, and she fasts and prays." (Narrated by Abu Dawud) (al-Qamar) Textually: what is intended is what al-Tirmidhi narrated from Aisha that she said: We used to menstruate during the time of the Messenger of Allah, then we would become pure, and he would command us to make up the fasts and not command us to make up the prayers. So it is known from this that women did not fast during the Prophet's era, and that there is no making up for prayer, and making up is required for fasting. Thus it is established that purity from menstruation is a condition for fasting. (al-Sanbali) So it did not extend, meaning this requirement to making up, for textual rulings that contradict analogy do not extend beyond the scope of the text. (al-Qamar) Regarding making up prayer etc. And postpartum bleeding usually lasts longer than the menstrual period, so the obligations also multiply in it, which entails hardship, and it is repelled. (al-Sanbali) To hardship generally. And postpartum bleeding usually lasts longer than the menstrual period, so hardship is conceivable in making up prayers during the postpartum state as well. (al-Qamar) And that it negates etc. For death demolishes the foundation of obligation. Statement of legal capacity in statement of illness. The rulings of this world that involve obligation, so zakat and all other acts of worship become void for the deceased. And the mention of zakat first is to repel the illusion of one who imagines that it is a financial act of worship not related to the action of the deceased, so the guardian may perform it for the deceased, as al-Shafi'i claimed, without wealth. So it (zakat) equals prayer and fasting in nullity. Only sin remains upon him; if Allah wills, He forgives him by His bounty and generosity, and if He wills, He punishes him by His justice and wisdom. This is the case regarding the rights of Allah. As for the rights of people, they are either a right owed to another, or a right owed to oneself against another. He indicated the first by his statement: 'And what is prescribed upon him due to the need of others.' If it is a right related to a specific item, it remains by its continued existence, like the mortgaged item being subject to the right of the mortgagee, the leased item subject to the right of the lessee, the sold item subject to the right of the buyer, the deposit subject to the right of the depositor. For these items, their owner takes them first without them entering the estate, and they are distributed among creditors or heirs. And if it is a debt, it does not remain merely by the liability (dhimma) unless wealth is added to it, or something that strengthens the liability, which is the liability of a guarantor, meaning if he did not leave wealth. (al-Sanbali) 'That involves obligation etc.' because death demolishes the foundation of obligation; because it is a complete inability to perform acts of worship by performance and by making up, and because he has gone from the abode of trial to the abode of recompense. (al-Sanbali) 'So zakat becomes void from the deceased and its performance is not obligatory from his estate, and all other acts of worship like prayer, hajj, and fasting. (al-Qamar) 'That is to repel; because zakat is an act of worship like prayer and fasting. (al-Qamar) 'And the purpose of it etc.' Do you not see that if a poor person finds zakat wealth, he has no right to take it and it is not discharged by that. (al-Qamar) So it (zakat) equals prayer and fasting in voidness. And Bahar al-Ulum Mawlana Abd al-Ali said: This is if he did not make a will. But if he made a will, then financial acts of worship like zakat and the expiation for missed fasts and prayers are performed from one third of his estate. (al-Qamar) 'For the sin, i.e., the sin of omitted obligations. (al-Qamar) 'If it is a right etc.' That is, the second division of the categories of worldly rulings is divided into several sections: the first is this, and the second is what he clarified by his statement: 'And if it is a debt' etc., and he omitted some that he clarified in other books. (al-Sanbali) 'And if, i.e., the right of another is a debt, it does not remain etc.' For the liability of obligation has become void by death. (al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage from a Hanafi usul work explains exceptions to legal capacity (ahliyyah) caused by natural states: menstruation (hayd), postpartum bleeding (nifas), and death. The author first discusses that the condition of purity (taharah) for fasting during hayd and nifas is established by textual evidence (nass) against analogy (qiyas). Normally, fasting is valid with minor impurity or janaba, so by analogy it should be valid during hayd, but the text prohibits it. The key legal principle is that such exceptional rulings are confined to their specific cases and not extended by analogy. This is why making up missed fasts is required but making up missed prayers is not—the hardship of making up prayers is much greater, especially for nifas which can last long. The author then turns to death, stating that it demolishes the foundation of obligation (taklif). All acts of worship (e.g., zakat, prayer, fasting) become void; only sin remains, subject to Allah's will. However, rights of others (like debts and specific property) persist: rights attached to specific items (e.g., collateral, lease, sale) are taken by the owner before division of the estate; debts do not automatically remain but require a source of payment or a guarantor. The text also mentions a dispute with al-Shafi'i regarding paying zakat from the deceased's estate—Hanafi holds it is not obligatory unless willed.

Key Terms
أهلية (ahliyyah): Legal capacity; the qualification of a person to acquire rights and incur obligations.
نص (nass): Explicit textual ruling from Quran or hadith that overrides analogical reasoning (qiyas).
قياس (qiyas): Analogical deduction from an existing ruling to a new case due to shared effective cause (illa).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi usul principle presented, why is a woman not required to make up missed prayers due to menstruation?
A) Because prayer is an act of worship that cannot be made up at all.
B) Because the nass that prohibits prayer during hayd is confined to its time; the condition does not extend to qada.
C) Because making up prayers is not commanded in the Quran.
D) Because the Prophet only commanded making up fasts, not prayers, due to hardship.

Key Takeaway
A textual ruling that contradicts analogy is strictly limited to its specific context and cannot be extended by analogy to other cases.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
8 min
Death Nullifies Obligations: The Hanafi Position on Zakat and Other Acts
Effect of death on legal capacity and the fate of obligations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi view that death voids all acts of worship and explain the exception for rights of others.

Core Idea
Death demolishes obligation; all acts of worship become void, only sin remains.

This lesson examines the effect of death on legal capacity. The Hanafi school holds that death completely terminates the foundation of obligation (taklif), rendering all unperformed acts of worship void. However, rights of people, such as debts and specific property rights, persist. We will also explore the dispute with al-Shafi'i regarding whether zakat must be paid from the deceased's estate.

Guided Path
1
State the general principle: death demolishes obligation
The text states that death demolishes the foundation of obligation because the deceased has left the abode of trial and is unable to perform acts of worship.
This is a fundamental usul axiom.
2
Apply to acts of worship: zakat, prayer, fasting become void
All acts of worship that require personal performance (like prayer, fasting, zakat) become void upon death. They are not obligatory on the estate unless the deceased made a will.
Financial acts are still 'ibadat; they require intention and choice.
3
Note the dispute with al-Shafi'i on zakat
Al-Shafi'i holds that zakat is a financial right of Allah attached to wealth, so the guardian must pay it from the estate. Hanafi refutes this, equating zakat to other acts of worship.
The practical difference is whether the estate must pay zakat.
4
Distinguish between rights of Allah and rights of people
Rights of Allah (acts of worship) are voided by death. Rights of people (debts, collateral, leases) survive because they are based on need and justice.
Property rights (like mortgages) are taken before estate division.
5
Explain that debts require payment from estate or guarantor
A debt does not automatically remain binding on the deceased's dhimma after death. It must be paid from left wealth or by a guarantor.
The text says 'unless wealth is added to it or a guarantor'.

حقا متعلقا بالعين يبقى ببقائه كالمرهون يتعلّق به حق المرتهن، والمستأجر يتعلّق به حق
أي لا بفعل الميت
العين
المستأجر، والمبيع يتعلق به حق المشتري، والوديعة يتعلّق بها حق المودع، فإن هذه الأعيان يأخذها صاحب الحق أوّلاً من غير أن تدخل في التركة، وتقسم على الغرماء أو الورثة.
وإن كان دينًا لم يبق بمجرد الذمة حتى يضم إليها، أي إلى الذمة.
مال أو ما يؤكد به الذمم، وهو ذمّة الكفيل يعني ما لم يترك مالاً
مما فيه تكليف إلخ لأن الموت هادم لأساس التكليف؛ لأنه عجز كله عن إتيان العبادات أداءً وقضاء، ولأنه ذهب من دار الابتلاء إلى دار الجزاء. (السنبلي) حتى بطلت أي سقطت الزكاة عن الميت ولا يجب أداؤها من تركته، وسائر القرب أي العبادات كالصلاة والحج والصوم القمر وذلك أي الدفع؛ لأنها أي الزكاة عبادة كالصلاة والصوم. (القمر) والمقصود منها إلخ : ألا ترى أنه لو ظفر الفقير بمال الزكاة ليس له أخذها ولا تسقط به.(القمر) فهي: أي الزكاة تساوي الصلاة والصوم في البطلان وقال بحر العلوم مولانا عبد العلي يه: هذا إذا كان لم يوص، وأما لو أوصى فالعبادات المالية كالزكاة وفدية الصوم والصلاة تؤدّى من المأثم أي إثم الواجبات المتروكة (القمر) فإن كان حقا إلخ أي هذا القسم الثاني من أقسام أحكام الدنيا ينقسم إلى عدة أقسام: الأول منها هذا والثاني ما بينه بقوله : وإن كان دينًا إلخ، وترك البعض الذي بينه في الكتب الأخرى
ثلث ماله. (القمر)
من الأصول. (السنبلي وإن كان أي حق الغير دينًا لم يبق إلخ فإن ذمة الوجوب قد بطلت بالموت. (القمر)
Statement of legal capacity. Statement of illness. This is where analogy aligns with transmitted text. And the requirement of purity from them (menstruation and postpartum bleeding) as a condition for the validity of fasting is established by text, contrary to analogy; for fasting is performed despite minor impurity and janaba, so it should be performed during menstruation and postpartum bleeding if not for the text. And it is established here that prayer and fasting are not performed during menstruation and postpartum bleeding. Therefore, there must be a distinction between making them up, which is that the condition of purity in it is contrary to analogy. (Meaning: the distinction is for fasting.) So it (the condition) does not extend to making up, because there is no hardship in making it up; for making up ten days of fasting within eleven months is not constraining, even if it is supposed that postpartum bleeding covers the entire month of Ramadan, though rare and not used as a basis for legal rulings, also there is no hardship; for making up one month of fasting in eleven months involves no hardship. Unlike prayer, for making up ten days of prayers within every twenty days generally leads to hardship. Thus we exempt it. And death, conjoined to what precedes, and it is the last of the celestial interrupting matters, and it negates legal capacity. That is his statement: childhood. The transmitted evidence is what al-Bukhari and Muslim narrated that Fatima bint Qais said: O Messenger of Allah, I am a woman who experiences istihadah (irregular bleeding) and I do not become pure, should I abandon prayer? He said: "No, that is a vein and not menstruation. When your menstruation comes, leave prayer, and when it ends, wash the blood from yourself and then pray" etc. (al-Sanbali) Textually: for the Prophet forbade the menstruating woman from fasting, and it is established that he forbade the postpartum woman by indication. In al-Mishkat from Adi ibn Thabit from his father from his grandfather from the Prophet that he said regarding the mustahadah: "She leaves prayer during the days of her menses which she used to menstruate, then she takes a bath and performs wudu for every prayer, and she fasts and prays." (Narrated by Abu Dawud) (al-Qamar) Textually: what is intended is what al-Tirmidhi narrated from Aisha that she said: We used to menstruate during the time of the Messenger of Allah, then we would become pure, and he would command us to make up the fasts and not command us to make up the prayers. So it is known from this that women did not fast during the Prophet's era, and that there is no making up for prayer, and making up is required for fasting. Thus it is established that purity from menstruation is a condition for fasting. (al-Sanbali) So it did not extend, meaning this requirement to making up, for textual rulings that contradict analogy do not extend beyond the scope of the text. (al-Qamar) Regarding making up prayer etc. And postpartum bleeding usually lasts longer than the menstrual period, so the obligations also multiply in it, which entails hardship, and it is repelled. (al-Sanbali) To hardship generally. And postpartum bleeding usually lasts longer than the menstrual period, so hardship is conceivable in making up prayers during the postpartum state as well. (al-Qamar) And that it negates etc. For death demolishes the foundation of obligation. Statement of legal capacity in statement of illness. The rulings of this world that involve obligation, so zakat and all other acts of worship become void for the deceased. And the mention of zakat first is to repel the illusion of one who imagines that it is a financial act of worship not related to the action of the deceased, so the guardian may perform it for the deceased, as al-Shafi'i claimed, without wealth. So it (zakat) equals prayer and fasting in nullity. Only sin remains upon him; if Allah wills, He forgives him by His bounty and generosity, and if He wills, He punishes him by His justice and wisdom. This is the case regarding the rights of Allah. As for the rights of people, they are either a right owed to another, or a right owed to oneself against another. He indicated the first by his statement: 'And what is prescribed upon him due to the need of others.' If it is a right related to a specific item, it remains by its continued existence, like the mortgaged item being subject to the right of the mortgagee, the leased item subject to the right of the lessee, the sold item subject to the right of the buyer, the deposit subject to the right of the depositor. For these items, their owner takes them first without them entering the estate, and they are distributed among creditors or heirs. And if it is a debt, it does not remain merely by the liability (dhimma) unless wealth is added to it, or something that strengthens the liability, which is the liability of a guarantor, meaning if he did not leave wealth. (al-Sanbali) 'That involves obligation etc.' because death demolishes the foundation of obligation; because it is a complete inability to perform acts of worship by performance and by making up, and because he has gone from the abode of trial to the abode of recompense. (al-Sanbali) 'So zakat becomes void from the deceased and its performance is not obligatory from his estate, and all other acts of worship like prayer, hajj, and fasting. (al-Qamar) 'That is to repel; because zakat is an act of worship like prayer and fasting. (al-Qamar) 'And the purpose of it etc.' Do you not see that if a poor person finds zakat wealth, he has no right to take it and it is not discharged by that. (al-Qamar) So it (zakat) equals prayer and fasting in voidness. And Bahar al-Ulum Mawlana Abd al-Ali said: This is if he did not make a will. But if he made a will, then financial acts of worship like zakat and the expiation for missed fasts and prayers are performed from one third of his estate. (al-Qamar) 'For the sin, i.e., the sin of omitted obligations. (al-Qamar) 'If it is a right etc.' That is, the second division of the categories of worldly rulings is divided into several sections: the first is this, and the second is what he clarified by his statement: 'And if it is a debt' etc., and he omitted some that he clarified in other books. (al-Sanbali) 'And if, i.e., the right of another is a debt, it does not remain etc.' For the liability of obligation has become void by death. (al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage from a Hanafi usul work explains exceptions to legal capacity (ahliyyah) caused by natural states: menstruation (hayd), postpartum bleeding (nifas), and death. The author first discusses that the condition of purity (taharah) for fasting during hayd and nifas is established by textual evidence (nass) against analogy (qiyas). Normally, fasting is valid with minor impurity or janaba, so by analogy it should be valid during hayd, but the text prohibits it. The key legal principle is that such exceptional rulings are confined to their specific cases and not extended by analogy. This is why making up missed fasts is required but making up missed prayers is not—the hardship of making up prayers is much greater, especially for nifas which can last long. The author then turns to death, stating that it demolishes the foundation of obligation (taklif). All acts of worship (e.g., zakat, prayer, fasting) become void; only sin remains, subject to Allah's will. However, rights of others (like debts and specific property) persist: rights attached to specific items (e.g., collateral, lease, sale) are taken by the owner before division of the estate; debts do not automatically remain but require a source of payment or a guarantor. The text also mentions a dispute with al-Shafi'i regarding paying zakat from the deceased's estate—Hanafi holds it is not obligatory unless willed.

Key Terms
أهلية (ahliyyah): Legal capacity; the qualification of a person to acquire rights and incur obligations.
نص (nass): Explicit textual ruling from Quran or hadith that overrides analogical reasoning (qiyas).
قياس (qiyas): Analogical deduction from an existing ruling to a new case due to shared effective cause (illa).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view, why do acts of worship become void upon death?
A) Because the deceased's wealth is no longer subject to obligation.
B) Because death demolishes the foundation of obligation (taklif), and worship requires personal performance.
C) Because the deceased has already been judged on the Day of Judgment.
D) Because the family can pray and fast on behalf of the deceased.

Key Takeaway
Death voids all personal acts of worship; only the rights of others, such as debts and property claims, survive and must be fulfilled from the estate.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate

Priority of Rights in the Deceased's Estate: The Need-Priority Principle
Establishes order of rights by priority of needs with analogical reasoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule of prioritizing needs to determine the order of rights in a deceased's estate and explain the continuity of kitaba after death using analogical reasoning.

Core Idea
The deceased's need for burial is stronger than all other claims: tajhiz precedes debts, bequests, and inheritance.

This passage from Al-Nur al-Anwar explains a core Hanafi usul principle: when multiple rights compete, the strongest need takes precedence. The author applies this to the deceased's estate, deriving a clear order: burial, debts, bequests, inheritance. The same reasoning extends to the kitaba contract, which continues after death because the need for freedom or payment persists. Understanding this principle is essential for grasping how Hanafi jurists prioritize competing claims using rational analogy (qiyas) and custom (urf).

Guided Path
1
Identify the four categories of rights after death
List the rights mentioned in order: tajhiz (burial preparation), debts (dayn), bequests (wasiyya), and inheritance (mirath). Note the order and the rationale given for each.
The text explicitly states: 'then, then, then.'
2
Understand the rationale: the strongest need takes precedence
Each right is prioritized based on the strength of need. Tajhiz is first because the deceased's need for burial is 'stronger than all needs.' Debts follow to exonerate the soul. Bequests are from one-third because they benefit the deceased in the afterlife. Inheritance is last as it comforts the soul through heirs' prayers.
This reflects the usul principle that need determines priority (taqdim al-ahamm).
3
Analyze the analogical argument (qiyas)
The author draws an analogy: just as a living person's clothing is given precedence over debts (because clothing is essential), so too is burial given precedence over debts. This is a qiyas jali (clear analogy) between life and death.
The key illa (effective cause) is the essence of the need.
4
Distinguish between rights attached to specific assets and general rights
The commentator (Al-Qamar) clarifies that the priority of tajhiz over debts applies only when the creditor's right is not attached to a specific asset (like a pawn or unpaid purchase). If the debt is secured by a specific asset, that asset is exempted from the general order.
This shows that the principle is not absolute but subject to exceptions.
5
Extend the principle to the kitaba contract
The passage argues that because death does not eliminate need, the kitaba continues whether the master or the mukatib dies, provided the mukatib leaves sufficient wealth. The need for freedom or the master's need for wala' and payment justify the contract's persistence.
This is an extension of the same need-priority logic to a contractual setting.

Source Text

بيان الأهلية غير مطالب به في الحال لوجود المانع في حقه وزواله في حق الكفيل، وأشار إلى الثاني الإفلاس بقوله: وإن كان حقا له، أي المشروع حقا للميت بقي له ما تقضى به الحاجة، ولذلك قدم تجهيزه؛ لأن حاجته إلى التجهيز أقوى من جميع الحوائج. ثم ديونه؛ لأن الحاجة إليها أمس لإبراء ذمته، بخلاف الوصية فإنها تبرّع. ثم وصاياه من ثلثه؛ لأن الحاجة إليها أقوى من حق الورثة، والثلثان حقهم الورثة فقط. ثم وجب الميراث بطريق الخلافة عنه نظرا له؛ لأن روحه يتشفّى بغنائهم، ولعلهم يُوَفَّقون بسبب حسن المعاش للدعاء والصدقة له. فيصرف إلى من يتصل به نسبًا، أي قرابةً، أو سببًا أي زوجيةً، أو دينًا بلا نسب أو سبب، يعني يوضع في بيت المال تُقضى به حوائج المسلمين، ولهذا، أي ولأن الموت لا ينافي الحاجة بقيت الكتابة بعد موت المولى، وبعد موت المكاتب عن وفاء، فإذا مات المولى وبقي المكاتب حيا يؤدّي الكتابة إلى ورثته لاحتياج المولى إلى الولاء وبدل الكتابة، وكذا إذا مات المكاتب لوجود المانع وهو الإفلاس وعدم التملك في حقه أي في حق الأصل، وزواله أي زوال المانع. (القمر) أي المشروع أي الحكم الذي شرع للعبد. (القمر) قدّم تجهيزه: أي على سائر الحقوق، وإنما يقدم التجهيز على الدين، وإذا لم يكن حق الغريم متعلقا بالعين، أما إذا كان متعلقا بالعين كما في المرهون والمشترى قبل القبض فصاحب الحق أحق بالعين وأولى بها من صرفها إلى التجهيز لتعلّق حقه بالعين تعلقا مؤكدا، كذا في "الكشف". (القمر) أقوى ألا ترى أن لباسه في حياته مقدّم على ديونه كذا ههنا (القمر) من ثلثه أي من ثلث ما بقي بعد التجهيز وقضاء الديون (القمر) أقوى لأن له نفعًا في إنفاذ الوصية في الآخرة.(القمر) بطريق الخلافة عنه والفرق بين الخلافة والنيابة: هذا إن الخلافة إقامة الشخص مقام الآخر ضرورةً بلا اشتراط واختيار، والنيابة إقامة الغير مقام الشخص الآخر على العكس ذلك ] قرابة من أصحاب الفروض والعصبات وذوي الأرحام. (القمر) أي: زوجية هذا التفسير بيان أحد أنواع الاتصال السبي، وإلا فمولى الموالاة ومولى العتاقة أيضًا مما يتصل سببًا بالميت. (القمر) لاحتياج المولى إلخ ليقضى منه ديونه مثلاً، والولاء ميراث يستحقه المرء بسبب العتق، كذا قيل.(القمر) عن وفاء أي مال وافٍ لبدل الكتابة، وبقي المولى حيًّا يؤدّي الوفاء ورثة المكاتب إلى المولى أي مع وفاء يحكم ببقاء الكتابة حتى يؤدّي لحاجته إلى تحصيل الحرّية حتى يكون ما بقي عنه ميرا لورثته، ويعتق أولاده المولودون المكاتب المتوفى المكاتب الميت والمشترون في حال الكتابة، ويعتق هو في آخر جزء من أجزاء حياته. وإنما قلنا: "عن وفاء"؛ لأنه إذا لم يترك وفاء لا ينبغى لأولاده أن يكسبوا الوفاء ويؤدّوه إلى المولى.
Statement of legal capacity: He is not demanded immediately due to the existence of an impediment in his right and its removal in the right of the guarantor, and he pointed to the second: insolvency by his saying: 'And if it is a right for him' i.e., the legislated right for the deceased remains for him what fulfills his need, therefore his preparation (tajhiz) is given precedence; because his need for preparation is stronger than all needs. Then his debts; because the need for them is more pressing to exonerate his liability, unlike the bequest which is a donation. Then his bequests from his third; because the need for them is stronger than the right of the heirs, and the two-thirds are exclusively their right. Then inheritance is obligatory by way of succession (khilafa) on his behalf, considering him; because his spirit is comforted by their enrichment, and perhaps they will be granted success through good livelihood to pray and give charity for him. So it is given to those connected to him by lineage, i.e., kinship, or by cause, i.e., marriage, or by religion without lineage or cause, meaning it is placed in the public treasury to fulfill the needs of Muslims. And for this, i.e., because death does not negate need, the kitaba (contract of manumission) remains after the death of the master, and after the death of the mukatib (slave under contract) with sufficient wealth. So if the master dies and the mukatib remains alive, he performs the kitaba payments to his heirs, due to the master's need for wala' (loyalty) and the substitute of the kitaba. Likewise if the mukatib dies due to the existence of the impediment, which is insolvency and lack of ownership in his right, i.e., in the right of the original, and its removal, i.e., the removal of the impediment. (Al-Qamar): i.e., the legislated, i.e., the ruling that was legislated for the slave. (Al-Qamar): He gave precedence to his preparation: i.e., over all other rights. And preparation is given precedence over debt only if the creditor's right is not tied to a specific asset. But if it is tied to a specific asset, as in a pawned item or an item purchased before taking possession, then the right-holder is more entitled to the asset and it has more priority than spending it on preparation, because his right is firmly attached to the asset. Thus in 'al-Kashf'. (Al-Qamar): Stronger: do you not see that his clothing during his lifetime is given precedence over his debts? Likewise here. (Al-Qamar): From his third: i.e., from the third of what remains after preparation and repayment of debts. (Al-Qamar): Stronger: because he has benefit in executing the bequest in the afterlife. (Al-Qamar): By way of succession from him, and the difference between succession (khilafa) and deputyship (niyaba): that succession is placing a person in the position of another out of necessity without stipulation and choice, while deputyship is placing another in the position of the person in the opposite manner. (From) relatives: among those with prescribed shares, agnates, and uterine relatives. (Al-Qamar): i.e., marriage: this interpretation is an explanation of one type of connection by cause; otherwise the patron of clientage and the patron of emancipation are also connected to the deceased by cause. (Al-Qamar): For the need of the master etc.: so that his debts may be paid from it, for example, and wala' is an inheritance deserved by a person due to emancipation, as it is said. (Al-Qamar): With sufficient wealth: i.e., wealth sufficient for the kitaba payment. And if the master remains alive, the heirs of the mukatib pay the kitaba payment to the master, i.e., with sufficiency. The kitaba is judged to remain until he pays, due to his need to obtain freedom so that what remains from him becomes inheritance for his heirs, and his children born during the kitaba are freed, and the purchasers during the kitaba, and he is freed in the last part of his life. And we only said 'with sufficient wealth' because if he does not leave sufficient wealth, his children should not earn the wealth and pay it to the master.
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage is a commentary establishing the order of rights in the deceased's estate based on the principle of prioritizing the strongest need. The author explains that the first right is the preparation of the body (tajhiz) for burial, because the deceased's need for a proper burial is the strongest of all needs, even stronger than the need to repay debts. After burial, the debts are paid to clear the deceased's liability. Then bequests are executed from one-third of the remaining estate, because the need to fulfill a bequest for the afterlife is stronger than the heirs' claim to that portion. Finally, the remaining two-thirds are distributed as inheritance to relatives, which benefits the deceased's soul indirectly. The passage then extends this principle to the contract of manumission (kitaba): even after death, the need for freedom or for wala' and payment continues, so the kitaba remains in effect if the mukatib leaves sufficient wealth. The commentator (Al-Qamar) clarifies various points, including the distinction between succession (khilafa) and deputyship (niyaba), and the condition that preparation is prioritized over debts only when the creditor's right is not attached to a specific asset; if it is attached (as in pawn or pre-purchase), the creditor's right takes precedence. The passage also notes that only the obligation to pay is inherited, not the right to enforce earning for the kitaba if the mukatib dies insolvent.

Key Terms
التجهيز (al-tajhiz): Preparation of the deceased's body for burial, including washing, shrouding, and funeral expenses.
الخلافة (al-khilafa): Succession: the heir stands in the place of the deceased by necessity, without stipulation or choice.
الكتابة (al-kitaba): A contract between a master and a slave whereby the slave earns his freedom by paying installments.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, why is burial preparation (tajhiz) given precedence over debts?
A) Because the deceased's spirit cannot rest until buried.
B) Because the need for burial is stronger than the need to clear debts.
C) Because debts are only a worldly matter.
D) Because the heirs prefer burial first.

Key Takeaway
The order of rights in inheritance is based on the strength of need: tajhiz, debts, bequests, then inheritance; the same principle ensures continuity of kitaba after death.

Ignorance as an Acquired Intervening Attribute
Definition and classification of ignorance as an acquired attribute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define both simple and compound ignorance, explain why ignorance is considered an acquired intervening attribute in Hanafi usul, and apply the distinction to assess culpability.

Core Idea
Ignorance is an acquired intervening attribute because persistence in ignorance is blameworthy when one can seek knowledge.

In this passage, the author explains that after discussing heavenly intervening attributes (like life and death), we now turn to acquired attributes—those in which human choice plays a role. The first type examined is ignorance (al-jahl). Ignorance is not merely the absence of knowledge; it can be simple or compound. Understanding this distinction is crucial for determining legal responsibility (taklīf) and the validity of excuses in Islamic law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the attribute category
Recognize that the passage introduces 'acquired intervening attributes' (al-ʿawāriḍ al-muktasaba) as those where the servant's choice has a role. Ignorance is the first example.
Heavenly attributes (e.g., sleep, death) are beyond choice. Acquired attributes involve human action or omission.
2
Define simple ignorance
Simple ignorance (jahl basīṭ) is the absence of knowledge concerning something that is knowable. Its relationship to knowledge is that of privation (ʿadam) to capacity (malaka).
It is not a positive belief; it is a lack.
3
Define compound ignorance
Compound ignorance (jahl murakkab) is a firm belief that does not match reality, accompanied by the belief that it does match. It is a defect that cannot be removed by learning because the person mistakenly thinks they know.
This is more serious than simple ignorance.
4
Resolve the apparent contradiction
Ignorance is original to humans (Quran 16:78: 'you knew nothing'), so why is it considered an intervening attribute? Because it is not permanent; it is additional to the human essence and can be removed. It is considered acquired because neglecting to seek knowledge when able makes one responsible for persisting in ignorance.
The phrase 'acquired' here includes omissions (tark) treated as acts.
5
Apply to legal capacity
Simple ignorance may excuse one from culpability if unavoidable; compound ignorance does not, because it involves a false belief that could have been corrected by seeking knowledge.
The mufta bihi: persistent ignorance without effort is blameworthy.

Source Text

بيان الأمور المعترضة المكتسبة ] وإذا فرغنا عن الأمور المعترضة السماوية شرعنا في بيان الأمور المعترضة المكتسبة، فقوله: أي على الأهلية " ومكتسب" عطف على قوله سماوي، وهو ما كان لاختيار العبد مدخل في حصوله، وهذا أنواع: الأول: بيان الجهل وأنواعه] الجهل الذي هو ضدّ العلم، وإنما عدّ من الأمور المعترضة مع كونه أصلاً في الإنسان؛ أي الجهل ضد العلم فإن كان بسيطا فحدّه أنه عدم العلم عما من شأنه العلم، فالتقابل حينئذ بينه وبين العلم تقابل العدم والملكة وإن كان مركبًا فحدّه أنه اعتقاد جازم غير مطابق للواقع مع اعتقاد المطابقة، وهو عيب لا يمكن إزالته بالتعلّم وإنما عد إلخ: أي وجه عد الجهل من العوارض وإن كان أصليا؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَاللَّهُ أَخْرَجَكُمْ مِنْ بُطُونِ أُمَّهَاتِكُمْ لا تَعْلَمُونَ شَيْئًا) (النحل: ۷۸) أنه أمر زائد على حقيقة الإنسان مفارق ثابت في حال دون حال، ووجه من المكتسبة وإن كان بلا اختيار العبد في أصل الخلقة لتقصيره في اكتساب العلم؛ لأنه كان قادرا على إزالته بتحصيل العلم، فجعل ترك تحصيله واستمراره على الجهل بمنزلة اكتسابه باختياره.
Explanation of intervening acquired matters. And when we finish with the heavenly intervening matters, we begin the explanation of the intervening acquired matters. His statement: (and acquired) is conjunct to his statement: heavenly, and it is that in the occurrence of which the choice of the servant has an entry. And its types: The first: Explanation of ignorance and its types. Ignorance is the opposite of knowledge. It is considered among the intervening matters despite being original in man. (i.e., ignorance is opposite to knowledge. If it is simple, its definition is that it is the absence of knowledge concerning that which is knowable. So the relationship between it and knowledge is the relationship of privation and capacity. If it is compound, its definition is that it is a firm belief that does not correspond to reality while believing it corresponds, and it is a defect that cannot be removed by learning. Why it is counted: i.e., the aspect of counting ignorance among the attributes (intervening) even though it is original. Due to His statement: 'And Allah brought you out of your mothers' wombs while you knew nothing.' (al-Nahl 78). It is something additional to the reality of man, separable, existing in some states and not others. And the aspect of being acquired is that even though it is without the servant's choice in the original creation, because of his negligence in acquiring knowledge, since he was able to remove it by attaining knowledge, so his abandoning its acquisition and continuing in ignorance is considered like acquiring it by his choice.
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage is a definitional and classificatory discussion in usul al-fiqh, specifically defining ignorance (al-jahl) as an intervening acquired attribute (al-āriḍ al-muktasab). The author first distinguishes between heavenly intervening matters (e.g., life, death) and acquired intervening matters. Acquired matters are those in which human choice has a role. The first such matter is ignorance. Ignorance is defined as the opposite of knowledge. Two types are distinguished: simple ignorance (jahl basīṭ) and compound ignorance (jahl murakkab). Simple ignorance is the absence of knowledge regarding something that is knowable. It is a privation (ʿadam) relative to the capacity (malaka) of knowledge. Compound ignorance is a firm belief that does not match reality, along with the belief that it does match. It is a defect that cannot be removed by learning because the person wrongly thinks they know. The text then addresses a potential objection: ignorance is original to humans (as per Quran 16:78: 'you knew nothing'), so why is it counted as an intervening attribute? The answer: it is intervening because it is additional to the essential human reality (it is separable and not always present; it can be removed). It is considered acquired because even though it originates without choice, one becomes culpable by failing to seek knowledge when able. Thus, persisting in ignorance is treated as an acquired act of omission.

Key Terms
الجهل البسيط (al-jahl al-basīṭ): Simple ignorance: not knowing something that is knowable, without any false belief.
الجهل المركب (al-jahl al-murakkab): Compound ignorance: a firm false belief that one knows, while being wrong.
العارض المكتسب (al-āriḍ al-muktasab): An acquired intervening attribute; a temporary quality that arises from human choice and action.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the relationship between simple ignorance and knowledge?
A) They are opposites with no overlap.
B) They are in a relationship of privation and capacity.
C) They are the same thing.
D) Simple ignorance is a type of knowledge.

Key Takeaway
Ignorance is classified as an acquired intervening attribute because the obligation to seek knowledge makes willful persistence in ignorance blameworthy, even if ignorance is initially original.

Ignorance as an Acquired Impediment to Legal Capacity
Defining ignorance and its classification as an acquired impediment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify ignorance according to Hanafi usul and identify which types excuse a person in this world and the Hereafter.

Core Idea
Ignorance is an acquired impediment because man can remove it by learning; only certain types excuse in this world.

In this passage from Nur al-Anwar, the author defines ignorance as an acquired incidental matter affecting legal capacity. Although humans are born ignorant (Quran 16:78), ignorance is treated as acquired because one can choose to learn. The passage then distinguishes three types of ignorance that are not excused in the Hereafter, while noting that in this world, the ignorance of a disbeliever may avert execution if he accepts dhimmi status.

Guided Path
1
Define ignorance and its classification
Identify jahl as the opposite of knowledge and note that it is counted among acquired impediments despite being innate, because humans can remove it by learning.
The author gives two reasons: ignorance is outside human reality, and persistence in it is a choice when learning is possible.
2
Understand the reason for treating ignorance as acquired
Analyze the Quranic verse (16:78) as a dalil that humans are born ignorant, but the Hanafi view is that this natural state becomes an acquired impediment when one fails to seek knowledge.
The verse shows original ignorance; the reasoning is that since removal is possible, neglecting learning is an act of acquisition.
3
List the three types of ignorance and their Hereafter excuse
Extract from the text: (1) ignorance of the disbeliever after clear proofs of tawheed and risala, (2) ignorance of the follower of desire (e.g., Mu'tazila) rejecting divine attributes, (3) ignorance of the rebel who disobeys the rightful imam while holding to a proof.
All three are not valid excuses in the Hereafter; for the disbeliever, it is like being without any excuse.
4
Examine the worldly excuse for the disbeliever
Note that the text says the disbeliever's ignorance is a valid excuse in this world to repel the punishment of execution if he accepts the dhimma (jizya agreement).
This is a practical legal concession (rukhsah) in this world, not a spiritual excuse.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان الأمور المعترضة المكتسبة . وإذا فرغنا عن الأمور المعترضة السماوية شرعنا في بيان الأمور المعترضة المكتسبة، فقوله: (ومكتسب) عطف على قوله سماوي، وهو ما كان لاختيار العبد مدخل في حصوله، وهذا أنواع: الأول: بيان الجهل وأنواعه. الجهل الذي هو ضدّ العلم، وإنما عدّ من الأمور المعترضة مع كونه أصلاً في الإنسان؛ لأنه خارج عن حقيقة الإنسان، أو لأنه لما كان قادراً على إزالته باكتساب العلم جعل ترکه اکتسابًا للجهل واختيارًا له. وهو أنواع: جهل باطل لا يصلح عذرًا في الآخرة كجهل الكافر بعد وضوح الدلائل على وحدانية الله تعالى ورسالة الرسل لا يصلح عذرًا في الآخرة، وإن كان يصلح عذرًا في الدنيا لدفع عذاب القتل إذا قبل الذمة. وجهل صاحب الهوى في صفات الله وأحكام الآخرة كجهل المعتزلة بإنكار الصفات وعذاب القبر، والرؤية، والشفاعة. وجهل الباغي بإطاعة الإمام الحق متمسكًا بدليل.
Statement on acquired incidental matters. And when we have finished with the celestial incidental matters, we begin the statement on acquired incidental matters. So his statement: (and acquired) is coordinated with his statement celestial, and it is that in whose occurrence the servant's choice has an entry. And this has types: the first: Statement on ignorance and its types. Ignorance is the opposite of knowledge, and it is counted among the incidental matters despite being original in man, because it is outside the reality of man, or because since he was able to remove it by acquiring knowledge, his leaving it is made an acquisition of ignorance and a choice of it. And it has types: vain ignorance that is not a valid excuse in the Hereafter, like the ignorance of the disbeliever after the clarity of evidences for the oneness of Allah and the message of the messengers; it is not a valid excuse in the Hereafter, though it is a valid excuse in this world to repel the punishment of execution if he accepts the dhimma. And the ignorance of the follower of desire concerning the attributes of Allah and the rulings of the Hereafter, like the ignorance of the Mu'tazila by denying the attributes, the punishment of the grave, the vision, and the intercession. And the ignorance of the rebel in obeying the rightful imam while clinging to a proof.
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage is a definition and classification of ignorance (jahl) as one of the acquired impediments to legal capacity (ahliyyah). The author first explains why ignorance, though innate in humans (as per Quran 16:78), is considered an acquired impediment: because it is outside the essential reality of man, and because man has the ability to remove it by learning, so persisting in it is treated as an acquisition. Then, three types of ignorance that are not valid excuses in the Hereafter are listed: 1) Ignorance of the disbeliever after clear proofs of tawheed and risala — this is not excused in the Hereafter but may be excused in this world if the disbeliever accepts dhimmi status (according to Abu Hanifa, his dini belief prevents the legal address from reaching him). 2) Ignorance of the follower of desire (like the Mu'tazila) who denies divine attributes, the punishment of the grave, vision of Allah, and intercession — this person is not a disbeliever but a sinner (fasiq) and is debated with. 3) Ignorance of the rebel (baghi) who disobeys the rightful imam while holding to a proof — such a rebel is debated and fought if he persists. The key legal point is that these three types of ignorance do not excuse punishment in the Hereafter, but worldly consequences (like execution) may be averted if conditions are met.

Key Terms
الجهل (al-jahl): Ignorance is the absence of knowledge; it is an impediment to legal capacity. It is either simple (absence of knowledge) or compound (false belief).
الجهل البسيط (al-jahl al-basīṭ): Simple ignorance: lack of knowledge regarding something that can be known.
الجهل المركب (al-jahl al-murakkab): Compound ignorance: firm belief that contradicts reality while believing it matches reality; cannot be removed by learning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Ignorance of the Mu'tazila regarding divine attributes.
B) Ignorance of the disbeliever after clear proofs, if he accepts dhimmi status.
C) Ignorance of the rebel who disobeys the rightful imam.
D) Simple ignorance of a Muslim about a fiqh ruling.

Key Takeaway
Ignorance is an acquired impediment; after clear proofs, it does not excuse one in the Hereafter, though worldly concessions may apply.

Types of Ignorance in Hanafi Jurisprudence and Their Legal Effects
Classification of ignorance and its effect on liability.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify the four types of ignorance (jahl) identified in the Hanafi tradition and state the legal consequence (hukm) of each type in this world and the Hereafter.

Core Idea
Ignorance is classified into four types; only the disbeliever's ignorance after clear proofs is inexcusable in the Hereafter, but it may excuse worldly punishment if he accepts dhimma.

In this passage, the author of Nur al-Anwar defines ignorance as a voluntary acquisition resulting from abandoning the pursuit of knowledge. He then delineates four distinct types of ignorance, each with a unique legal ruling. Understanding this classification is crucial for discerning when ignorance can serve as a valid excuse in Islamic law, particularly in matters of liability and punishment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of ignorance
The author defines ignorance as being outside human reality or as a voluntary choice. Note: This establishes that ignorance is not always an excuse; it can be blameworthy.
2
Distinguish the first type (jahal batil)
This is the ignorance of the disbeliever after clear proofs. It does not excuse in the Hereafter but may excuse worldly execution if the disbeliever accepts dhimma.
Key factor: clarity of evidence.
3
Recognize the second type (sahib hawa)
This applies to those who deny certain attributes of Allah or matters of the Hereafter based on desire. They are considered sinners, not disbelievers.
They are to be debated, not killed.
4
Analyze the third type (baghi)
The rebel follows a specious interpretation to disobey the rightful imam. His liability depends on whether he has military force (man'a); if no force, he is liable; if force, he is not liable after repentance.
Analogous to warring disbelievers after embracing Islam.
5
Examine the fourth type (mujtahid opposing the Book)
This includes ijtihad that contradicts clear nass, such as al-Shafi'i's ruling on eating meat without tasmiyah intentionally. Such ignorance invalidates the ijtihad.
Examples highlight the need for strong evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان الأهلية
١٨٤
بيان الجهل وأنواعه
لكونه خارجًا عن حقيقة الإنسان، أو لأنه لما كان قادرًا على إزالته باكتساب العلم جعل ترکه اکتسابًا للجهل واختيارًا له.
وهو أنواع جهل باطل لا يصلح عذرًا في الآخرة كجهل الكافر بعد وضوح الدلائل أي أربعة على وحدانية الله تعالى ورسالة الرسل لا يصلح عذرًا في الآخرة، وإن كان يصلح عذرًا في الدنيا لدفع عذاب القتل. إذا قبل الذمة وجهل صاحب الهوى في صفات الله وأحكام الآخرة كجهل المعتزلة بإنكار الصفات وعذاب القبر، والرؤية، والشفاعة. وجهل الباغي بإطاعة الإمام الحق متمسكًا بدليل فاسد حتى يضمن مال العادل ونفسه إذا أتلفه إذا لم يكن له منعة؛ لأنه يمكن إلزامه بالدليل والجبر على الضمان وأما إذا كان له منعة فلا يؤخذ بضمان ما أتلفه بعد التوبة كما لا يؤخذ أهل الحرب بعد الإسلام.
وجهل من خالف في اجتهاده الكتاب كجهل الشافعي له في حلّ متروك التسمية عامدًا قياسًا على متروك التسمية ناسيا، فإنه مخالف لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَلا تَأْكُلُوا مِمَّا لَمْ يُذْكَرِ اسْمُ اللَّهِ عَلَيْهِ﴾ (الأنعام: ۱۲۱)، والسنة المشهورة كالفتوى ببيع أمهات الأولاد ونحوه، فالجهل بفتوى بيع أمهات الأولاد جهل من داود الأصفهاني وتابعيه حيث ذهبوا إلى جواز بيعها لحديث جابر أمهات الأولاد على عهد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم * وهو مخالف للحديث المشهور أعني قوله عليه السلام لامرأة ولدت من سيّدها: "هي معتقة عن دبر "منه والجهل في نحوه كجهل الشافعي في جواز القضاء بشاهد ويمين فإنه مخالف للحديث المشهور
Statement of legal capacity. Statement of ignorance and its types. Because it is outside the reality of man, or because since he is capable of removing it by acquiring knowledge, his abandonment [of acquiring knowledge] is made an acquisition of ignorance and a choice for it. And it has types: 1) Invalid ignorance that is not a valid excuse in the Hereafter, like the ignorance of the disbeliever after the clarity of evidences, i.e., four [matters] on the Oneness of Allah Most High and the message of the messengers, not a valid excuse in the Hereafter, although it is a valid excuse in this world to ward off the punishment of execution, if he accepts the dhimma. 2) The ignorance of the follower of desire concerning the attributes of Allah and the rulings of the Hereafter, like the ignorance of the Mu'tazila in denying the attributes, the punishment of the grave, the vision [of Allah], and intercession. 3) The ignorance of the rebel in disobeying the rightful imam while clinging to a corrupt proof, such that he is liable for the property and person of the obedient [citizen] if he destroys it, if he has no military force, because it is possible to compel him by proof and force him to guarantee; but if he has military force, he is not taken [to account] for the guarantee of what he destroyed after repentance, just as the people of war are not taken after Islam. 4) The ignorance of one who, in his ijtihad, opposes the Book, like the ignorance of al-Shafi'i concerning the permissibility of [eating] that on which the name of Allah has been intentionally omitted, by analogy to that on which the name has been forgotten, for it opposes the saying of Allah Most High: 'And do not eat of that upon which the name of Allah has not been mentioned' (al-An'am 121), and the well-known Sunnah, like the legal opinion on selling ummahat al-awlad and the like. The ignorance in the legal opinion on selling ummahat al-awlad is the ignorance of Dawud al-Isfahani and his followers who held its permissibility due to the hadith of Jabir that 'we sold ummahat al-awlad in the time of the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ)', which contradicts the well-known hadith, namely his saying (ﷺ) to a woman who gave birth from her master: 'She is free from his dhimma [after his death].' And ignorance similar to it is like the ignorance of al-Shafi'i on the permissibility of judging by a single witness and an oath, for it contradicts the well-known hadith.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage classifies ignorance (jahal) into four types within Hanafi jurisprudence, explaining their legal effects in this world and the Hereafter. The author begins by defining ignorance as being outside human reality, or as a voluntary acquisition due to abandoning knowledge. The first type is invalid ignorance (jahal batil), that of a disbeliever after clear proofs of Tawhid and prophethood are established; it does not excuse in the Hereafter (he will be punished) but may excuse in this world from capital punishment if he accepts dhimma. The second type is the ignorance of a follower of desire (sahib hawa), like the Mu'tazila who deny divine attributes; they are considered sinners but not disbelievers, and debate with them is permissible. The third type is the ignorance of a rebel (baghi) who disobeys the rightful imam with a specious proof; if he has no military force (man'a), he is liable for damages to property and persons of the obedient, but if he has force, he is not held liable in this world after repentance, analogous to warring disbelievers after embracing Islam. The fourth type is the ignorance of a mujtahid who opposes clear Quranic text or well-known hadith, exemplified by Imam al-Shafi'i's ruling on eating meat without tasmiyah intentionally (by analogy to forgetting) and on selling ummahat al-awlad. Such ignorance is considered invalid because it contradicts definitive texts. The passage stresses that opposition to categorical evidence (nass qat'i) is not permissible, and such ijtihad is rejected.

Key Terms
جهل (jahl): Lack of knowledge that is either excusable or inexcusable depending on type
باغي (baghi): Rebel against the rightful imam with a specious interpretation

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the ruling on the liability of a rebel (baghi) who destroys property of a compliant citizen during rebellion?
A) He is always liable regardless of circumstances.
B) He is liable only if he has no military force (man'a); if he has force, liability is dropped after repentance.
C) He is never liable because rebellion is a valid interpretation.
D) He is liable only if he kills, not for property.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi tradition classifies ignorance into four categories, each with distinct worldly and Hereafter consequences, reminding jurists that not all ignorance is equal.

Ignorance (Jahl) as an Excuse in Agency and Interdiction
Explains the rule of ignorance as an excuse in agency and interdiction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that ignorance of a newly created legal status (agency or interdiction) excuses the agent or authorized slave from liability until news reaches him.

Core Idea
Ignorance of a change in legal status excuses actions before knowledge.

In Hanafi usul, ignorance (jahl) can serve as a valid excuse in certain contractual and agency contexts. The following passage explains that when a person is unaware of being appointed as an agent or being granted permission, or unaware of being revoked or interdicted, his actions before knowledge are treated differently. Understanding this rule helps clarify how legal capacity is affected by the absence of information.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
There are two opposite pairs: ignorance of agency/permission versus ignorance of revocation/interdiction. For each, note whether the person's action is valid or not.
The first pair: the person does not know he has been appointed. The second: he does not know he has been removed.
2
Determine the ruling for each
In the first scenario (ignorance of new status), his action is not effective against the principal/master. In the second (ignorance of revocation), his action is effective.
The rationale: in the first, he is acting without authority; in the second, his authority is technically ended but he doesn't know, so he is excused.
3
Extract the legal maxim
The underlying principle: ignorance of a legal change excuses until knowledge. This applies when the person could not have known of the change.
This is similar to the rule that contracts made before knowledge of interdiction are valid.
4
Apply to similar cases
Think of analogous situations: a person appointed to sell perishable goods does not sell because he didn't know of the appointment; the goods spoil. The agent is not liable. Or a person authorized to buy valuable goods buys for himself before knowing of the authorization; the purchase is for himself.
These cases illustrate the practical effect of ignorance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان الأهلية
بيان الجهل وأنواعه
أي بالوكالة والإذن، وضده أي بالعزل والحجر فتصرّفا قبل بلوغ الخبر إليهما، فهذا الجهل أي إذن التجارة أي عن الوكالة أي عن التجارة من منهما يكون عذراً، فلم ينفذ تصرفهما على المؤكل والمولى في الصورة الأولى؛ لأنها الوكيل والعبد المأذون دفعا للضرر عنهما يعلما بأمرهما، وينفذ تصرفهما عليهما في الصورة الثانية؛ لأنهما لم يعلما بحجرهما. والسكر عطف على الجهل، وهو إن كان من مباح، أي حصل من شرب شيء مباح كشرب الدواء المسكر مثل البنج والأفيون على رأي المتقدمين دون المتأخرين، وشرب المكره والمضطر أي شرب المكره بالقتل، أو بقطع العضو الخمر وشرب المضطر للعطش إياه فهو أي الخمر كالإغماء، يعني يجعل مانعًا، فيمنع صحة الطلاق والعتاق وسائر التصرفات كالإغماء كذلك. على المؤكل إلخ: فإن كان وكيلاً ببيع ما يتسارع إليه الفساد فلم يبعه لعدم علمه بالوكالة. ففسد ذلك الشيء لا يجب الضمان على الوكيل وكذا لو كان وكيلاً بشراء شيء كثير المنفعة فاشتراه لنفسه قبل العلم بالوكالة صح له لا يمكن للمؤكل أخذه عنه. (السنبلي) في الصورة الأولى: أي قبل العلم بالوكالة والإذن. (القمر) وينفذ تصرّفهما أي تصرف الوكيل والعبد المأذون عليهما أي على المؤكل والمولى في الصورة الثانية أي قبل العلم بالعزل والحجر. (القمر) والسكر هو غفلة تحصل باستعمال بعض المشروبات والمأكولات. (القمر) والسكر إلخ قال صاحب "التلويح": هي حالة تعرض الإنسان من امتلاء دماغه من الأبخرة المتصاعدة إليه، فيتعطّل معه عقله المميز بين الأمور الحسنة والقبيحة. (السنبلي) كشرب الدواء: فبكونه دواءً صار مباحًا وإن لم يشرب بدوائيته، فصار محرّما. (القمر) مثل البنج والأفيون: قال ابن الملك في شرحه اعلم أن فخر الإسلام له وكثيرًا من العلماء ذكروا البنج من أمثلة المباح مطلقًا، وذكر قاضي خان في شرحه "الجامع" ناقلاً عن أبي حنيفة بالله: " إن الرجل إذا كان عالماً بتأثير البنج في العقل فأكل فسكر يصح طلاقه وعتاقه وهذا يدل على أنه حرام ، وأما الأفيون ففي "جامع الرموز" أنه حلال، وفي "الدر المختار: ويحرم أكل البنج والأفيون؛ لأنه مفسد للعقل ويصدّ عن ذكر الله تعالى، وعن الصلاة. (القمر) شرب المكره إلخ بأن قال المكره : اشرب الخمر وإلا أقطع عضوك أو أقتلك، فشرب الخمر، والمضطرّ بأن اضطرّ من العطش، فشرب الخمر. (السنبلي) كالإغماء إلخ : أي السكر الحاصل بطريق المباح بمنزلة الإغماء حتى لا يصح طلاقه وعتاقه وسائر تصرفاته؛ لأن ذلك ليس من جنس اللهو، فصار من أقسام المرض. (السنبلي مانعًا: أي من التصرّفات؛ لأن هذا السكر ليس من جنس اللهو بل بمباح، فهذا السكر عذر (القمر) فيمنع إلخ إذ لا اعتبار بعباراته.(القمر)

وإن كان من محظور، أي حصل من شرب شيء مُحرّم كالخمر والسكر ونحوه، فلا ينافي الخطاب بالإجماع؛ لأن قوله تعالى: ﴿ولا تَقْرَبُوا الصَّلاةَ وَأَنْتُمْ سُكَارَى﴾ (النساء : ٤٣ ) إن كان خطابًا في حال السكر فهو المطلوب أنه لا ينافي الخطاب وإن كان في حال الصحو فهو فاسد؛ إذ يصير المعنى إذا سكرتم فلا تقربوا الصلاة كقوله للعاقل : إذا جننت فلا تفعل كذا، وهو إضافة الخطاب إلى حال منافٍ له فلا يجوز. وتلزمه أحكام الشرع، وتصح عباراته في الطلاق والعتاق والبيع، والشراء والأقارير زجرا له عن ارتكاب المنهي عنه، وتنبيها له على أن مثل هذا السكر المحرّم لا يكون عذراً له في إبطال أحكام الشرع. إلا الردّة والإقرار بالحدود الخالصة، فإنه إذا ارتد السكران وتكلم بكلمة الكفر لا يحكم بكفره؛ لأن الردّة عبارة عن تبدّل الاعتقاد، وهو غير معتقد لِمَا يقوله، وكذا إذا أقرّ بالحدود الخالصة لله كشرب الخمر والزنا لا يُحدّ؛ لأن الرجوع عنه صحيح، والسكر دليل الرجوع، بخلاف ما لو أقرّ بالحدود الغير الخالصة لله كالقذف أو القصاص، فإنه لا يصح الرجوع؛ إذ صاحب الحق يكذبه، فيؤاخذ بالحد والقصاص، وبخلاف ما إذا زنى في حال سكره وثبت من غير إقرار فيه، فإنه يُحدّ صاحيًا.

حال السكر
كالخمر إلخ الخمر هو النّي من ماء العنب إذا غلى واشتدّ وقذف بالزبد والسكر بفتحتين، وهي النّي من ماء الرطب إذ اشتد وقذف بالزبد ونحوه نقيع الزبيب بشرط أن يقذف بالزبد بعد الغليان، كذا في "الدر المختار" . (القمر) فلا ينافي إلخ لأن السكر لا يؤثر في العقل بالإعدام، ومدار الخطاب على العقل. (القمر) إذا سكرتم وخرجتم عن أهلية الخطاب (القمر) فلا يجوز لاستلزامه اجتماع المتنافيين فإن النهي يصح عما يمكن أن يُفعل، وفي حالة الجنون أو السكر لا يصح أن يفعل فكيف يكون مخاطبًا بالنهي في هذه الحالة.(القمر) بالحدود الخالصة أي بما يوجب الحدود الخالصة التي لا يكون فيها حق العبد (القمر) وهو: أي السكران غير معتقد لما يقوله فإنه لا قصد له ولا يذكره بعد الصحو. (القمر) دليل الرجوع وإنما كان السكر دليل الرجوع؛ لأن السكران لا يستقر على أمر ولا يثبت على كلام فإن من عادة السكران أن يخلط كلامه. (القمر)
Explanation of legal capacity. Explanation of ignorance and its types: i.e., regarding agency and permission, and its opposite regarding revocation and interdiction; so their actions before news reaches them – this ignorance is an excuse, so their actions are not effective against the principal and the master in the first scenario because they did not know their situation, and their actions are effective against them in the second scenario because they did not know of the revocation/interdiction. Intoxication is conjoined to ignorance, and if it arises from a permissible source, such as drinking an intoxicating medicine like hemp and opium according to the earlier scholars but not later ones, or drinking under coercion or necessity – it is like unconsciousness, meaning it becomes a preventer, preventing the validity of divorce, emancipation, and all transactions, just as unconsciousness does. If it arises from a prohibited source, like wine or date-wine, then it does not contradict address (khitab) by consensus, because Allah's statement: "Do not approach prayer while you are intoxicated" (4:43) – if it is an address in the state of intoxication, then that proves it does not contradict address; if it is in the state of sobriety, then it is invalid because the meaning would be: if you become intoxicated, do not approach prayer, like saying to a sane person: if you become insane, do not do such-and-such, which is adding address to a state that contradicts it and is not permissible. And the rulings of the Shariah apply to him, and his utterances are valid in divorce, emancipation, sale, purchase, and confessions, as a deterrent and to indicate that such prohibited intoxication is not an excuse for nullifying Shariah rulings. Except for apostasy and confession of pure hadd penalties: if the intoxicated person apostatizes and speaks a word of disbelief, he is not judged as an apostate because apostasy is a change of belief, and he does not believe what he says; similarly, if he confesses to pure hadd penalties, like drinking wine or zina, he is not punished because retraction is valid, and intoxication is evidence of retraction. Unlike confessions of non-pure hadd penalties, like qadhf or qisas, where retraction is not valid because the right-holder would deny it, so he is subjected to hadd or qisas; and unlike if he commits zina while intoxicated and it is established without his confession, then he is punished when sober.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage from Noorul Anwar discusses the effect of two states – ignorance and intoxication – on legal capacity (ahliyyah). The author first explains ignorance: when a person is unaware of a change in his legal status (such as being appointed agent or being revoked), his actions before knowledge are excused. For example, if a person is appointed as agent but does not know, his transactions are not valid against the principal; conversely, if he is revoked but does not know, his transactions are valid because the revocation was not communicated. Then the passage turns to intoxication. It distinguishes between intoxication from permissible causes (like medicine) and prohibited causes (like wine). For permissible intoxication, the person is treated like one who is unconscious: his divorce, emancipation, and other statements are invalid because he lacks rational capacity. For prohibited intoxication, the person remains addressed by the Shariah (khitab), and his utterances are valid as a deterrent, except in two cases: apostasy and confession of pure hadd penalties. In those cases, his words are not binding because he is not truly intending them and can retract; intoxication serves as evidence of retraction because a drunk person is inconsistent. The passage also notes scholarly disagreement on whether opium and hemp are permissible intoxicants, with some earlier Hanafi scholars considering them permissible and later ones forbidding them.

Key Terms
جهل (jahl): Lack of knowledge of a legal fact (such as agency or interdiction) that serves as an excuse for actions taken before knowledge.
وكالة (wakalah): Agency; the act of appointing someone to act on one's behalf.
حجر (hajr): Interdiction; a legal restriction on one's capacity to manage property, e.g., due to debt or insanity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if an agent is unaware of his appointment and sells property, what is the effect on the principal?
A) The sale is binding on the principal.
B) The sale is not binding on the principal.
C) The sale is void automatically.
D) The sale is valid only if the price is fair.

Key Takeaway
Ignorance of a newly created agency or an interdiction excuses the person's actions until he learns of the change, protecting both parties from injustice.
