Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
10 min
Intoxication (Sukr): Permissible vs Prohibited and Its Legal Effect
Explains the two types of intoxication and their effect on legal capacity, with a Quranic proof and an intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between permissible and prohibited intoxication, apply the rule that prohibited intoxication does not nullify legal address, and identify the exceptions for apostasy and hadd confessions.

Core Idea
Prohibited intoxication does not suspend legal capacity; permissible intoxication does.

The Hanafi school makes a crucial distinction between intoxication arising from permissible causes (like medicine or necessity) and prohibited causes (like wine). This lesson explores how each type affects a person's legal capacity (ahliyyah) and the validity of their utterances. Using a Quranic proof, the author demonstrates that the drunk person from prohibited intoxication remains addressed by the Shariah (mukhatab), while the one from permissible causes is like an unconscious person. The lesson also covers the exceptional cases of apostasy and confessions of hudud penalties.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two types of intoxication
Note that intoxication can arise from a permissible source (e.g., medicine, duress) or a prohibited source (e.g., wine). The passage calls these 'mubah' and 'mahzur'.
Permissible includes cases like forced drinking or medical necessity.
2
Ruling for permissible intoxication
If the intoxication is from a permissible cause, it is treated like unconsciousness: all statements (divorce, emancipation, contracts) are invalid.
The person is considered ma'zur (excused) and his words have no legal effect.
3
Ruling for prohibited intoxication
If from a prohibited cause, the person remains fully addressed: his utterances in divorce, sale, confession are valid. This is based on the Quranic verse 4:43 which addresses the drunk person directly.
The verse 'Do not approach prayer while intoxicated' proves the drunk is still addressed.
4
Analyze the exception
Even in prohibited intoxication, apostasy and confessions of pure hadd (e.g., zina, wine drinking) are not accepted because the drunk is not fully aware. He can retract, and his intoxication is evidence of retraction.
For non-pure hadd (e.g., qadhf, qisas), confessions stand.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute on opium/hemp
Earlier scholars considered hemp permissible as medicine, but later scholars (like in al-Durr al-Mukhtar) declared it prohibited because it intoxicates and corrupts the mind. The later view is relied upon.
This dispute affects whether a drunkard's utterances are valid or not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان الأهلية
بيان الجهل وأنواعه
أي بالوكالة والإذن، وضده أي بالعزل والحجر فتصرّفا قبل بلوغ الخبر إليهما، فهذا الجهل أي إذن التجارة أي عن الوكالة أي عن التجارة من منهما يكون عذراً، فلم ينفذ تصرفهما على المؤكل والمولى في الصورة الأولى؛ لأنها الوكيل والعبد المأذون دفعا للضرر عنهما يعلما بأمرهما، وينفذ تصرفهما عليهما في الصورة الثانية؛ لأنهما لم يعلما بحجرهما. والسكر عطف على الجهل، وهو إن كان من مباح، أي حصل من شرب شيء مباح كشرب الدواء المسكر مثل البنج والأفيون على رأي المتقدمين دون المتأخرين، وشرب المكره والمضطر أي شرب المكره بالقتل، أو بقطع العضو الخمر وشرب المضطر للعطش إياه فهو أي الخمر كالإغماء، يعني يجعل مانعًا، فيمنع صحة الطلاق والعتاق وسائر التصرفات كالإغماء كذلك. على المؤكل إلخ: فإن كان وكيلاً ببيع ما يتسارع إليه الفساد فلم يبعه لعدم علمه بالوكالة. ففسد ذلك الشيء لا يجب الضمان على الوكيل وكذا لو كان وكيلاً بشراء شيء كثير المنفعة فاشتراه لنفسه قبل العلم بالوكالة صح له لا يمكن للمؤكل أخذه عنه. (السنبلي) في الصورة الأولى: أي قبل العلم بالوكالة والإذن. (القمر) وينفذ تصرّفهما أي تصرف الوكيل والعبد المأذون عليهما أي على المؤكل والمولى في الصورة الثانية أي قبل العلم بالعزل والحجر. (القمر) والسكر هو غفلة تحصل باستعمال بعض المشروبات والمأكولات. (القمر) والسكر إلخ قال صاحب "التلويح": هي حالة تعرض الإنسان من امتلاء دماغه من الأبخرة المتصاعدة إليه، فيتعطّل معه عقله المميز بين الأمور الحسنة والقبيحة. (السنبلي) كشرب الدواء: فبكونه دواءً صار مباحًا وإن لم يشرب بدوائيته، فصار محرّما. (القمر) مثل البنج والأفيون: قال ابن الملك في شرحه اعلم أن فخر الإسلام له وكثيرًا من العلماء ذكروا البنج من أمثلة المباح مطلقًا، وذكر قاضي خان في شرحه "الجامع" ناقلاً عن أبي حنيفة بالله: " إن الرجل إذا كان عالماً بتأثير البنج في العقل فأكل فسكر يصح طلاقه وعتاقه وهذا يدل على أنه حرام ، وأما الأفيون ففي "جامع الرموز" أنه حلال، وفي "الدر المختار: ويحرم أكل البنج والأفيون؛ لأنه مفسد للعقل ويصدّ عن ذكر الله تعالى، وعن الصلاة. (القمر) شرب المكره إلخ بأن قال المكره : اشرب الخمر وإلا أقطع عضوك أو أقتلك، فشرب الخمر، والمضطرّ بأن اضطرّ من العطش، فشرب الخمر. (السنبلي) كالإغماء إلخ : أي السكر الحاصل بطريق المباح بمنزلة الإغماء حتى لا يصح طلاقه وعتاقه وسائر تصرفاته؛ لأن ذلك ليس من جنس اللهو، فصار من أقسام المرض. (السنبلي مانعًا: أي من التصرّفات؛ لأن هذا السكر ليس من جنس اللهو بل بمباح، فهذا السكر عذر (القمر) فيمنع إلخ إذ لا اعتبار بعباراته.(القمر)

وإن كان من محظور، أي حصل من شرب شيء مُحرّم كالخمر والسكر ونحوه، فلا ينافي الخطاب بالإجماع؛ لأن قوله تعالى: ﴿ولا تَقْرَبُوا الصَّلاةَ وَأَنْتُمْ سُكَارَى﴾ (النساء : ٤٣ ) إن كان خطابًا في حال السكر فهو المطلوب أنه لا ينافي الخطاب وإن كان في حال الصحو فهو فاسد؛ إذ يصير المعنى إذا سكرتم فلا تقربوا الصلاة كقوله للعاقل : إذا جننت فلا تفعل كذا، وهو إضافة الخطاب إلى حال منافٍ له فلا يجوز. وتلزمه أحكام الشرع، وتصح عباراته في الطلاق والعتاق والبيع، والشراء والأقارير زجرا له عن ارتكاب المنهي عنه، وتنبيها له على أن مثل هذا السكر المحرّم لا يكون عذراً له في إبطال أحكام الشرع. إلا الردّة والإقرار بالحدود الخالصة، فإنه إذا ارتد السكران وتكلم بكلمة الكفر لا يحكم بكفره؛ لأن الردّة عبارة عن تبدّل الاعتقاد، وهو غير معتقد لِمَا يقوله، وكذا إذا أقرّ بالحدود الخالصة لله كشرب الخمر والزنا لا يُحدّ؛ لأن الرجوع عنه صحيح، والسكر دليل الرجوع، بخلاف ما لو أقرّ بالحدود الغير الخالصة لله كالقذف أو القصاص، فإنه لا يصح الرجوع؛ إذ صاحب الحق يكذبه، فيؤاخذ بالحد والقصاص، وبخلاف ما إذا زنى في حال سكره وثبت من غير إقرار فيه، فإنه يُحدّ صاحيًا.

حال السكر
كالخمر إلخ الخمر هو النّي من ماء العنب إذا غلى واشتدّ وقذف بالزبد والسكر بفتحتين، وهي النّي من ماء الرطب إذ اشتد وقذف بالزبد ونحوه نقيع الزبيب بشرط أن يقذف بالزبد بعد الغليان، كذا في "الدر المختار" . (القمر) فلا ينافي إلخ لأن السكر لا يؤثر في العقل بالإعدام، ومدار الخطاب على العقل. (القمر) إذا سكرتم وخرجتم عن أهلية الخطاب (القمر) فلا يجوز لاستلزامه اجتماع المتنافيين فإن النهي يصح عما يمكن أن يُفعل، وفي حالة الجنون أو السكر لا يصح أن يفعل فكيف يكون مخاطبًا بالنهي في هذه الحالة.(القمر) بالحدود الخالصة أي بما يوجب الحدود الخالصة التي لا يكون فيها حق العبد (القمر) وهو: أي السكران غير معتقد لما يقوله فإنه لا قصد له ولا يذكره بعد الصحو. (القمر) دليل الرجوع وإنما كان السكر دليل الرجوع؛ لأن السكران لا يستقر على أمر ولا يثبت على كلام فإن من عادة السكران أن يخلط كلامه. (القمر)
Explanation of legal capacity. Explanation of ignorance and its types: i.e., regarding agency and permission, and its opposite regarding revocation and interdiction; so their actions before news reaches them – this ignorance is an excuse, so their actions are not effective against the principal and the master in the first scenario because they did not know their situation, and their actions are effective against them in the second scenario because they did not know of the revocation/interdiction. Intoxication is conjoined to ignorance, and if it arises from a permissible source, such as drinking an intoxicating medicine like hemp and opium according to the earlier scholars but not later ones, or drinking under coercion or necessity – it is like unconsciousness, meaning it becomes a preventer, preventing the validity of divorce, emancipation, and all transactions, just as unconsciousness does. If it arises from a prohibited source, like wine or date-wine, then it does not contradict address (khitab) by consensus, because Allah's statement: "Do not approach prayer while you are intoxicated" (4:43) – if it is an address in the state of intoxication, then that proves it does not contradict address; if it is in the state of sobriety, then it is invalid because the meaning would be: if you become intoxicated, do not approach prayer, like saying to a sane person: if you become insane, do not do such-and-such, which is adding address to a state that contradicts it and is not permissible. And the rulings of the Shariah apply to him, and his utterances are valid in divorce, emancipation, sale, purchase, and confessions, as a deterrent and to indicate that such prohibited intoxication is not an excuse for nullifying Shariah rulings. Except for apostasy and confession of pure hadd penalties: if the intoxicated person apostatizes and speaks a word of disbelief, he is not judged as an apostate because apostasy is a change of belief, and he does not believe what he says; similarly, if he confesses to pure hadd penalties, like drinking wine or zina, he is not punished because retraction is valid, and intoxication is evidence of retraction. Unlike confessions of non-pure hadd penalties, like qadhf or qisas, where retraction is not valid because the right-holder would deny it, so he is subjected to hadd or qisas; and unlike if he commits zina while intoxicated and it is established without his confession, then he is punished when sober.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage from Noorul Anwar discusses the effect of two states – ignorance and intoxication – on legal capacity (ahliyyah). The author first explains ignorance: when a person is unaware of a change in his legal status (such as being appointed agent or being revoked), his actions before knowledge are excused. For example, if a person is appointed as agent but does not know, his transactions are not valid against the principal; conversely, if he is revoked but does not know, his transactions are valid because the revocation was not communicated. Then the passage turns to intoxication. It distinguishes between intoxication from permissible causes (like medicine) and prohibited causes (like wine). For permissible intoxication, the person is treated like one who is unconscious: his divorce, emancipation, and other statements are invalid because he lacks rational capacity. For prohibited intoxication, the person remains addressed by the Shariah (khitab), and his utterances are valid as a deterrent, except in two cases: apostasy and confession of pure hadd penalties. In those cases, his words are not binding because he is not truly intending them and can retract; intoxication serves as evidence of retraction because a drunk person is inconsistent. The passage also notes scholarly disagreement on whether opium and hemp are permissible intoxicants, with some earlier Hanafi scholars considering them permissible and later ones forbidding them.

Key Terms
سكر (sukr): A state of heedlessness acquired through consuming certain drinks or foods, characterized by the mind's inability to distinguish between good and bad actions.
خطاب (khitab): Legal address; the divine speech directed to legally responsible persons (mukallafun).
حدود (hudud): Fixed punishments prescribed by Shariah for specific crimes, like zina, drinking wine, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a person becomes intoxicated by drinking wine (haram) and pronounces divorce, what is the ruling?
A) The divorce is invalid because he was not in his senses.
B) The divorce is valid as a deterrent for committing the prohibited act.
C) The divorce is valid only if he remembers it after sobriety.
D) The divorce is invalid unless he intended it before intoxication.

Key Takeaway
Prohibited intoxication does not suspend legal address; the drunk person's statements are valid as a deterrent, except for apostasy and confessions of pure hadd penalties.

The Intoxicated Person's Legal Capacity in Hanafi Usul
Explaining the effect of intoxication on legal capacity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi usul principle that intoxication does not nullify the legal address and apply it to distinguish between valid and invalid utterances of an intoxicated person.

Core Idea
Intoxication does not destroy legal capacity; the drunk's utterances are valid except for apostasy and confession to pure hudud.

This passage from Nur al-Anwar addresses the common question: does intoxication exempt a person from the binding commands of Sharia? The Hanafi position, supported by a careful reading of Quran 4:43, affirms that intoxication does not negate legal responsibility. However, specific exceptions exist for matters requiring conscious intent and for confessions to purely divine penalties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general principle and its basis
The passage begins by stating that intoxication from a prohibited substance does not contradict the address by consensus. Note the term 'khitab' and its significance. Students should recognize that the principle is that intoxication does not remove legal capacity (ahliyyah) for most acts.
The consensus (ijma) is cited as support; this is a strong evidence in Hanafi usul.
2
Analyze the Quranic proof
The verse 'Do not approach prayer while intoxicated' is used to demonstrate that the address is directed to the sober, not the intoxicated. Work through why attributing the address to the intoxicated would be invalid.
The commentators (al-Qamar) explain that intoxication does not destroy reason completely, so the address remains applicable.
3
List the binding consequences
The passage lists that the intoxicated person's statements in divorce, manumission, sale, purchase, and acknowledgments are valid and binding. This is a deterrent and a principle that intoxication does not serve as an excuse to invalidate contract-like utterances.
The Hanafi view here is strict to prevent misuse of intoxication.
4
Identify the exceptions and their rationale
Apostasy and confession to pure hudud (Allah's rights only) are not effective. For apostasy, because it requires belief change; for pure hadd confession, because retraction is valid and intoxication indicates retraction. Mixed hudud (involving a private right) are binding because the victim would reject retraction.
This distinction between pure and mixed hudud is unique to Hanafi fiqh.
5
Define key terms
The passage defines khamr and suk, which are specific intoxicants. Recognize that the definition matters for when intoxication is prohibited.
The definitions are from Durr al-Mukhtar, a standard Hanafi reference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان الجهل وأنواعه وإن كان من محظور، أي حصل من شرب شيء مُحرّم كالخمر والسكر ونحوه، فلا ينافي الخطاب بالإجماع؛ لأن قوله تعالى: ﴿ولا تَقْرَبُوا الصَّلاةَ وَأَنْتُمْ سُكَارَى﴾ إن كان خطابًا في حال السكر فهو المطلوب أنه لا ينافي الخطاب وإن كان في حال الصحو فهو فاسد؛ إذ يصير المعنى إذا سكرتم فلا تقربوا الصلاة كقوله للعاقل: إذا جننت فلا تفعل كذا، وهو إضافة الخطاب إلى حال منافٍ له فلا يجوز. كالصلاة والصوم وغيرهما أي للخطاب وتلزمه أحكام الشرع، وتصح عباراته في الطلاق والعتاق والبيع والشراء والأقارير زجرا له عن ارتكاب المنهي عنه، وتنبيها له على أن مثل هذا السكر المحرّم لا يكون عذراً له في إبطال أحكام الشرع. إلا الردّة والإقرار بالحدود الخالصة، فإنه إذا ارتد السكران وتكلم بكلمة الكفر لا يحكم بكفره؛ لأن الردّة عبارة عن تبدّل الاعتقاد، وهو غير معتقد لِمَا يقوله، وكذا إذا أقرّ بالحدود الخالصة لله كشرب الخمر والزنا لا يُحدّ؛ لأن الرجوع عنه صحيح، والسكر دليل الرجوع، بخلاف ما لو أقرّ بالحدود الغير الخالصة لله كالقذف أو القصاص، فإنه أي التي فيها حق العبد لا يصح الرجوع؛ إذ صاحب الحق يكذبه، فيؤاخذ بالحد والقصاص، وبخلاف ما إذا زنى في حال سكره وثبت من غير إقرار فيه، فإنه يُحدّ صاحيًا. حال السكر كالخمر إلخ الخمر هو النّي من ماء العنب إذا غلى واشتدّ وقذف بالزبد والسكر بفتحتين، وهي النّي من ماء الرطب إذ اشتد وقذف بالزبد ونحوه نقيع الزبيب بشرط أن يقذف بالزبد بعد الغليان، كذا في الدر المختار. Explanation of ignorance and its types: And if it is from a prohibited [act], i.e., it occurs from drinking something forbidden like wine, suk, and the like, then it does not contradict the address by consensus; because the statement of Allah Most High: 'And do not approach prayer while you are intoxicated' (An-Nisa: 43) – if it is an address in a state of intoxication, then it is the desired [meaning] that it does not contradict the address; and if it is in a state of sobriety, then it is invalid; for the meaning becomes 'if you become intoxicated, then do not approach prayer', like saying to a sane person: 'if you become insane, then do not do such-and-such', and this is attributing the address to a state that contradicts it, so it is not permissible. Like prayer, fasting, and others, i.e., for the address. And the rulings of the Law are binding upon him, and his statements are valid in divorce, manumission, sale, purchase, and acknowledgments, as a deterrent to him from committing what is prohibited, and to alert him that such prohibited intoxication is not an excuse for him to invalidate the rulings of the Law. Except for apostasy and acknowledgment of pure hadd [penalties]. For if the intoxicated person apostatizes and speaks a word of disbelief, he is not judged to be a disbeliever; because apostasy is a change of belief, and he does not believe what he says. Likewise, if he confesses to pure hadd for Allah, like drinking wine and fornication, he is not punished; because retraction from it is valid, and intoxication is evidence of retraction. Contrary to if he confesses to hadd that are not pure for Allah, like slander or retaliation, then – i.e., those in which there is a right of the slave – retraction is not valid; because the claimant would belie him, so he is subjected to the hadd and retaliation. And contrary to if he commits fornication while intoxicated and it is established without confession, then he is punished when sober. The state of intoxication: like wine etc. Wine is the fresh juice from grape juice when it boils, ferments, and froths; and suk (with two fathas) is the fresh juice from wet dates when it ferments and froths; and similar is raisin juice provided that it froths after boiling. Thus in al-Durr al-Mukhtar. (al-Qamar) 'so it does not contradict' etc. because intoxication does not affect the mind by destruction, and the address is based on reason. (al-Qamar) 'if you become intoxicated and exit from the capacity for address' (al-Qamar) 'so it is not permissible' because it entails the conjunction of two opposites, for prohibition applies to what can possibly be done, and in the state of insanity or intoxication, it cannot be done, so how can one be addressed with prohibition in that state? (al-Qamar) 'by pure hadd' i.e., that which necessitates pure hadd in which there is no right of the slave. (al-Qamar) 'and he': i.e., the intoxicated person does not believe what he says, for he has no intention and does not remember it after sobriety. (al-Qamar) 'evidence of retraction' and intoxication is evidence of retraction only because the intoxicated person does not settle on a matter and does not stabilize on speech, for it is the habit of the intoxicated to mix his speech. (al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage is a ruling regarding the legal capacity of an intoxicated person. It begins by stating that intoxication from a forbidden substance does not negate the legal address (khitab) by consensus. The proof is the verse 'Do not approach prayer while intoxicated', which is interpreted as addressing the sober person, not the intoxicated one. If interpreted as addressing the intoxicated, it would be contradictory because the state of intoxication precludes valid action. Therefore, the intoxicated person is still bound by the rulings of Sharia: his utterances in divorce, manumission, sales, purchases, and acknowledgments are valid, as a deterrent. However, exceptions are made for apostasy and confessions to pure hudud (rights of Allah only). An intoxicated person who utters kufr is not judged an apostate because apostasy requires belief change, and he does not believe. Similarly, confession to pure hudud like drinking wine or zina is not accepted because he can retract, and his intoxication indicates possible retraction. But for mixed hadd (involving a private right), like qadhf (false accusation) or qisas (retaliation), the confession is binding because the victim would deny retraction. If zina is proven by evidence, not confession, the person is punished when sober. The passage also defines khamr and suk according to Hanafi fiqh. The commentator adds that intoxication does not destroy reason, so the address still applies in principle, but the address itself is directed to the sober.

Key Terms
سكر (sukr): Intoxication from a prohibited substance; does not destroy reason entirely but clouds it.
حدود خالصة (hudud khalisa): Penalties that are purely the right of Allah, like hadd for drinking wine and zina.
ردة (ridda): Apostasy, change of belief from Islam. Requires intent and belief, lacking in the intoxicated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling, if an intoxicated person confesses to false accusation (qadhf), what is the outcome?
A) The confession is invalid and he is not punished.
B) The confession is valid and he is punished because it involves a private right.
C) He is only punished if he confesses twice.
D) He must be sober before being punished.

Key Takeaway
The intoxicated person remains legally responsible for most actions except apostasy and confessions to pure hudud, due to the requirement of conscious intent.

Definition and Legal Effect of Jest (Hazl) in Contracts
Defining jest and its legal condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define hazl (jest) in Hanafi usul, state its condition, and distinguish it from khiyar al-shart.

Core Idea
Jest invalidates a contract because consent to the ruling is absent, even though consent to the utterance exists.

In Hanafi usul, the validity of a contract depends not only on the words uttered but on the intention behind them. A contract made in jest (hazl) presents a unique problem: the speaker performs the act willingly but does not intend its legal consequences. This lesson unpacks the definition of hazl, its necessary condition, and why it differs from the valid but revocable contract under khiyar al-shart.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its category
Recognize that hazl is a state of intention affecting the validity of a contract, not a type of contract itself.
Hazl is the opposite of jidd (seriousness).
2
Understand the definitional refinement
The author's original phrasing had a grammatical flaw; the commentator corrects it to avoid contradiction. Learn the clearer definition: hazl is when the literal nor figurative meaning is intended.
The refined definition avoids the logical strain of the original.
3
Analyze the legal effect
The jester does not choose or consent to the ruling (e.g., transfer of ownership), though he consents to the utterance. This lack of consent to the ruling renders the contract void (fasid).
Consent to the ruling is essential; consent to the act alone is insufficient.
4
Distinguish from khiyar al-shart
In khiyar al-shart, the buyer may not fully consent initially, but the contract remains valid because consent to the ruling exists subject to the option. Hazl corrupts the sale; khiyar al-shart does not.
The difference lies in the nature of consent to the ruling.
5
Apply the condition for jest
For a contract to be considered jest, the parties must explicitly state before the contract that it is pure play, providing no benefit at all. Without this explicit statement, the contract is presumed serious.
The condition is procedural, not merely factual.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والهزل، عطف على ما قبله وهو أن يراد بالشيء ما لم يوضع له، ولا ما صلح له اللفظ أي قول الجهل أي ذلك الشيء استعارة، يعني لا يكون اللفظ محمولاً على معناه الحقيقي أو المجازي، بل يكون لعبا محضا، ولكن العبارة لا تخلو عن تمحل والأولى أن يقول: 'وما لا يصلح له' بتأخير كلمة 'لا' ليكون معطوفا على قوله: 'ما لم يوضع له' أو أن يقول: 'ولا صلح له' بحذف كلمة 'ما' ليكون معطوفا على قوله: 'لم يوضع له'. وهو ضد الجد، وهو أن يراد بالشيء ما وضع له أو ما يصلح له اللفظ استعارة، وأنه أي الهزل الحكم، ينا في اختيار الحكم والرضاء به، ولا ينافي الرضاء بالمباشرة يعني أن الهازل لا يختار ولا يرضى به، ولكنه يرضى بمباشرة السبب؛ إذ التلفظ إنما هو عن رضا واختيار صحيح أي بالحكم وهو نفس التصرف لكنه غير قاصد ولا راض للحكم. فصار الهزل بمعنى خيار الشرط أبدًا في البيع لعدم الرضاء بحكم البيع، لا بعدم الرضاء وهو ملك المشتري بنفس البيع، ولكن بينهما فرق من حيث إن الهزل يُفسد البيع، وخيار الشرط لا يفسده. الهزل وخيار الشرط و شرطه أي شرط الهزل أن يكون صريحًا مشروطًا باللسان بأن يذكر العاقدان قبل العقد لعبًا محضًا أي لا يفيد فائدةً أصلاً، لا حقيقيًا ولا مجازيًا. (القمر) تمحل إلخ لأن المتبادر من قوله: 'ولا ما صلح' أن المعنى: ولا يراد ما صلح له اللفظ وهو ينبئ أن المعطوف أيضًا منفي كما هذا، أي المعطوف عليه منفي والحال أن المعطوف ليس عدم الإرادة بل فيه ثبوت الإرادة، فلا يحصل مقصود المصنف محليه أن وهو الهزل أن يُراد بالشيء غير الموضوع له وغير المستعار له، فافهم وتدبّر ، وتكلّف بعضهم بأن كلمة 'ما' فيه زائدة كما في قوله تعالى: ﴿لَيْسَ كَمِثْلِهِ شَيْءٌ﴾ (الشورى: ۱۱) الكاف زائدة، أو عبارة المصنف محمول على القلب، وكلاهما تكلف بارد (السنبلي) والأولى إلخ قلت والأوضح أن يقال في تعريفه: هو أن لا يُراد باللفظ معناه الحقيقي ولا المجازي. (السنبلي) لا يختار الحكم فإن الهازل لا يريد بالكلام مفهومه. (القمر) لا بعدم الرضاء إلخ لوجود البيع برضاء العقد واختياره. (القمر)
And jest is conjoined to what came before, and it is that by the thing is intended what it was not placed for, nor what the expression is suitable for (i.e., the statement of ignorance, i.e., that thing [is used as] metaphor). Meaning, the expression is not carried upon its literal or figurative meaning, but is pure play. However, the expression is not free from strain, and it is better that he says: 'and what is not suitable for it' by delaying the word 'la' to be conjoined to his statement 'what it was not placed for', or that he says: 'nor what is suitable for it' by dropping the word 'ma' to be conjoined to his statement 'was not placed for'. It is the opposite of seriousness, which is that by the thing is intended what it was placed for or what the expression is suitable for as metaphor. And that (i.e., jest) [has] the ruling: it conflicts with choosing the ruling and being pleased with it, but it does not conflict with being pleased with the direct [act]; meaning the jester does not choose nor is pleased with [the ruling], but he is pleased with performing the cause, since the utterance is only out of pleasure and valid choice (i.e., with the ruling, and it is the disposition itself), but he is not intending nor pleased with the ruling. Thus jest becomes like a stipulation of option forever in sale due to lack of pleasure with the ruling of sale, not due to lack of pleasure with the sale itself (and he is the owner of the buyer by the sale itself), but there is a difference between them in that jest corrupts the sale, while the stipulation of option does not corrupt it. And its condition (i.e., the condition of jest) is that it be explicit and tied to the tongue, by the two contracting parties mentioning before the contract that it is pure play, i.e., it yields no benefit at all, neither literal nor figurative. And some strained by saying the word 'ma' is extra as in His statement: 'There is nothing like unto Him' (Ash-Shura: 11), where the kaf is extra, or that the author's expression is to be taken as inverted, and both are cold straining. (al-Sunbuli) 'and it is better' etc. I say the clearest is to say in its definition: it is that by the expression is intended neither its literal meaning nor its figurative. (al-Sunbuli) 'he does not choose the ruling' because the jester does not intend the concept of his speech. (al-Qamar) 'not due to lack of pleasure' etc. because the sale exists with the pleasure of the contract and its choice. (al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This passage defines 'hazl' (jest) in legal context. Jest is contrasted with 'jidd' (seriousness). In serious speech, the speaker intends the literal or figurative meaning; in jest, the speaker intends neither, but engages in pure play. The definition is refined: the author originally states that in jest, one intends 'what the expression was not placed for, and what it is not suitable for', but the commentator points out a grammatical strain: the second part is positive in meaning while the first is negative. He suggests better phrasings. The legal effect of jest is that the speaker does not choose or consent to the legal ruling (e.g., the transfer of ownership in a sale), though he does consent to the utterance itself. Therefore, a contract made in jest is invalid (fasad) because consent to the ruling is lacking. This is compared to khiyar al-shart (option of stipulation), where the buyer may lack full consent to the ruling initially but the contract remains valid. The key difference: jest corrupts the sale, while khiyar al-shart does not. The condition for a contract to be considered jest is that it be explicitly stated before the contract that it is pure play, providing no benefit at all. The commentator also notes that some scholars suggest that the word 'ma' is extra or the phrase is inverted, but he prefers the clear definition: jest is when the literal nor figurative meaning is intended.

Key Terms
هزل (hazl): Jest in legal acts: intending neither literal nor figurative meaning but pure play.
جد (jidd): Seriousness: intending the literal or figurative meaning; opposite of hazl.
خيار الشرط (khiyar al-shart): Option of stipulation: a clause in a contract allowing one party to cancel within a set period; does not invalidate the contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the key difference between a sale done in jest and a sale with khiyar al-shart?
A) Both are invalid.
B) Jest invalidates the sale; khiyar al-shart does not.
C) Khiyar al-shart invalidates the sale; jest does not.
D) There is no difference.

Key Takeaway
Jest invalidates a contract only if explicitly stated as pure play before the contract, because consent to the ruling is absent.

Jest in the Price Amount: The Hanafi Rule and Intra-Madhhab Dispute
Ruling on jest in the price amount with prior collusion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four scenarios of jest in the price amount with prior collusion, and apply the Hanafi usul rule that validity is the origin in contracts to distinguish between Abu Hanifa's view and the Sahibayn's view.

Core Idea
Jest in the price amount does not nullify the sale; the named price prevails unless the parties build on the collusion, where Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn differ.

This passage from Nur al-Anwar addresses a nuanced case: when parties secretly agree on a real price but publicly jest about a different amount. How does the law treat such jest? The text presents four scenarios and reveals a key intra-Hanafi dispute. By studying this, you will sharpen your ability to distinguish between the roles of external declaration (musamma) and hidden intent (muwada'a) in contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four scenarios
The text enumerates four possible agreements between the parties after the public jest: both turn away from the collusion, both agree no collusion was present, they differ on whether they turned away or built upon it, or both agree they built upon it. List these scenarios and note the ruling in each.
The first scenario (turning away) is so obvious that some copies omit it.
2
Analyze the third scenario: disagreement
When the parties differ on whether they built upon or turned away from the collusion, the text states that the jest is void and the named price is valid. Understand the reason: validity is the origin (asl) in contracts.
This shows the Hanafi principle that contracts are presumed valid unless invalidity is certain.
3
Analyze the fourth scenario: building upon collusion
When both agree they built upon the collusion, Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn diverge. Abu Hanifa holds the price is the nominal 2000; the Sahibayn hold it is the hidden 1000. Understand each side's reasoning.
Abu Hanifa's analogy: if the hidden price were taken, the acceptance would be conditional, invalidating the sale like selling a free person and a slave together.
4
Trace the usul principle behind the dispute
The core issue is how to treat a statement made in jest (hazl) when there is a certain hidden agreement. Abu Hanifa prioritizes the contract's validity (avoiding conditional acceptance), while the Sahibayn prioritize the certain hidden intent.
This reflects a broader usul rule: hazl (jest) is void if it contradicts a serious intention, but its effect depends on whether the jest is considered part of the contract's expression.
5
Apply the rule to a new scenario
Consider a case where the parties jest about the quantity of goods, not the price. Use the same framework: if they build upon the jest, does the hidden quantity prevail? Apply the analogy from the price case.
This tests your understanding of the underlying illa (effective cause).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن كان ذلك في القدر بأن يقولا : إن البيع بيننا وبينك تام، ولكن تواضع في القدر أي في السر ونظهر بحضور الخلق أن الثمن ألفان، وفي الواقع يكون الثمن ألفًا، فهذه أيضًا أربعة أقسام: فإن اتفقا على الأعراض كان الثمن ألفين؛ لأنهما لما أعرضا عن المواضعة والهزل يكون الاعتبار بالتسمية، وهذا القسم لظهوره لم يُذكر في بعض النسخ. بالاتفاق وإن اتفقا على أنهما لم يحضرهما شيء، أو اختلفا، فالهزل باطل، والتسمية صحيحة من البناء والأعراض في البناء والأعراض عنده وعندهما العمل بالمواضعة واجب والألف الذي هزلا به باطل؛ فيكون الثمن عنده أي الإمام أي الصاحبين ألفين، وعندهما ألف بناءً على ما تقدّم من أصله وأصلهما. الصاحبين وإن اتفقا على البناء على المواضعة، فالثمن ألفان عنده؛ لأنه لو جعل الثمن ألفا يكون قبول الألف الذي هو غير داخل في البيع شرطًا لقبول الآخر، فيفسد البيع بمنزلة ما لو جمع أي في البيع بين حرّ ،وعبد، فلا بد أن يكون الثمن ألفين ليصح العقد، وعندهما الثمن ألف؛ لأن غرضه من ذكر الألف هزلاً هو المقابلة بالمبيع، فكان ذكره هو الظاهر: فإنه لم يوجد ناقض تلك المواضعة صراحةً. (القمر) وإن كان ذلك: أي الهزل في القدر أي قدر الثمن. (القمر) فإن اتفقا أي بعد تفرّق الناس على الأعراض أي عن المواضعة على الهزل. (القمر) شيء: أي الأعراض عن المواضعة أو البناء عليها (القمر) أو اختلفا بأن يقول رجل: إنا بيننا العقد على المواضعة على الهزل وقال الآخر: إنا أعرضنا عن المواضعة وعقدنا على هذا القدر جدًا. (القمر) صحيحة لأن الصحة أصل في العقد وأولى بالاعتبار. (القمر) واجب فإن وجود المواضعة يقيني، ولم يتحقق رافعه صريحًا. (القمر) ألف والألف الزائد على المواضعة باطل (القمر) فكان ذكره إلخ: فلا يلزم ذكر غير الثمن شرطًا لقبول العقد، فإن غرضهما من ذكر الألف الذي هزلا به السمعة، وهذا قد حصل. (القمر) والسكوت عنه سواء كما في النكاح، وهو رواية عن أبي حنيفة له أيضًا. أي ما قال صاحباه
And if that (jest) is in the amount, such that they say: The sale between us and you is complete, but we colluded in the amount (i.e., secretly) and we show in front of people that the price is two thousand, while in reality the price is one thousand, then these also have four divisions: If they both agree on turning away (from the collusion), then the price is two thousand, because since they turned away from the collusion and jest, consideration is given to what is named, and this division due to its obviousness was not mentioned in some copies. By agreement. And if they agree that nothing (about turning away) was present in their minds, or they differ, then the jest is void and the naming (of the price) is valid. Regarding building upon or turning away from the collusion, according to him (Imam Abu Hanifa) and according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), acting upon the collusion is obligatory, and the thousand with which they jested is void; thus the price according to him (Imam Abu Hanifa) is two thousand, and according to the two it is one thousand, based on what preceded of his and their principles. And if they agree on building upon the collusion, then the price is two thousand according to him (Imam), because if the price were made one thousand, the acceptance of the one thousand which is not included in the sale would become a condition for the acceptance of the other, thus the sale would be invalid, like when one combines (in a sale) a free person and a slave, so the price must be two thousand for the contract to be valid. And according to the two, the price is one thousand, because their purpose in mentioning the thousand in jest is to match it with the object of sale, so its mention is apparent, since no explicit repudiator of that collusion has occurred. (al-Qamar) 'And if that is' meaning jest in the amount, i.e., the amount of the price. (al-Qamar) 'If they both agree' meaning after the people disperse, on turning away, i.e., from the collusion on jest. (al-Qamar) 'Nothing' meaning turning away from the collusion or building upon it. (al-Qamar) 'Or they differ' such that one says: We performed the contract based on the collusion on jest, and the other says: We turned away from the collusion and contracted on this amount seriously. (al-Qamar) 'valid' because validity is the origin in contracts and more deserving of consideration. (al-Qamar) 'obligatory' because the existence of the collusion is certain, and its repudiator has not been realized explicitly. (al-Qamar) 'a thousand' and the extra thousand beyond the collusion is void. (al-Qamar) 'So its mention etc.': It does not necessitate considering something other than the price as a condition for accepting the contract, because their purpose in mentioning the thousand with which they jested is reputation, and this has been achieved. (al-Qamar) And remaining silent about it is the same, as in marriage, and this is a narration from Abu Hanifa as well. i.e., what his two companions said.
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the effect of jest (hazl) in the amount of the price in a sale where the parties have secretly colluded (muwada'a) on a different price. The text first sets up a case where they agree to show a price of two thousand dirhams in public but in reality the price is one thousand. It then enumerates four scenarios: 1) both parties turn away from the collusion and treat the nominal price seriously – here the price is the named two thousand. 2) they agree that no collusion or turning away entered their minds at the time of contract – here the jest is void and the named price stands. 3) they differ on whether they were building upon the collusion or had turned away – according to Abu Hanifa, the collusion is given effect and the price is the hidden one thousand (but read carefully: the text says 'عنده وعندهما العمل بالمواضعة واجب والألف الذي هزلا به باطل؛ فيكون الثمن عنده ألفين وعندهما ألف' – actually it says the price according to him is two thousand and according to them is one thousand? Wait: it says 'فيكون الثمن عنده أي الإمام أي الصاحبين ألفين، وعندهما ألف' – so according to Imam Abu Hanifa the price is two thousand, and according to the two companions it is one thousand. This is a key ikhtilaf. 4) they both agree that they were building upon the prior collusion – here the text explains that according to Abu Hanifa the price must be two thousand to avoid the sale being invalid due to a conditional acceptance, while according to the Sahibayn the price is one thousand because the jested amount is considered merely for matching the object of sale and silence about it is the same as its mention. The text then provides a commentary from al-Qamar explaining the details of each scenario, and notes a narration from Abu Hanifa that agrees with the Sahibayn's position in one case.

Key Terms
الهزل (al-hazl): In this context, jest or joking in a statement of price that contradicts the secretly agreed price.
المواضعة (al-muwada'a): A secret agreement or collusion between contracting parties to conceal the true price and state a different price in public.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case where both parties agree that they built upon the prior collusion (al-bina' 'ala al-muwada'a) and the hidden price is 1000 but the named price is 2000, what is the price according to Abu Hanifa?
A) 1000
B) 2000
C) The sale is invalid
D) The price is determined by qiyas

Key Takeaway
Jest (hazl) in the price amount does not automatically nullify the sale; the named price generally prevails unless the parties intentionally build on the collusion, in which case there is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school between Abu Hanifa (nominal price) and the Sahibayn (hidden price).

Definition of Hazl and Its Effect on Contracts
Defines hazl and its effect on various contracts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define hazl (jest) in Hanafi usul, distinguish its effect on contracts involving property vs. non-property, and apply the ruling to the dispute over dower in marriage.

Core Idea
Jest in marriage, divorce, and oath is binding; in property contracts intent matters but dower in marriage is an exception due to its subsidiary nature.

This passage from a Hanafi usul text defines hazl (jest) and its legal effect across different contracts. It explains a fundamental principle: serious statements made in jest are binding for marriage, divorce, and oaths as per the hadith. However, in property contracts the intent may be considered, leading to a well-known intra-Hanafi dispute over the dower amount when publicly stated differently.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term and its scope
Read the passage's definition of hazl (jest) and note that it applies to legal statements where the speaker does not intend the apparent meaning. The text then categorizes contracts based on the role of property (mal).
2
Apply the hadith to non-property contracts
The hadith "Three things..." is cited to show that in contracts without property (divorce, manumission, oath), the serious ruling applies regardless of jest. Note that the hadith is zanni in transmission but qati in meaning according to Hanafi usul.
The hadith is the key dalil; its general implication (amm) indicates binding for all instances.
3
Distinguish contracts with property as primary vs subsidiary
In sale (property primary), ignoring the stated price due to hazl would empty the contract, so the stated price is binding. In marriage (property subsidiary), the dower is not the primary aim; the passage then examines jest in origin vs jest in amount.
This distinction is crucial for understanding the following dispute.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on dower amount
For a marriage with a publicly stated dower of 2000 but privately intended 1000, Abu Hanifa rules 2000 is due (to avoid a corrupt condition), while the Sahibayn rule 1000 (by analogy to sale where jest in price invalidates). Trace the reasoning: Abu Hanifa treats dower as subsidiary, so the stated amount prevents corruption; the Sahibayn treat it like sale where intent prevails.
The thamarah al-khilaf: practical difference in the dower amount.
5
Summarize the overall ruling for hazl
Conclude: for non-property contracts (divorce, etc.) and the origin of marriage, hazl is irrelevant and the contract is binding. For property in sale, hazl invalidates the price/contract. For the dower amount in marriage, there is disagreement, with Abu Hanifa's view being the relied-upon position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان الأهلية
تعريف الهزل وشرطه بخلاف الثاني؛ إذ لو اعتبرت المواضعة فيه بعدم المسمى ويوجب خلو العقد عن الثمن في البيع، وهو يُفسد البيع، فلذا وجبت التسمية، ولم يعتبر العمل بالمواضعة. وإن كان في الذي لا مال فيه كالطلاق والعتاق واليمين فذلك صحيح، والهزل باطل بالحديث، وهو قوله عليه السلام: "ثلاث جدّهن جدّ وهزلهن جدّ: النكاح والطلاق واليمين" وفي بعض الروايات "النكاح والعتاق واليمين"، وصورة المواضعة فيه أن يواضعا على أن ينكحها ويطلقها، أو يعتقها بحضور الناس، وليس في الواقع كذلك، والمراد باليمين: التعليق بأن يواضع الرجل مع امرأته أو عبده أن يعلق طلاقها أو عتاقه علانية، ولا يكون في الواقع كذلك، وليس المراد به اليمين بالله تعالى؛ إذ لا يتصوّر المواضعة فيها، ففي هذه الصور في كل حال من الأحوال يلزم العقد ويبطل الهزل، ويلحق بهذه الصور العفو عن القصاص والنذر ونحوه.
وإن كان المال فيه تبعًا كالنكاح، فإن المهر فيه ليس بمقصود، وإنما المقصود ابتغاء البضع. فإن هَزَلا بأصله بأن يقول لها: إني أنكحك بحضور الخلق، وليس بيننا نكاح، فالعقد لازم والهزل باطل، سواء اتفقا على البناء أو الأعراض، أو عدم حضور شيء منهما، أو اختلفا فيه. وإن هزلا في القدر بأن يزوجها علانية بألفين، ويكون المهر في الواقع ألفًا، فإن اتفقا على قدر البدل في النكاح الأعراض فالمهر ألفان بالاتفاق؛ لأن لهما ولاية الأعراض عن الهزل، وإن اتفقا على البناء فالمهر ألف بالاتفاق؛ لأن ذكر أحد الألفين كان على سبيل الهزل، والمال لا يثبت مع الهزل والفرق لأبي حنيفة بينه وبين البيع حيث أوجب الألفين في البيع، والألف في النكاح أنه لو لم يجعل الثمن ألفين لكان شرطًا فاسدًا، كذلك: أي تعليق الطلاق والعتاق، يعني يكون الزوج أو المولى هازلاً في ذلك لا قاصدًا. ويلحق بهذه إلخ فلو عفا عن القصاص هزلاً أو نذر هزلاً فذلك صحيح والهزل باطل. وإن كان المال : هذا قسم ثانٍ لِمَا لا يحتمل النقض. ليس بمقصود إلخ : فإن المقصود الأصلي من الجانبين: الحلّ الذي يحصل به التوالد والتناسل، والمال فيه لإظهار حظر المحل لا مقصودا، فيكون تبعًا. بيننا نكاح: أو يقول: إني أنكح فلانةً وليس بيننا نكاح على البناء: أي على المواضعة السابقة أو الأعراض أي عن المواضعة السابقة أو عدم حضور شيء منهما أي من البناء والأعراض وقت عقد النكاح، أو اختلفا فيه أي قال واحد إنا بنينا على المواضعة السابقة وقال الآخر: أعرضنا عنها. يكون فالنكاح صحيح أوجب الألفين والصاحبان الألف قياسًا على النكاح مطلقا في الأحوال كلها. على البناء: أي بناء العقد على الاتفاق السابق. لكان شرطًا فاسدًا : وهو شرط قبول الألف الذي هو غير داخل.
Explanation of legal capacity. Definition of hazl and its condition: contrary to the second; for if the mutual agreement (muwada‘a) is considered in it by not specifying the price, it causes the contract to be empty of the price in sale, and that invalidates the sale. Therefore, specification is required, and acting upon the mutual agreement is not considered. And if it is in something that has no property like divorce, manumission, and oath, then that is valid, and the hazl is invalid by the hadith, which is his saying (peace be upon him): 'Three things their seriousness is serious and their jest is serious: marriage, divorce, and oath.' In some narrations: 'marriage, manumission, and oath.' The form of mutual agreement in it is that they agree that he will marry her and divorce her, or emancipate her in front of people, while in reality it is not so. And what is meant by oath is the conditional: that a man agrees with his wife or his slave that he will conditionally divorce her or emancipate him publicly, while in reality it is not so. And what is meant by it is not an oath by Allah; for mutual agreement cannot be imagined in it. So in these cases, in every circumstance, the contract becomes binding and the hazl is invalid. And joining these cases is forgiveness of qisas, nadhr, and the like. And if the property is subsidiary like marriage, then the dower is not intended; rather the intended end is seeking the vulva. Then if they jest in its origin — such as he says to her: 'I marry you in front of people, and there is no marriage between us' — then the contract is binding and the hazl is invalid, whether they agree upon building (on the previous agreement) or turning away, or the absence of either of them, or they differ about it. And if they jest in the amount — such that he marries her publicly for two thousand, while the dower in reality is one thousand — then if they agree upon the consideration in the contract being the turning away, the dower is two thousand by agreement, because they have authority over turning away from hazl. And if they agree upon building, then the dower is one thousand by agreement, because the mention of one of the thousands was by way of hazl, and property is not established with hazl. And for Abu Hanifa, the difference between this and sale — where he obligated two thousand in sale and one thousand in marriage — is that if he had not made the price two thousand, it would have been a corrupt condition. Likewise: meaning conditional divorce and manumission, meaning the husband or master is jesting in that, not intending. And joining these: if one forgives qisas as a jest or makes a nadhr as a jest, that is valid and the hazl is invalid. And if the property: this is a second division for what does not admit of nullification. [The dower] is not intended, etc.: for the primary objective from both sides is the licitness (hull) that results in procreation, and property therein is to show the prohibition of the place, not intended, so it is subsidiary. 'No marriage between us': or he says: 'I marry so-and-so and there is no marriage between us.' 'On building': i.e., on the previous agreement, or 'turning away' i.e., from the previous agreement, or 'absence of either of them' i.e., of building or turning away at the time of the marriage contract, or 'they differ about it' i.e., one says 'we built on the previous agreement' and the other says 'we turned away from it.' Then the marriage is valid; [Abu Hanifa] obligated two thousand, while the two companions obligated one thousand by analogy to marriage, absolutely in all circumstances. 'On building': i.e., building the contract on the previous agreement. 'It would have been a corrupt condition': that is, the condition of accepting the thousand that is not included.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the definition of hazl (jest) and its conditions, from the chapter on legal capacity (al-ahliyya). The text begins by explaining that in contracts where hazl involves the specification of the price (as in sale), considering the mutual agreement (muwada‘a) to ignore the named price would lead to an invalid contract, so the specified price must be taken seriously. In contrast, for contracts that involve no property like divorce, manumission, and oath, the hadith 'Three things their seriousness is serious and their jest is serious: marriage, divorce, and oath' establishes that the contract is binding regardless of jest. The hadith is cited from various sources. The passage then categorizes contracts based on the role of property: (1) contracts where property is subsidiary like marriage (the primary aim is sexual relations), (2) contracts with no property like divorce, and (3) contracts where property is primary like sale. For marriage, jest in the origin (denying the marriage itself) is irrelevant; the contract is valid. Jest in the amount of dower (e.g., publicly stating two thousand but privately intending one thousand) leads to a dispute: Abu Hanifa rules that the stated amount (two thousand) is due, because otherwise the condition would be corrupt, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the two companions) rule that the intended amount (one thousand) is due, analogizing to marriage. The text also clarifies that forgiveness of qisas and nadhr are included in the same rule. The commentary by later scholars like al-Sanblī, al-Qamar, and al-Muhashshī provides additional clarification on terms and distinctions.

Key Terms
الهزل (al-hazl): Jest or mockery in a legal statement, where the speaker utters a binding contract but does not intend its legal effect.
المواضعة (al-muwāḍa‘a): Mutual agreement between two parties to act in a certain way, often in secrecy or jest.
البضع (al-baḍ‘): Vulva; metaphorically, sexual relations or the object of marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on a marriage contract where the groom publicly states a dower of two thousand but privately intends one thousand, and they both agree on the public statement?
A) The marriage is invalid because of jest.
B) The dower is one thousand because that is the real intent.
C) The dower is two thousand according to Abu Hanifa.
D) The dower is two thousand according to the two companions.

Key Takeaway
Hazl (jest) does not affect contracts of marriage, divorce, and oaths; in property contracts, intent may be considered, but in marriage the stated dower prevails to avoid a corrupt condition.

The Ruling of Hazl (Jest) in Marriage Contracts
Explaining the definition and legal effect of hazl in marriage and analogous contracts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul rule that hazl in the principal of a contract does not invalidate it, and distinguish between hazl in the principal versus the quantity/type of the dower, determining the operative ruling based on the parties' agreement (bina' vs i'rad) and the hierarchy of istihsan over qiyas.

Core Idea
Hazl in the principal of marriage does not void the contract; but jest in the dower amount is nullified because wealth is subordinate.

This passage from Nur al-Anwar explores the legal effect of uttering a marriage contract in jest (hazl). While some might think that joking invalidates the entire contract, the Hanafi school holds a nuanced position: the marriage itself remains binding, but the jest may nullify certain subordinate elements like the dower. Understanding the distinction between hazl in the principal (asl) and hazl in the quantity (qadr) or type (jins) of the dower is essential, as is the ikhtilaf between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two students regarding the basis of the ruling—whether to analogize to sale or to give precedence to the subordinate nature of wealth in marriage.

Guided Path
1
Define hazl and its scope
Identify the definition of hazl from the text: it is jest while uttering a contract, but only applicable where hypothetical agreement (muwada'a) is possible. Exclude oaths by Allah. Then list the contracts covered: marriage, talaq, emancipation, pardon for qisas, vows.
Note that the text explicitly excludes oaths because they do not admit of prior agreement.
2
Distinguish hazl in asl vs. qadr/jins
Hazl in the principal (asl) of the contract—e.g., saying 'I marry you in jest'—still makes the contract binding. Hazl in the dower (qadr or jins) affects only the dower, not the marriage itself. The text splits the discussion into these two categories.
The distinction is crucial because the ruling on the dower depends on whether the parties agree on bina' (building on the prior jest agreement) or i'rad (turning away from it).
3
Apply the hadith and qiyas/istihsan
The text cites a hadith (mentioned) that three matters are serious: marriage, divorce, emancipation—even if jest is intended. This establishes the general rule that hazl does not nullify these contracts. Then, for the dower, compare sale (where price is primary) to marriage (where dower is subordinate). Abu Hanifa uses istihsan to override qiyas on sale, giving precedence to the subordinate nature of the dower.
Identify the two steps: first the hadith for the principal, then the ijtihadi reasoning for the dower.
4
Trace the ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn
When the parties disagree about bina' or i'rad, or neither is present, the text presents two narrations: one from Abu Hanifa (via Muhammad) that the mahr is the lower amount (1000) based on istihsan, and another from Abu Yusuf that it is the higher amount (2000) based on qiyas on sale. Understand each position's reasoning.
This ikhtilaf is the core of the passage. Note that the Sahibayn's position is also attributed in some sources to Abu Hanifa, but the mufta bihi is the lower amount.
5
Extend to other contracts and hazl in jins
The text broadens the ruling to similar cases: pardon for qisas, vows, and conditional divorce/emancipation. Then it discusses hazl in the type of dower (e.g., dinars vs dirhams) with similar principles. Conclude by synthesizing the pattern: hazl in subordinate matters is ineffective, but the contract remains valid.
Pay attention to the extensions: the same logic applies to any wealth in a contract where wealth is not the primary objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان الأهلية
تعريف الهزل وشرطه
ولا يكون في الواقع كذلك، وليس المراد به اليمين بالله تعالى؛ إذ لا يتصوّر المواضعة فيها، ففي هذه الصور في كل حال من الأحوال يلزم العقد ويبطل الهزل، ويلحق بهذه الصور العفو عن القصاص والنذر ونحوه.
وإن كان المال فيه تبعًا كالنكاح، فإن المهر فيه ليس بمقصود، وإنما المقصود ابتغاء البضع.
أي فيما وقع فيه الهزل
فإن هَزَلا بأصله بأن يقول لها: إني أنكحك بحضور الخلق، وليس بيننا نكاح، فالعقد لازم والهزل باطل، سواء اتفقا على البناء أو الأعراض، أو عدم حضور شيء منهما، أو اختلفا فيه.
بالحديث المذكور
وإن هزلا في القدر بأن يزوجها علانية بألفين، ويكون المهر في الواقع ألفًا، فإن اتفقا على قدر البدل في النكاح الأعراض فالمهر ألفان بالاتفاق؛ لأن لهما ولاية الأعراض عن الهزل أي من الهزل وإن اتفقا على البناء فالمهر ألف بالاتفاق؛ لأن ذكر أحد الألفين كان على سبيل الهزل، والمال لا يثبت مع الهزل والفرق لأبي حنيفة الله بينه وبين البيع حيث أوجب الألفين في البيع، والألف في النكاح أنه لو لم يجعل الثمن ألفين لكان شرطًا فاسدًا،
كذلك: أي تعليق الطلاق والعتاق، يعني يكون الزوج أو المولى هازلاً في ذلك لا قاصدًا. (القمر) ويلحق بهذه إلخ فلو عفا عن القصاص هزلاً أو نذر هزلاً فذلك صحيح والهزل باطل.(القمر)
وإن كان المال : هذا قسم ثانٍ لِمَا لا يحتمل النقض. (المحشي) ليس بمقصود إلخ : فإن المقصود الأصلي من الجانبين:
الحلّ الذي يحصل به التوالد والتناسل، والمال فيه لإظهار حظر المحل لا مقصودا، فيكون تبعًا. (السنبلي) بيننا نكاح: أو يقول: إني أنكح فلانةً وليس بيننا نكاح (المحشي على البناء: أي على المواضعة السابقة أو الأعراض أي عن المواضعة السابقة أو عدم حضور شيء منهما أي من البناء والأعراض وقت عقد النكاح، أو اختلفا فيه أي قال واحد إنا بنينا على المواضعة السابقة وقال الآخر: أعرضنا عنها. (القمر)
يكون فالنكاح صحيح أوجب الألفين والصاحبان الألف قياسًا على النكاح (المحشي)
مطلقا في الأحوال كلها. (المحشي) على البناء: أي بناء العقد على الاتفاق السابق.(القمر)
لكان شرطًا فاسدًا : وهو شرط قبول الألف الذي هو غير داخل.(القمر)
بيان الأهلية
تعريف الهزل وشرطه
أي الشرط الفاسد
وهو يؤثر في فساد البيع، ولا يؤثر في فساد النكاح، لا في أصل العقد ولا في الصداق. وإن اتفقا على أنه لم يحضر هما شيء، أو اختلفا، فالنكاح جائز بألف في رواية محمد عن أبي حنيفة رحله وقيل: بألفين في رواية أبي يوسف له عنه، وجه الرواية الثانية: هو القياس على البيع، ووجه الرواية الأولى : وهو الاستحسان أن المهر في النكاح تابع، فلا يجوز ترجيح جانب التسمية على الهزل؛ لأنه يكون المهر حينئذٍ مقصودًا بالذات، وهو خلاف الأصل، بخلاف البيع؛
أي رواية محمد الله
أي حين الترجيح
لأن الثمن مقصود فيه، فيكون تصحيحه أيضًا مقصودًا ، فيرجح جانب التسمية على الهزل.
وإن كان في الجنس بأن تواضعا على الدنانير والمهر في الحقيقة دراهم،
أي الهزل أي جنس المهر
فإن اتفقا على
الأعراض فالمهر ما سميا، وإن اتفقا على البناء، واتفقا على أنه لم يحضرهما
أي عن الهزل
أي على المواضعة السابقة شيء، أو اختلفا يجب مهر المثل في الصور الثلاث، أما في الأولى فبالإجماع؛ لأنهما قصدا
الهزل بالمسمى والمال لا يجب به وما كان مهرًا في الواقع لم يذكر في العقد،
أي بالهزل
أي الدراهم
ولا يؤثر فإن النكاح لا يفسد بالشرط الفاسد، لا أصله ولا ،صداقه بل يبطل الشرط، فلا ضرر ههنا لو لم يجعل الألف الزائد مهرًا ويقع شرطًا، ففي صحة النكاح لا يكون ضرراً. (القمر)
شيء: ء أي الأعراض عن المواضعة أو البناء عليها (القمر) وجه الرواية الثانية هي رواية أبي يوسف الله هو القياس على البيع، وحكمه قد مرّ. (القمر) وهو خلاف الأصل فيعتبر الهزل، فالعبرة للأصل وهو الألف. (القمر) مقصود فيه لأنه أحد ركني البيع. (القمر) فإن اتفقا إلخ : هذا أيضًا على أربعة أوجه، والنكاح في كل الوجوه بالاتفاق، وإنما الكلام في وجوب المسمى الوجه الأول ما قال فإن اتفقا على الأعراض إلخ، والوجه
صحيح
الثاني: وإن اتفقا على البناء، والثالث قوله أو اتفقا على أنه إلخ والرابع قوله: أو اختلفا إلخ. (السنبلي) ما ستميا : أي الدنانير لبطلان الواضعة بالأعراض. (المحشي شيء: أي الأعراض عن المواضعة أو البناء عليها.(القمر) أو اختلفا أي قال أحد إنا بنينا على المواضعة السابقة، فقال الآخر: إنا أعرضنا عنها. (القمر)
لم يذكر في العقد وبدون الذكر فيه لا يصير مهرًا، فصار كأنه تزوّجها على غير المهر، ولكن لا يفسد النكاح؛ لأنه يصح بغير تسمية، فيجب مهر المثل، بخلاف حكم البيع، فإنه إذا خلا عن الثمن فسد، فلا يمكن الجمع بين المواضعتين في الهزل بجنس الثمن وفي الجد بأصل البيع (السنبلي)
The definition of hazl and its condition. It is not in reality so, and what is meant is not the oath by Allah; for hypothetical agreement (muwada'a) is not conceivable in it. So in these cases in every situation the contract becomes binding and hazl is invalid. To these cases is attached the pardon for qisas, the vow, and the like. And if the wealth in it is subordinate like marriage, for the mahr in it is not intended, rather the intention is the seeking of the vulva. Meaning: in what hazl occurred. So if they jest in its principal by him saying to her: 'I marry you in the presence of people, but there is no marriage between us,' then the contract is binding and hazl is void, whether they agree on building upon (the prior agreement) or turning away, or that none of them was present, or they differ about it. By the mentioned hadith. And if they jest in the quantity by publicly marrying her for two thousand, while the mahr in reality is one thousand, then if they agree on the amount of the substitute in marriage with turning away, the mahr is two thousand by agreement; because they have authority over turning away from hazl. And if they agree on building upon, then the mahr is one thousand by agreement, because the mention of one thousand was by way of hazl, and wealth does not establish with hazl. And the distinction for Abu Hanifa between it and sale is that in sale he obligated two thousand, and in marriage one thousand: because if he had not made the price two thousand, it would have been a corrupt condition. Similarly: meaning making talaq and emancipation conditional, meaning the husband or master is jesting in that without intending. Attached to these etc. So if one pardons qisas jokingly or makes a vow jokingly, that is valid and the hazl is void. And if the wealth in it is subordinate like marriage... (commentary continues).
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition of the legal effect of hazl (jest) in contracts, particularly focusing on marriage (nikah). It begins by defining hazl and clarifying that it only applies to contracts where a hypothetical agreement (muwada'a) is possible, excluding oaths by Allah. The first major ruling: hazl in the principal (asl) of a contract—e.g., saying 'I marry you in public but there is no marriage'—does not nullify the contract; the contract is binding and the jest is void. This is supported by a mentioned hadith. Then the text discusses hazl in the quantity (qadr) of the dower in marriage. Using the example of marrying for 2000 but secretly agreeing on 1000, it presents the positions: if both parties agree that they have turned away from the prior jest understanding (i'rad), the mahr is 2000; if they agree that they based the contract on the jest understanding (bina'), the mahr is 1000; if they disagree or neither situation occurs, Abu Hanifa's position (in one narration) is that the mahr is 1000, using istihsan because mahr is subordinate, while the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) analogize with sale where the full mentioned price is due. The text also extends similar rulings to talaq, emancipation, pardon for qisas, and vows. Finally, it discusses hazl in the type (jins) of dower, e.g., agreeing on dinars but actual mahr is dirhams, where the rulings are similarly based on the presence or absence of building upon or turning away. Throughout, the commentary emphasizes that marriage is less affected by corrupt conditions than sale, because mahr is subordinate and not a primary pillar.

Key Terms
الهزل (al-hazl): The act of jesting or joking while uttering a contract, without intending its legal consequences.
البناء (al-bina'): Building the formal contract upon the prior hypothetical agreement (muwada'a), indicating that the parties intend to continue the jest.
الأعراض (al-i'rad): Turning away from the prior hypothetical agreement, indicating that the parties intend the nominal terms seriously.
المواضعة (al-muwada'a): The prior hypothetical agreement between the parties to jest in the contract.
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): Juristic preference; departing from qiyas for a stronger consideration, here the subordinate nature of wealth in marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi opinion in the passage, if a man publicly marries a woman for a mahr of 2000 dirhams but secretly agreed that the real mahr is 1000, and later both parties disagree about whether they built upon the secret agreement or turned away from it, what is the ruling?
A) The marriage is invalid due to the uncertainty.
B) The mahr is 2000 dirhams because the public utterance is binding.
C) The mahr is 1000 dirhams based on istihsan.
D) The mahr is mahr al-mithl because the mahr specification is void.

Key Takeaway
Hazl (jest) in the principal of a marriage contract does not invalidate it, but hazl in the subordinate element of the dower may nullify that element, with the operative ruling depending on the parties' agreement (bina' or i'rad) and the application of istihsan over strict qiyas.

The Effect of Jest (Huzl) on Contracts: Qiyas vs Istihsan
Defining huzl and its effect with an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on huzl in sale and marriage, and explain how qiyas and istihsan lead to different positions on the dower.

Core Idea
Huzl invalidates sale but not marriage; the dower dispute shows qiyas yields 2000, istihsan yields 1000.

This passage from Noor al-Anwaar defines huzl (jest) and its legal effect on sale and marriage. It then presents an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani regarding the dower when both parties were joking. The disagreement is rooted in two different usul methods: qiyas with sale versus istihsan that respects the subordinate nature of the dower. Understanding this dispute will deepen your appreciation of how usul principles shape fiqh rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Rule
State the basic Hanafi rule: huzl (a fasid condition of jest) invalidates sale but does not invalidate marriage, neither the contract nor the dower.
Note that 'invalid condition' refers to a mental reservation not expressed in the contract.
2
Locate the Ikhtilaf
When both parties agree no specific mahr was intended, or they disagree, the marriage is valid. The dispute is over the amount: Muhammad's riwaya says 1000, Abu Yusuf's says 2000.
Both narrations come from Abu Hanifa; they are both part of Zahir al-Riwayah.
3
Analyze the Reasoning Behind Each Position
Abu Yusuf uses qiyas with sale: in sale, the price (thaman) is essential, so seriousness prevails over jest. By analogy, in marriage the dower is like a price, so seriousness gives mahr 2000 (the standard minimum?). Muhammad uses istihsan: the dower is subordinate (taba') in marriage, so jest is given effect and the mahr is reduced to 1000.
The text says 'the basis of the first narration is istihsan because the dower is a follower'.
4
Understand the Thamarah al-Khilaf
The practical difference is the amount of mahr: 1000 vs 2000. But both agree the marriage is valid.
This shows that ikhtilaf can affect subsidiary details without changing the core ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تعريف الهزل وشرطه أي الشرط الفاسد وهو يؤثر في فساد البيع، ولا يؤثر في فساد النكاح، لا في أصل العقد ولا في الصداق. وإن اتفقا على أنه لم يحضر هما شيء، أو اختلفا، فالنكاح جائز بألف في رواية محمد عن أبي حنيفة رحله وقيل: بألفين في رواية أبي يوسف له عنه، وجه الرواية الثانية: هو القياس على البيع، ووجه الرواية الأولى : وهو الاستحسان أن المهر في النكاح تابع، فلا يجوز ترجيح جانب التسمية على الهزل؛ لأنه يكون المهر حينئذٍ مقصودًا بالذات، وهو خلاف الأصل، بخلاف البيع؛ أي رواية محمد الله أي حين الترجيح لأن الثمن مقصود فيه، فيكون تصحيحه أيضًا مقصودًا ، فيرجح جانب التسمية على الهزل.
Explanation of huzl (jest) and its condition, i.e., the invalid condition. It affects the invalidity of sale, but does not affect the invalidity of marriage, neither in the contract itself nor in the dower. If they both agree that nothing came to their minds, or they disagree, then the marriage is valid with one thousand in the narration of Muhammad from Abu Hanifa, and it is said with two thousand in the narration of Abu Yusuf from him. The basis of the second narration is analogy with sale, and the basis of the first narration is juristic preference (istihsan) that the dower in marriage is subordinate, so the side of naming (seriousness) cannot be given preference over jest, because then the dower would be intended in itself, which is contrary to the original principle, unlike sale, because the price is intended therein, so its validation is also intended, thus the side of naming is given preference over jest.
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage defines the concept of huzl (jest) in legal transactions and its effect on sale and marriage. It states that a condition that is invalid (fasid) affects the validity of sale but not marriage. In marriage, even if both parties were joking about the dower, the marriage remains valid. If they agreed that no specific dower was intended, or they differ, the marriage is valid with a dower of 1000 (according to Muhammad's narration from Abu Hanifa) or 2000 (according to Abu Yusuf's narration). Abu Yusuf's position is based on qiyas (analogy) with sale, where the price is essential, so seriousness prevails. Muhammad's position, based on istihsan, holds that in marriage the dower is secondary (taba'), so the jest is not overridden. This explains why huzl in sale nullifies the contract but in marriage it does not.

Key Terms
الهزل (al-hazl): Jest or mockery in a legal transaction where the parties do not intend the legal effects
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical deduction used by Abu Yusuf to compare marriage to sale
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): Juristic preference used by Muhammad to give priority to jest in marriage

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on a marriage contract entered in jest regarding the dower, if the parties later agree no specific amount was intended?
A) The marriage is invalid because the dower is not specified.
B) The marriage is valid with a mahr of 2000 based on qiyas.
C) The marriage is valid with a mahr of 1000 in the preferred narration.
D) The marriage is valid but requires a new mahr agreement.

Key Takeaway
Huzl invalidates sale but not marriage, and within Hanafi law the preferred position is that the dower in a jocular marriage is 1000, based on istihsan rather than qiyas.

Huzl in the Genus of Mahr: Istihsan Over Qiyas in Marriage
Analyzing huzl in genus with scenarios and usul reasoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul rule of istihsan to distinguish marriage from sale in cases of huzl regarding mahr genus.

Core Idea
In marriage, absence of a specified mahr due to jest does not void the contract; mahr al-mithl is obligatory, unlike sale where price is essential.

This passage extends the Hanafi discussion of huzl to cases where the parties joke about the genus of the mahr (e.g., dinars vs dirhams). The core usul debate is whether to apply qiyas on sale (Abu Yusuf) or istihsan (Muhammad al-Shaybani). The Hanafi school favors Muhammad's riwaya, emphasizing that marriage does not require mahr specification at contracting, so the jest is given effect and mahr al-mithl becomes due.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four scenarios
Extract the four scenarios from the passage: (1) both abandon mockery, (2) both build on mockery with no recollection, (3) both build and disagree on what was said, (4) one says build, other says abandon. Note the ruling for each.
The text says three scenarios where mahr al-mithl is obligatory, but actually four are listed; the first scenario (abandon) results in named mahr.
2
Understand the usul reasoning
Abu Yusuf applies qiyas on sale: in sale, the price is essential, so seriousness prevails and the named amount applies. Muhammad applies istihsan: marriage does not require mahr specification, so the jest is given effect and mahr al-mithl is due.
Istihsan overrides qiyas due to the difference between marriage and sale.
3
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: in scenarios 2-4 (building or disagreement), Muhammad says mahr al-mithl, Abu Yusuf says the named mahr (e.g., dinars).
4
Determine the mufta bihi position
The text favors Muhammad's riwaya by highlighting that marriage is valid without mahr specification, so the jest does not harm the contract.
This is the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(القمر) شيء: ء أي الأعراض عن المواضعة أو البناء عليها (القمر) وجه الرواية الثانية هي رواية أبي يوسف الله هو القياس على البيع، وحكمه قد مرّ. (القمر) وهو خلاف الأصل فيعتبر الهزل، فالعبرة للأصل وهو الألف. (القمر) مقصود فيه لأنه أحد ركني البيع. (القمر) فإن اتفقا إلخ : هذا أيضًا على أربعة أوجه، والنكاح في كل الوجوه بالاتفاق، وإنما الكلام في وجوب المسمى الوجه الأول ما قال فإن اتفقا على الأعراض إلخ، والوجه صحيح الثاني: وإن اتفقا على البناء، والثالث قوله أو اتفقا على أنه إلخ والرابع قوله: أو اختلفا إلخ. (السنبلي) ما ستميا : أي الدنانير لبطلان الواضعة بالأعراض. (المحشي شيء: أي الأعراض عن المواضعة أو البناء عليها.(القمر) أو اختلفا أي قال أحد إنا بنينا على المواضعة السابقة، فقال الآخر: إنا أعرضنا عنها. And if it is in the genus, that they agreed upon dinars while the actual mahr is dirhams. If they agree on turning away (from the mockery), then the mahr is what they named. If they agree on building (upon the mockery), and agree that nothing came to their minds, or they disagree, then mahr al-mithl is obligatory in three scenarios. As for the first, by consensus, because they intended jest with the named amount and the property is not due by it, and what was actually the mahr was not mentioned in the contract, and it has no effect because marriage is not invalidated by an invalid condition, neither its contract nor its dower; rather the condition becomes void. So there is no harm here if the extra thousand is not made mahr and becomes a condition; in the validity of marriage there is no harm. (al-Qamar) Something: meaning turning away from the prior understanding or building upon it. (al-Qamar) The basis of the second narration is the riwaya of Abu Yusuf, it is analogy with sale, and its ruling has passed. (al-Qamar) It is contrary to the original principle, so the jest is considered, and the consideration is for the original, which is the thousand. (al-Qamar) Intended therein because it is one of the pillars of sale. (al-Qamar) 'If they agree etc.': this also has four aspects, and marriage in all aspects is agreed upon, but the discussion is about the obligation of the named. (al-Muhashshi) 'Something': meaning turning away from the prior understanding or building upon it. (al-Qamar) 'Or they disagree': that one says 'we built upon the prior understanding' and the other says 'we turned away from it.' (al-Qamar) It was not mentioned in the contract and without mention it does not become mahr, so it is as if he married her without specifying mahr, but the marriage is not invalid because it is valid without specification, so mahr al-mithl is obligatory, unlike the ruling of sale, for if it is devoid of the price it becomes void, so the two understandings cannot be combined: jest in the genus of the price and seriousness in the original sale (al-Sunbuli).
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage extends the discussion of huzl to cases where the parties joke about the genus (jins) of the mahr, e.g., they agree on dinars but the actual mahr is dirhams. Four scenarios arise: (1) Both abandon the mockery: the named mahr applies. (2) Both stick to the mockery but have no recollection of the actual mahr: mahr al-mithl applies. (3) Both stick to the mockery and disagree on what was said: mahr al-mithl. (4) One says they built on mockery, the other says they abandoned it: mahr al-mithl. The key point: in marriage, the contract does not fail even without a specified mahr, unlike sale where the price is essential. The marginal notes explain that Muhammad's riwaya (mahr al-mithl) is based on istihsan, while Abu Yusuf's riwaya (named mahr) is based on qiyas with sale.

Key Terms
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The equivalent dower determined by the social status of the woman and her family
الأعراض (al-a'rad): Turning away from the prior mockery, i.e., abandoning the jest

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, in which scenario does the named mahr apply?
A) Both parties build on the mockery and have no recollection
B) Both parties abandon the mockery
C) Both parties disagree on whether they built on the mockery
D) None of the above

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, istihsan overrides qiyas in marriage, making the contract valid with mahr al-mithl when the mahr is jokingly specified.
