Hazl Has No Effect in Contracts Where Property Is Essential (Khul', I'taq, Sulh)
Discussing huzl in contracts where property is a pillar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul rule that hazl (jest) has no effect in contracts where property is essential, such as khul' and sulh, and identify the source hadith and rationale.

Core Idea
In contracts where property is a pillar, jest does not nullify the obligation; the contract is binding.

This passage from Noor al-Anwar addresses a critical exception in Hanafi usul: while in ordinary contracts like sale, hazl (jest) may render the contract void, in contracts where property is an essential element—such as khul' (divorce by compensation) and al-sulh 'an dam al-'amd (settlement for intentional homicide)—hazl has no effect. According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), even if the parties openly agree to act in jest, the contract remains enforceable: divorce occurs and the property is due. This rule is derived from the principle that khul' does not admit khiyar al-shart (option condition), and since hazl is analogous to an option, it too is ineffective.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contracts where property is essential
From the source text, note the three contracts: khul', i'taq bi mal (emancipation for money), and al-sulh 'an dam al-'amd (settlement for intentional homicide). In these, property (mal) is a fundamental element because it must be mentioned and named for the contract to be valid.
Contrast with marriage, where mahr is not an essential pillar for the contract's validity.
2
Understand the scenario of hazl
The parties agree to perform the contract in front of people as a jest, intending it to be empty. They may build on a prior understanding (al-bina') or turn away from it (al-a'rad), or disagree about the understanding.
The hazl here is in the very essence of the contract, not just a side condition.
3
Locate the ruling of the Sahibayn
According to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), hazl has no effect: the divorce occurs and the property is binding. This holds regardless of whether they built on the mockery, turned away, or disagreed.
The text emphasizes 'على أصلهما' (according to their principle).
4
Analyze the reasoning
Khul' does not bear khiyar al-shart (option condition). For example, if a wife stipulates an option for herself in khul', the property is due and divorce occurs, but the option is void. Since hazl is analogous to an option ('بمنزلة الخيار'), it too is ineffective in khul'.
This analogy is a form of qiyas: hazl is treated like a void condition.
5
Recognize the hadith evidence
A marginal note cites the hadith: 'الحديث ورد بأن الهزل جد في الطلاق والخلع طلاق' (The hadith came that hazl is serious in divorce and khul' is divorce). This directly establishes that hazl in khul' is serious.
The hadith is the primary dalil, but the reasoning via khiyar al-shart provides further support.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن كان المال فيه مقصودا كالخلع والعتق على مال والصلح عن دم العمد، فإن المال مقصود في كل واحد من هذه الأمور؛ لأنه لا يجب بدون الذكر والتسمية فإن هزلا بأصله بأن تواضعا على أن يعقدا هذه العقود بحضور الناس، ويكون في الواقع هزلاً. واتفقا على البناء على المواضعة بعد العقد فالطلاق واقع والمال لازم عندهما، ثم اختلفت العقد أي في صورة الخلع نسخ المتن في هذا المقام، فذكر في بعضها ههنا تحت مذهب صاحبيه هذه العبارة: لأن الهزل لا يؤثر في الخلع عندهما، ولا تختلف الحال عندهما بالبناء أو بالأعراض أو بالاختلاف؛ وذلك لأن الخلع لا يحتمل خيار الشرط، ولهذا لو شرط الخيار لها في الخلع وجب المال ووقع الطلاق، وبطل الخيار، وإذا لم يحتمل خيار الشرط فلا يحتمل الهزل؛ لأن الهزل بمنزلة الخيار فسواء اتفقا على البناء، أو على الأعراض، أو عدم الخصور، ام عام الخلع أو اختلفا فيه يبطل الهزل، ويقع الطلاق، ويلزم المال على أصلهما. في جميع الصور المذكورة لما ذكرنا أي في دليل الصورة الأولى (القمر) وإن كان القسم الثالث لما لا يحتمل النقض. And if the property is intended in it, such as khul' (divorce for ransom), emancipation for money, and compromise for intentional bloodshed, then the property is intended in each of these matters because it is not obligatory without mention and naming. Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage discusses contracts where the mal (property) is a fundamental element, such as khul' (divorce by compensation), i'taq bi mal (manumission for payment), and sulh 'an dim al-amd (settlement for intentional homicide). In these, the property is essential because the contract requires mentioning the property. If the parties make a mockery (hazl) of the entire contract by agreeing to perform it publicly as a jest, the contract is still binding: divorce occurs and the property is due. This is because these contracts, especially khul', do not admit option or jest; they are akin to serious transactions. The marginal notes clarify that according to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), hazl has no effect in khul', and the outcome is the same whether they built on the mockery, turned away, or disagreed. The reason is that khul' does not bear the option condition (khiyar al-shart), and since hazl is like an option, it is ineffective. This contrasts with marriage and sale discussed earlier.

Key Terms
الخلع (al-khul'): Divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation (usually financial) paid to the husband
الصلح عن دم العمد (al-sulh 'an dam al-'amd): Settlement for intentional homicide where the victim's family forgives the killer in exchange for blood money
الهزل (al-hazl): Jest, mockery, or acting in a contract without serious intent

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the reason that hazl is ineffective in khul'?
A) Because khul' is a form of talaq and hazl in talaq is serious
B) Because khul' does not bear khiyar al-shart
C) Both A and B
D) Because property is essential

Key Takeaway
In contracts where property is a primary element, like khul' and sulh, hazl does not affect the contractual obligations; the Hanafi usul principle holds that such contracts are binding even if entered in jest.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

Jest (Hazl) in Khul' and Other Contracts: The Usul Rule
Ruling on jest in legal transactions, especially khul' divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul rule that jest does not affect khul' and similar irrevocable contracts, and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Jest in khul' is treated as serious—divorce is among things where jest is not jest.

This lesson explores the concept of jest (hazl) in Islamic legal theory, specifically its effect on contracts like khul' (divorce for compensation). The Hanafi school has a unique rule: while jest generally invalidates consent, in certain contracts such as divorce and manumission, jest is considered serious due to a prophetic hadith. We will analyze the usul principle behind this, the intra-madhhab dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two companions, and the practical implications for juristic reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal definition of hazl and its general effect
First, understand that hazl is playful speech not meant seriously. In most contracts, it negates true consent and voids the act.
This is the default rule, but there are exceptions.
2
Examine the textual evidence (dalil naqli) that makes jest serious in divorce and khul'
The hadith states: 'Divorce is among things where jest is serious.' This is an ahad hadith but its meaning is clear (qat'i dalala). Khul' is a form of divorce, so it falls under this ruling.
The hadith is the basis for the exception.
3
Contrast Abu Hanifa's view with the Sahibayn's view
According to the Sahibayn, jest in khul' does not affect the divorce: it is valid and the named dower is due immediately. According to Abu Hanifa, the divorce is suspended on the wife's acceptance of the full dower; if she does not accept, no divorce occurs.
Both views are rooted in valid usul reasoning.
4
Understand the subsidiary nature of the dower (mal) and the principle of taba'iyya
The dower is subsidiary to the divorce. Even if jest could affect the dower in isolation, it does not here because the principal (divorce) is unaffected. The ruling of the subsidiary follows the principal unless otherwise established.
This is a key Hanafi usul point: subsidiary rulings can differ from the principal in some cases.
5
Extend the rule to analogous cases
The same principle applies to manumission for property, settlement for intentional homicide blood money, and acknowledgments in jest. In all these, jest is considered serious because they are analogous to divorce.
The author mentions these to show the scope of the rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان الأهلية
تعريف الهزل وشرطه
فإن اتفقا على البناء، أي بناءهما على المواضعة بعد المجالسة، فعندهما الطلاق واقع، والمال أي بعد تفرق المجلس كله؛ لما مرّ أن الهزل لا يؤثر في الخلع عندهما، وإن كان مؤثرًا في المال ولكن المال لازم أي المصنف تابع فيه، ولا يقال: كيف يكون المال تابعًا فيه، وقد نص فيما قبل أن المال مقصود فيه، الخلع ولو سلّم أن المال تابع فيه لكن لا يلزم أن يكون حكمه حكم المتبوع كالنكاح، فإن أي في الخلع المال فيه تابع، ويؤثر الهزل فيه مع أنه لا يؤثر في النكاح؛ لأنا نقول: إن المال في الخلع وإن أي المهر كان مقصودًا للمتعاقدين لكنه تابع للطلاق في حق الثبوت، وأن المال في النكاح وإن أي المال كان تبعًا بالنسبة إلى مقصود المتعاقدين لكنه أصل في الثبوت؛ إذ يثبت بدون الذكر. وعنده يجب أن يتعلّق الطلاق باختيارها فما لم تكن المرأة قابلة لجميع المال لا يقع الطلاق عند اتفاقهما على المواضعة. وإن اتفقا على أنه لم يحضرهما شيء وقع الطلاق ووجب المال اتفاقًا، أما عندهما فظاهر أي من البناء والأعراض مما مرّ، بل هذا أولى مما مرّ، وأما عنده فلرجحان جانب الجد، ولم يذكر ما إذا اتفقا أي المصنف على الأعراض أو اختلفا فيه؛ لأن حكم الأول ظاهر بالطريق الأولى، وحكم الثاني أن أي في الأعراض يكون القول قول من يدعى الأعراض، اتفقا أي اتفقا على أنا قائمان على ما واضعنا قبل. (المحشي) لا يؤثر في الخلع إلخ: لحديث ذكر سابقا، مفاده: أن الطلاق من الأشياء التي يكون هزلها جدا، والخلع أيضًا طلاق، فيكون هزله أيضًا جدا. (السنبلي) تابع فلا يؤثر الهزل ههنا في المال أيضًا، فيجب المسمّى (القمر) لا يلزم إلخ حتى لا يؤثر الهزل في التابع أي المال كما لا يؤثر في الأصل أي الخلع. (القمر) مقصود المتعاقدين: فإن مقصود المتعاقدين في النكاح هو الحل والتناسل لا المال. (القمر) يجب أن يتعلق الطلاق إلخ لأن الطلاق مشروط بالمال، ولا يلزم المال إلا برضاء المرأة. (القمر) مما مر من أن الهزل لا يؤثر في الخلع. (القمر) بل هذا أولى لعدم حضور شيء، فالعبرة للعبارة حينئذ. (القمر) على الأعراض أي عن المواضعة السابقة أو اختلفا فيه بأن قال أحد بالبناء على المواضعة، وقال الآخر بالأعراض عنها. (القمر) ظاهر : وهو لزوم الطلاق والمال كله لجدهما. (القمر)

بيان الأهلية ٢٠٢
تعريف الهزل وشرطه
أما عنده فلما تقدّم، وأما عندهما فلبطلانه، هكذا قيل.
وإن كان في الجنس بأن تواضعا على أن يذكرا في العقد مائة دينار، ويكون البدل فيما أي الهزل بينهما مائة درهم يجب المسمى عندهما بكل حال، سواء اتفقا على الأعراض أو على وهو غير جنس الدينار البناء، أو على أن لم يحضر هما شيء، أو اختلفا لبطلان الهزل في الخلع والمال يجب تبعًا.
وعنده إن اتفقا على الأعراض وجب المسمى لبطلان الهزل بالأعراض، عن المواضعة وإن اتفقا على البناء توقف الطلاق على قبولها المسمي؛ لأنه هو الشرط في العقد، أي القبول وإن اتفقا على أنه لم يحضر هما شيء وجب المسمّى، ووقع الطلاق؛ لرجحان جانب الجد.
وإن اختلفا فالقول لمدعى الأعراض؛ لكونه هو الأصل، وهذا كله في الإنشاءات. وإن كان ذلك أي الهزل في الإقرار بما يحتمل الفسخ كالبيع بأن يواضعا على أن يُقرا بالبيع بحضور الناس، ولم يكن في الواقع إقرار، وبما لا يحتمله كالنكاح والطلاق بأن يواضعا على
فلما تقدم من أن الترجيح للجد ومدعي الأعراض عن المواضعة السابقة جادّ فله الترجيح، وعند الصاحبين الهزل باطل؛ لأنه لا يؤثر في الخلع، فإن هزل فيه أحد يكون هزله جدا وبطل هزله. (السنبلي) فلبطلانه أي الهزل، فإن الهزل لا يؤثر في الخلع. (القمر) على الأعراض أي عن المواضعة السابقة، أو على البناء أي على تلك المواضعة، أو على أن لم يحضر هما شيء أي من البناء والأعراض، أو اختلفا بأن قال أحد بالأعراض والآخر بالبناء. (القمر) شيء أي من البناء على المواضعة والأعراض عنها. (القمر) لمدعي الأعراض: اعتبارا للجد، وذكر في "المبسوط" أن الطلاق يقع ويجب المسمى بكل حال من غير ذكر خلاف، واعلم أن مثل ثبوت الحكم والتفريع في الخلع ثبوت الحكم، والتفريع في نظائره من الإعتاق على مال والصلح عن دم عمد، ولم يذكر المصنف ليه تسليم الشفعة هزلا وحكم أنه قبل طلب المواثبة كالسكوت يبطلها وبعده يبطل التسليم فتبقى الشفعة؛ لأنه من جنس ما يبطل الخيار ؛ لأنه في معنى التجارة لكونه استيفاء أحد العوضين على ملكه فيتوقف على الرضاء بالحكم، والهزل بنفيه، ولم يذكر إبراء المديون والكفيل هزلاً، وحكمه أنه يبطل به؛ لأن فيه معنى التمليك ويرتدّ بالردّ فيؤثر فيه الهزل، فيبقى الدين على حاله، ولذا قال: أبرأتك على أني "بالخيار" لا يسقط كذا ذكره فخر الإسلام له وصاحب "الكشف"، "فتح الغفار". (السنبلي) لكونه هو الأصل فإن جانب الجد مرجح. (القمر)
Statement of legal capacity. Definition of jest and its condition. If they both agree on building, i.e., building upon the prior agreement after the session, then according to the two companions divorce occurs, and the dower is due after the entire session disperses; because it has passed that jest does not affect khul' according to them, even if it affects the dower, but the dower is subsidiary. And it is not said: how can the dower be subsidiary when it was stated previously that the dower is intended in khul'? Even if it is granted that the dower is subsidiary, it is not necessary that its ruling be the same as the principal, like in marriage; for in khul' the dower is subsidiary, and jest affects it even though it does not affect marriage; because we say: the dower in khul', though intended by the contracting parties, is subsidiary to divorce in terms of establishment; and the dower in marriage, though subsidiary relative to the intended purpose of the parties, is a principal in establishment since it is established without mention. According to him [Abu Hanifa], divorce must be tied to her acceptance; so if the woman is not capable of accepting all the dower, divorce does not occur when they agree on the prior understanding. If they agree that nothing was present (no prior understanding), divorce occurs and the dower is due by consensus. As for them [the two companions], it is apparent from what has passed; indeed this is more obvious; and as for him [Abu Hanifa], due to the preponderance of seriousness. He [the author] did not mention if they agree on turning away or disagree; because the ruling of the first is apparent by priority, and the ruling of the second is that in case of turning away, the statement of the one claiming turning away is taken. They agreed that we are standing on what we agreed before. (al-Muhashshi) 'Does not affect khul' etc.' Because of a hadith mentioned earlier, indicating that divorce is among things where jest is serious, and khul' is also divorce, so its jest is also serious. (al-Sanbali) Subsidiary, so jest here does not affect the dower either, so the named dower is due. (al-Qamar) 'Not necessary' etc. so that jest does not affect the subsidiary, i.e., the dower, just as it does not affect the principal, i.e., khul'. (al-Qamar) Intended purpose of the contracting parties: the intended purpose in marriage is permissibility and procreation, not the dower. (al-Qamar) 'Must be tied to divorce' etc. because divorce is conditioned on the dower, and the dower is not binding except with the woman's consent. (al-Qamar) From what passed that jest does not affect khul'. (al-Qamar) 'Rather this is more obvious' due to nothing being present, so the consideration is for the statement then. (al-Qamar) 'On turning away' i.e., from the prior agreement, or they differed in that one said building on the prior understanding and the other said turning away from it. (al-Qamar) 'Apparent': meaning the occurrence of divorce and the entire dower due for both of them. (al-Qamar)

Statement of legal capacity 202. Definition of jest and its condition. As for him [Abu Hanifa], due to what preceded; as for them [the two companions], due to its invalidity, thus it is said. And if it is in the same type, such that they agree to mention in the contract one hundred dinars, but the substitute is one hundred dirhams, then the named dower is due according to them in all cases, whether they agree on turning away or on building, or that nothing was present, or they differ, due to the invalidity of jest in khul' and the dower follows. According to him [Abu Hanifa], if they agree on turning away, the named dower is due due to the invalidity of jest through turning away; if they agree on building, the divorce is suspended on her acceptance of the named dower because it is the condition in the contract; if they agree that nothing was present, the named dower is due and divorce occurs due to the preponderance of seriousness. If they differ, the statement of the one claiming turning away is taken because it is the default. All this is in creations (direct contracts). And if that (jest) occurs in acknowledgment that can be rescinded, like sale, such that they agree to make a false acknowledgment of sale in front of people while no real acknowledgment exists, and in what cannot be rescinded like marriage and divorce, such that they agree... Then due to what preceded that the preponderance is for seriousness and the claimant of turning away from the prior agreement is serious, so he has the preponderance. According to the two companions, jest is invalid because it does not affect khul', for if one jest in it, his jest becomes serious and his jest is void. (al-Sanbali) 'Due to its invalidity' i.e., of jest, for jest does not affect khul'. (al-Qamar) 'On turning away' i.e., from the prior agreement, or 'on building' i.e., on that prior agreement, or 'that nothing was present' i.e., of building and turning away, or they differed such that one said turning away and the other building. (al-Qamar) 'Something' i.e., of building on the prior agreement and turning away from it. (al-Qamar) 'For the claimant of turning away': considering seriousness; it is mentioned in al-Mabsut that divorce occurs and the named dower is due in all cases without mentioning a difference. Know that the establishment of the ruling and its branches in khul' is parallel to the establishment of the ruling and its branches in its analogues: manumission for property and settlement for intentional homicide blood money. The author did not mention handing over preemption in jest and its ruling: that before demand for immediate payment it is like silence and voids it, and after demand it voids the handing over so the preemption remains; because it is of the type that voids options; because it is in the meaning of trade, being the taking of one of the two compensations on one's property, so it depends on consent to the ruling, and jest negates that. He did not mention acquittal of the debtor and the guarantor in jest, and its ruling: that it is voided by it; because it has the meaning of ownership and is revocable by repudiation, so jest affects it, and the debt remains as it was. Hence he said: I acquit you on condition that I have the option – it is not dropped. Thus mentioned by Fakhr al-Islam and the author of al-Kashf and Fath al-Ghaffar. (al-Sanbali) 'Because it is the default' – for the side of seriousness is preponderant. (al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the effect of jest (hazl) in legal transactions, focusing on khul' (divorce for compensation). It opens by defining the condition of jest, then details scenarios under which the rulings differ between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two companions, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. According to the two companions, jest does not affect khul' at all: the divorce is valid and the named dower is due, because a hadith states that divorce is among things where jest is considered serious. This principle extends to khul' as a type of divorce. The dower is subsidiary to the divorce, so jest also does not affect it. In contrast, Abu Hanifa holds that if the parties jest, the divorce is suspended upon the wife's acceptance of the full dower; if she does not accept, the divorce does not occur. The text then addresses cases where the parties agree on a different type of dower (e.g., dinars but agree on dirhams), and similar distinctions apply. Finally, the passage extends the discussion to jest in acknowledgments (iqrar) for transactions that can be rescinded (like sale) and those that cannot (like marriage and divorce), with marginal notes clarifying the positions and citing sources like al-Mabsut. The key takeaway for a Hanafi student is that jest does not automatically void all contracts; its effect depends on the nature of the transaction and the madhhab's hierarchy of principles.

Key Terms
الهزل (al-hazl): Jest or playful speech that is not meant seriously
البناء (al-binā'): Building upon a prior agreement or understanding (al-muwāḍa‘a)
الأعراض (al-a‘rāḍ): Turning away from or abandoning the prior agreement

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), if a husband and wife jest in the khul' contract, what is the ruling?
A) The divorce does not occur and no dower is due.
B) The divorce occurs and the named dower is due.
C) The divorce occurs but no dower is due.
D) The divorce is suspended upon her acceptance of the dower.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, jest in irrevocable contracts like divorce and khul' is treated as serious due to the hadith, making the contract valid and the dower due.

Definition and Rulings of Jest (Hazl) in Hanafi Law
Defines hazl and its conditions, and explains its effects across contracts, acknowledgments, and apostasy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define hazl, state its essential condition (mutawadi'a), and apply its legal effects to different contexts (khul', iqrar, apostasy) while distinguishing between the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Jest in legal acts is generally invalid; only explicit prior agreement to jest overrides the presumption of seriousness.

This lesson dives into the Hanafi legal concept of hazl (jest) — statements or acts made without the intention of their legal consequences. The passage distinguishes between situations where jest is effective (i.e., it voids the act) and where it is disregarded, placing a strong presumption on seriousness (jidd). Understanding this distinction is key to correctly applying rulings in contracts, acknowledgments, and even apostasy.

Guided Path
1
Define hazl and its condition
Start by extracting the definition from the passage: hazl is saying or doing something without intending its legal consequences, but its effect depends on prior agreement (mutawadi'a) between the parties.
The condition for hazl to be considered is that both parties agree to act in jest; otherwise, seriousness is presumed.
2
Analyze the ikhtilaf in khul'
Work through the scenarios in the passage where the parties agree to a different amount in a khul' contract. Note the difference: Abu Hanifa allows the possibility of jest depending on their post-agreement, while the Sahibayn hold that jest in khul' is always invalid and the named amount is due.
The thamarah al-khilaf is: does the divorce occur and property become due? According to Sahibayn, always yes; according to Abu Hanifa, it depends.
3
Apply to acknowledgments (iqrar)
Distinguish between iqrar of what can be rescinded (like sale) and what cannot (marriage, divorce). The passage rules that hazl invalidates iqrar in both cases because iqrar inherently admits to a fact, and if the fact is false, the acknowledgment is void.
Key principle: iqrar is probative; hazl cannot make a false claim true.
4
Examine the unique ruling on apostasy
Read the Quranic proof (9:65-66) and the commentary: hazl in apostasy is itself disbelief because it constitutes mockery of religion, regardless of inner belief. This is an exception where the act itself, not the intent, determines the ruling.
The dalil is a direct Quranic verse with qati' thubut and dalala.
5
Extend to other cases (shuf'a, ibra) and conclude
The passage analogizes to transfer of pre-emption rights and release of debt. In both, hazl invalidates the act, reinforcing the general rule that jest does not produce legal effects unless the law presumes seriousness.
This step solidifies the overall principle: hazl is exceptional, and the default is jidd.

Source Text

تعريف الهزل وشرطه
أما عنده فلما تقدّم، وأما عندهما فلبطلانه، هكذا قيل.
وإن كان في الجنس بأن تواضعا على أن يذكرا في العقد مائة دينار، ويكون البدل فيما أي الهزل بينهما مائة درهم يجب المسمى عندهما بكل حال، سواء اتفقا على الأعراض أو على البناء، أو على أن لم يحضر هما شيء، أو اختلفا لبطلان الهزل في الخلع والمال يجب تبعًا.
وعنده إن اتفقا على الأعراض وجب المسمى لبطلان الهزل بالأعراض، عن المواضعة وإن اتفقا على البناء توقف الطلاق على قبولها المسمي؛ لأنه هو الشرط في العقد، أي القبول وإن اتفقا على أنه لم يحضر هما شيء وجب المسمّى، وقع الطلاق؛ لرجحان جانب الجد.
وإن اختلفا فالقول لمدعى الأعراض؛ لكونه هو الأصل، وهذا كله في الإنشاءات. وإن كان ذلك أي الهزل في الإقرار بما يحتمل الفسخ كالبيع بأن يواضعا على أن يُقرا بالبيع بحضور الناس، ولم يكن في الواقع إقرار، وبما لا يحتمله كالنكاح والطلاق بأن يواضعا على أن يُقرا بالنكاح والطلاق بحضور العامة ولم يكن بينهما إقرار، فالهزل يبطله؛ لأن الإقرار محتمل للصدق والكذب، والمخبر عنه إذا كان باطلاً فالإخبار به كيف يصير حقا.
والهزل في الردّة كفر، أي إذا تلفظ بألفاظ الكفر هزلا يصير كافرا، ويرد عليه أنه كيف يكون كافرًا مع أنه لم يعتقد به؟ فأجاب بقوله: لا بما هزل به أي ليس كفره بلفظ هزل به من غير اعتقاد، لكن بعين الهزل؛ لكونه استخفافًا بالدين، وهو كفر؛ لقوله تعالى: قلْ أَبِاللَّهِ وَآيَاتِهِ وَرَسُولِهِ كُنتُمْ تَسْتَهْزِئُونَ لَا تَعْتَذِرُوا قَدْ كَفَرْتُمْ بَعْدَ إِيمَانِكُمْ . (التوبة: ٦٦٦٥)
فالهزل يبطله وكذلك تسليم الشفعة بعد الطلب والإشهاد يبطله الهزل؛ لأنه عن جنس ما يبطل بخيار الشرط، وكذلك إبراء الغريم بطريق الهزل يبطله الهزل حتى لو أبرأ غريما بطريق الهزل يبقى الدين على حاله. (السنبلي) إذا كان باطلاً لأن الهزل يدل على بطلان المخبر عنه فإن الهازل يُظهر عند الناس خلاف ما هو في الواقع. (القمر) والهزل: هذا قسم ثالث فيما يتعلّق بالاعتقاد لم يعتقد به ومبنى الردّة على تبدل الاعتقاد.(القمر) لا بما هزل به فإنه لا اعتقاد لمفهوم ما هزل .به (القمر) وهو أي الاستخفاف بالدين كفر سواء حصل الاعتقاد بما هزل به أو لم يحصل. (القمر) قل يا محمد للمنافقين أبالله وآياته ورسوله كنتم تستهزئون، لا تعتذروا، أي لا تقولوا العذر فيما استهزأتم به قد كفرتم أي أظهرتم الكفر بعد إيمانكم، أي بعد الإيمان اللساني. (القمر)
Statement of legal capacity. Definition of jest and its condition. As for him (Abu Hanifa) due to what preceded, and as for them (the two disciples) because it is invalid, thus it is said. And if it is in the genus such that they agree to mention in the contract one hundred dinars, but the substitute between them is one hundred dirhams (which is not of the same genus as the dinar), the named amount is obligatory according to both of them in every case, whether they agree on turning away (from the prior agreement) or on building (upon it), or on that nothing is present between them, or they differ, because jest is invalid in khul' and the property follows. And according to him (Abu Hanifa) if they agree on turning away, the named amount is obligatory because jest is invalid upon turning away from the prior agreement. And if they agree on building, the divorce is suspended upon her acceptance of the named amount because it is the condition in the contract, i.e., acceptance. And if they agree that nothing is present between them, the named amount is obligatory and divorce occurs due to the preponderance of the side of seriousness. And if they differ, the word is of the claimant of turning away because it is the original. And all this is in creations (contracts). And if jest is in acknowledgment of what can be rescinded like sale, such that they agree to acknowledge a sale in the presence of people while in reality there is no acknowledgment, and what cannot be like marriage and divorce, such that they agree to acknowledge marriage and divorce in the presence of the public while there is no acknowledgment between them, then jest invalidates it because the acknowledgment is susceptible to truth and falsehood, and if the thing informed about is invalid, how can the informing become valid? And jest in apostasy is disbelief, i.e., if one utters words of disbelief jestingly, he becomes an unbeliever. It is objected that how can he be an unbeliever when he does not believe in it? He answered: not by what he jested with, i.e., his disbelief is not by the utterance of jest without belief, but by the act of jest itself because it is mockery of the religion, and that is disbelief due to His saying: Say, 'Is it Allah and His verses and His Messenger that you were mocking?' Make no excuse; you have disbelieved after your belief. (At-Tawbah: 65-66). So jest invalidates it, and likewise the transfer of shuf'a after request and witnessing, jest invalidates it because it is of the kind that is invalidated by the option of condition, and likewise the release of a debtor by way of jest, jest invalidates it so that if one releases a debtor by way of jest, the debt remains as it was. (Al-Sunbuli) Because it is invalid, for jest indicates the invalidity of the thing informed about, since the jester shows to people the opposite of what is in reality. (Al-Qamar) And jest: this is a third division regarding belief without believing in it, and the basis of apostasy is change of belief. (Al-Qamar) Not by what he jested with, for there is no belief in the meaning of what he jested with. (Al-Qamar) And it, i.e., mockery of the religion, is disbelief whether belief in what was jested with occurs or not. (Al-Qamar) Say, O Muhammad, to the hypocrites: 'Is it Allah and His verses and His Messenger that you were mocking? Do not make excuses; you have disbelieved after your faith,' i.e., after verbal faith. (Al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage is a ruling defining jest (hazl) and its legal effect in various contracts and acknowledgments according to Hanafi law. The text presents the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani). The author first describes a scenario where parties agree to state a different amount (e.g., 100 dinars in the contract but 100 dirhams as the actual substitute). According to the two disciples, the named amount is obligatory in all cases because jest is invalid in khul' (divorce for compensation). Abu Hanifa distinguishes: if they agree to disregard the prior jest, the named amount is due; if they build on the jest, divorce is suspended on acceptance; if they have no prior agreement, the named amount is due and divorce occurs immediately due to the presumption of seriousness. In cases of dispute, the one claiming seriousness (turning away) is believed. For acknowledgments (iqrar) that can be rescinded (like sale), jest invalidates them because acknowledgment is inherently ambiguous. For acknowledgments that cannot be rescinded (like marriage and divorce), jest also invalidates. A special ruling: jest in apostasy (uttering words of disbelief jokingly) constitutes actual disbelief because it is mockery of religion, supported by Quran 9:65-66. The text concludes by analogizing to transfer of pre-emption rights and release of debts, where jest invalidates the action.

Key Terms
الهزل (al-hazl): Jest or joking; saying or doing something without intending its legal consequences
الجد (al-jidd): Seriousness; the opposite of jest, presumed in legal acts
الخلع (al-khul'): Divorce initiated by the wife with compensation to the husband

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), what is the ruling on jest in the context of khul' (divorce for compensation)?
A) Jest invalidates the khul' only if both parties agree to jest
B) Jest is invalid in khul'; any jest therein is treated as serious and the khul' takes effect
C) Jest is always effective and no divorce occurs
D) Khul' is not affected by jest because it is a contract

Key Takeaway
Jest (hazl) is generally invalid in shar'i acts, but the presumption of seriousness (jidd) prevails unless both parties explicitly agree to jest; in matters of apostasy, hazl itself constitutes disbelief.

Definition and Ruling of Foolishness (Safah)
Defines safah and explains it as an acquired disqualifier

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to DEFINE safah in Hanafi legal terminology and IDENTIFY the elements that constitute safah as an acquired disqualifier.

Core Idea
Safah is acting against the Law through wasteful spending, even in good deeds.

Safah (foolishness) is a legal disqualifier in Hanafi law that can lead to interdiction from managing one's wealth. In this lesson, we unpack its precise technical definition as given by the author of Noor al-Anwar, distinguishing it from the broader linguistic meaning and clarifying its scope: it applies to extravagance and waste, even when the basic act (like spending money) is permissible. Understanding this definition is essential for correctly applying rules of legal capacity (ahliyyah).

Guided Path
1
Distinguish linguistic vs technical meaning
Note that 'safah' linguistically means lightness, but technically it is 'acting contrary to the requirement of the Law through extravagance and waste.' Recognize that the technical meaning is narrower.
The passage states: 'in language lightness, and in terminology... acting contrary to the requirement of the Law.'
2
Identify the key phrase: 'even if its origin is permissible'
Understand that safah applies even to acts that are permissible in origin, like spending one's own money, if done excessively. This distinguishes it from sinful acts which are already prohibited.
The text says: 'even if its origin is permissible, and it is extravagance and waste.'
3
Recognize safah as an acquired disqualifier
Al-Sunbuli explains that safah is 'among acquired disqualifiers and is not congenital.' It arises from one's actions, not from birth.
This affects legal capacity: a person is not born a safih but becomes one through behavior.
4
Apply the definition to examples
Consider the example from al-Durr al-Mukhtar: spending on building mosques excessively can be safah if it contradicts the proper dictates of the Law or reason.
The passage warns that even virtuous spending can be safah if it is wasteful or against reason.
5
Exclude irrelevant actions
Note that the technical definition here focuses on financial matters, not on committing sins like adultery or drinking wine, which fall under a different category.
The text explicitly says: 'the latter meaning... includes committing prohibitions... but it is not discussed in this context.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تعريف السفه وحكمه
والسفه، عطف على ما قبله وهو في اللغة الخفة وفي الاصطلاح ما عرفه المصنف اليه أي قوله: الجهل أي خفة العقل بقوله : وهو العمل بخلاف موجب الشرع وإن كان أصله مشروعًا، وهو السرف والتبذير، أي تجاوز الحد وتفريق المال إسرافًا.
(السنبلي) العمل إلخ فيكون السفه من العوارض المكتسبة ولا يكون سماويًا، والمعنى الأخير وإن كان مناسبا للمعنى اللغوي، ولكنه يشمل ارتكاب المحرمات كالزنا وشرب الخمر وهو وإن كان سفهًا، ولكنه غير مبحوث في هذا المقام، والمعنى الأول يناسب المقام وإن لم يناسب المعنى اللغوي.
وإن كان أصله أي أصل ذلك العمل مشروعًا. وهو السرف إلخ فصرف المال مشروع بأصله؛ لأنه تصرف في ماله لكنه لما وصل إلى أحد الصرف يكون خلاف موجب الشرع، وفي الدر المختار": السفه تبذير المال وتضييعه على خلاف مقتضى الشرع أو العقل ورد ولو في الخير كأن يصرفه في بناء المساجد ونحو ذلك.(القمر)
Definition of foolishness and its ruling. And foolishness (safah) is a conjunction to what preceded, and it is in language lightness, and in terminology what the author defined as: ignorance, i.e., lightness of intellect, by his saying: It is acting contrary to the requirement of the Law, even if its origin is permissible, and it is extravagance and waste, i.e., exceeding the limit and dispersing wealth wastefully. (Al-Sunbuli) The action etc., thus safah is among acquired disqualifiers and is not congenital, and the latter meaning although suitable for the linguistic meaning, but it includes committing prohibitions like adultery and drinking wine, and although that is foolishness, it is not discussed in this context, and the first meaning suits the context although it does not suit the linguistic meaning. And even if its origin, i.e., the origin of that action, is permissible. And it is extravagance etc., so spending money is permissible in its origin because it is a disposition in one's own wealth, but when it reaches a certain type of spending it becomes contrary to the requirement of the Law, and in al-Durr al-Mukhtar: Safah is squandering and wasting wealth contrary to the dictates of the Law or reason, even if in good deeds such as spending it on building mosques and the like. (Al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage defines safah (foolishness/judiciousness) in Hanafi legal terminology. Linguistically, safah means lightness or levity. Technically, the author defines it as acting contrary to what the Law requires, even if the action itself is permissible in origin, specifically through extravagance (israf) and waste (tabdhir) — exceeding limits and dispersing wealth wastefully. The commentary by al-Sunbuli clarifies that safah is an acquired disqualifier ('arid muktasab) meaning it is not congenital but arises from one's actions. While a broader definition could include committing sins like adultery, the focus here is on financial foolishness. The text then emphasizes that even if the basic act (like spending money) is permissible, if it reaches the level of extravagance, it becomes legally prohibited. Al-Qamar quotes from al-Durr al-Mukhtar that safah includes wasting wealth even in good causes like building mosques, if it is against the proper dictates of the Law or reason.

Key Terms
السفه (as-safah): Foolishness in legal terminology: acting contrary to the requirement of the Law through extravagance and waste
السرف (al-israf): Extravagance; exceeding proper limits in spending
التبذير (at-tabdhir): Waste; squandering wealth in a manner contrary to the Law or reason

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following best describes safah in Hanafi terminology?
A) Acting contrary to the Law only in sinful acts like drinking wine.
B) Acting contrary to the Law through extravagance and waste, even if the act is permissible in origin.
C) Being ignorant of the Law entirely.
D) Spending less than required, such as miserliness.

Key Takeaway
Safah is an acquired disqualifier defined as acting against the Law through wasteful spending, even in permissible acts, and can lead to interdiction.

The Legal Effect of Hazl (Jest) on Contracts and Apostasy
Defining hazl and its ruling on nikkah, talaq, shufa, ibra, and riddah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that hazl (jest) invalidates serious legal acts and identify the Quranic proof for hazl being kufr in apostasy.

Core Idea
Hazl invalidates contracts requiring serious intent and constitutes kufr because mockery of religion is disbelief.

The passage you are about to study addresses a critical distinction in Hanafi usul: when does jest (hazl) affect legal rulings? While playful speech may seem harmless, Islamic law treats hazl as undermining the seriousness required for certain acts. This lesson explores how hazl invalidates contracts like marriage, divorce, pre-emption, and debt discharge, and explains why even joking about Islam triggers apostasy. You will also examine the Quranic proof that mocks the hypocrites.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal definition of hazl
From the commentary, hazl is saying or doing something contrary to your real intent, as a joke. Note that it is distinct from outright lying because the speaker intends no serious effect.
Hazl is not mere fun; it is a deliberate contradiction between outward expression and inner intent.
2
Apply hazl to specific legal acts
The passage lists nikkah, talaq, shufa (pre-emption), and ibra (discharge) as acts invalidated by hazl. For each, ask: What serious intent does this act require? How does hazl negate that?
For ibra, hazl leaves the debt intact; for shufa, it voids the right.
3
Examine the case of apostasy (riddah)
The passage states that uttering words of kufr as a jest makes one a disbeliever. This is because the act of mocking religion is itself kufr, regardless of inner belief.
The key is that the jest is an act of contempt (istikhfaf), not merely words.
4
Analyze the Quranic support
The verse from Surah at-Tawbah (9:65-66) is cited. Identify how it proves that mockery of Allah, His verses, and His Messenger is kufr. Note that the verse addresses hypocrites who joked while claiming belief.
The dalala of the verse is qati because it directly equates mockery with kufr.
5
Resolve the objection about belief
The passage anticipates an objection: 'How can hazl cause kufr if one does not believe the words?' The answer: disbelief is due to the act of hazl itself (mockery), not belief in the content. Distinguish between the two.
This is a crucial usul point: the ruling attaches to the outward act, not hidden intention.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أن يُقرا بالنكاح والطلاق بحضور العامة و لم يكن بينهما إقرار، فالهزل يبطله؛ لأن الإقرار محتمل للصدق والكذب، والمخبر عنه إذا كان باطلاً فالإخبار به كيف يصير حقا. والهزل في الردّة كفر ، أي إذا تلفظ بألفاظ الكفر هزلا يصير كافرا، ويرد عليه أنه كيف يكون كافرًا مع أنه لم يعتقد به؟ فأجاب بقوله : لا بما هزل به أي ليس كفره بلفظ هزل به من غير اعتقاد، لكن بعين الهزل؛ لكونه استخفافًا بالدين، وهو كفر؛ لقوله تعالى: قلْ أَبِاللَّهِ وَآيَاتِهِ وَرَسُولِهِ كُنتُمْ تَسْتَهْزِئُونَ لَا تَعْتَذِرُوا قَدْ كَفَرْتُمْ بَعْدَ إِيمَانِكُمْ . فالهزل يبطله وكذلك تسليم الشفعة بعد الطلب والإشهاد يبطله الهزل؛ لأنه عن جنس ما يبطل بخيار الشرط، وكذلك إبراء الغريم بطريق الهزل يبطله الهزل حتى لو أبرأ غريما بطريق الهزل يبقى الدين على حاله. (السنبلي) إذا كان باطلاً لأن الهزل يدل على بطلان المخبر عنه فإن الهازل يُظهر عند الناس خلاف ما هو في الواقع. (القمر) والهزل: هذا قسم ثالث فيما يتعلّق بالاعتقاد لم يعتقد به ومبنى الردّة على تبدل الاعتقاد.(القمر) لا بما هزل به فإنه لا اعتقاد لمفهوم ما هزل .به (القمر) وهو أي الاستخفاف بالدين كفر سواء حصل الاعتقاد بما هزل به أو لم يحصل. (القمر) قل يا محمد للمنافقين أبالله وآياته ورسوله كنتم تستهزئون، لا تعتذروا، أي لا تقولوا العذر فيما استهزأتم به قد كفرتم أي أظهرتم الكفر بعد إيمانكم، أي بعد الإيمان اللساني. (القمر)
That a marriage and divorce are read in the presence of the public and there is no acknowledgment between them, so jest invalidates it; because acknowledgment is probable of truth and falsehood, and if the reported matter is false, how can reporting it become true? And jest in apostasy is disbelief: if one utters words of disbelief jokingly, he becomes a disbeliever, and it is objected: how can he be a disbeliever while he did not believe it? He answered: not because of what he jested about, i.e., his disbelief is not due to a word of jest without belief, but because of the very jest; because it is mockery of religion, and that is disbelief; due to His statement: Say: Is it Allah and His verses and His Messenger that you were mocking? Make no excuse; you have disbelieved after your belief. Then jest invalidates it, and likewise handing over pre-emption after demand and witnessing is invalidated by jest; because it is of the same type as what is invalidated by option of stipulation; and likewise discharging a debtor by way of jest is invalidated by jest, so if he discharged a debtor by way of jest, the debt remains as it was. (al-Sanbali) Because it is false, as jest indicates the falsity of the reported matter, because the jester shows to people contrary to what is real. (al-Qamar) And hazl: this is a third category regarding belief: he does not believe in it, and apostasy is built on change of belief. (al-Qamar) Not because of what he jested about, for there is no belief in the concept of what he jested about. (al-Qamar) And it, i.e., mockery of religion, is disbelief whether he obtains belief in what he jested about or not. (al-Qamar) Say, O Muhammad, to the hypocrites: Is it Allah and His verses and His Messenger that you were mocking? Make no excuse, meaning do not offer an excuse for what you mocked, you have disbelieved, meaning you have manifested disbelief after your belief, i.e., after verbal belief. (al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage defines the legal concept of hazl (jest) and its effects. The passage begins by stating that jest invalidates declarations of nikkah and talaq when made in public without any acknowledgment between the parties. The reasoning is that acknowledgment (iqrar) is inherently ambiguous, capable of truth or falsehood; if the underlying matter is false, the acknowledgment cannot make it true. The passage then addresses hazl in the context of apostasy (riddah). Even if one utters words of kufr jokingly without belief, he becomes a disbeliever because the very act of jesting implies mockery of Islam, which is itself kufr. This is supported by the Quranic verse concerning the hypocrites who mocked the Prophet (Quran 9:65-66). The passage further extends the principle: hazl invalidates legal acts such as the exercise of pre-emption (shuf'a) after demand and witnessing, and the discharge (ibra') of a debtor. Just as a conditional option (khiyar al-shart) can nullify a contract, hazl nullifies these acts because it demonstrates a lack of serious intent. The commentary by al-Sanbali and al-Qamar emphasizes that hazl reveals the falsity of the reported matter, as the jester displays the opposite of reality. In apostasy, hazl is considered a third category of disbelief: one may not believe the words, but the act of jesting itself is disbelief due to its mockery of the divine. The ruling is consistent with the Hanafi principle that apostasy is based on a change of belief (tabaddul al-i'tiqad), and here the manifestation of contempt suffices.

Key Terms
الهزل (al-hazl): Saying or doing something contrary to one's real intent, as a joke, without serious purpose.
الردة (al-riddah): Renunciation of Islam by word or deed, including jesting about religion.
استخفاف (istikhfaf): Contempt or mockery, treating something as insignificant.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does hazl invalidate a divorce pronounced in public without acknowledgment?
A) Because the spouses did not intend divorce.
B) Because the acknowledgment is ambiguous and the jest shows the reported matter is false.
C) Because public divorce is invalid anyway.
D) Because hazl always invalidates any statement.

Key Takeaway
Hazl (jest) destroys the serious intent required for valid legal acts and, in cases of apostasy, is itself kufr because it is mockery of religion.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

Safah: Definition, Legal Effect, and Internal Hanafi Dispute
Defining safah, its effect on legal capacity, and the internal Hanafi dispute on age of returning wealth.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define safah according to the Hanafi school, identify its effect on legal capacity, and compare the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on returning wealth to a safih.

Core Idea
Safah withholds wealth but not duties; the dispute on returning wealth hinges on condition (rashd) vs. age limit (25).

In this passage, the author first defines safah as an acquired impediment involving extravagance in financial matters, even if the act is permissible in origin. He then clarifies that safah does not affect one's capacity for religious obligations (ahliyyah al-ada'), but it does prevent the safih from controlling his wealth. The core of the lesson is the internal Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa sets a maximum age of 25 for returning wealth based on qiyas, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) insist on the explicit condition of rashd (discernment) from Quran 4:6. The relied-upon opinion (mufta bihi) is that of the Sahibayn.

Guided Path
1
Define safah
Identify the definition from the passage: 'acting contrary to shariah in financial matters through extravagance and waste, even if the action is based on a permissible origin.' Note that it is an acquired impediment (arid muktasab), not congenital.
The passage distinguishes financial safah from general sins; only financial mismanagement is relevant here.
2
Understand the effect on legal capacity
The text states that safah does not cause a defect in ahliyyah (legal capacity) for performing duties (ahliyyat al-wujub and ahliyyat al-ada'). The safih is still obligated to pray, fast, etc., but his wealth is withheld by a guardian.
This is a key Hanafi principle: withholding wealth does not imply loss of religious capacity.
3
Examine the Quranic proof
The passage cites Quran 4:5-6. There are two interpretations of 'your wealth' in 4:5. The relevant interpretation (second) is that it refers to the safih's own wealth. Quran 4:6 then conditions the return of wealth on perceiving rashd from the safih.
The Sahibayn rely on this condition; Abu Hanifa uses qiyas to set a limit.
4
Trace the dispute
Abu Hanifa argues that by age 25 a person becomes a grandfather (12 years after puberty + two pregnancies), indicating maturity, so wealth should be returned then. The Sahibayn hold that the verse's condition (rashd) must be met regardless of age.
The thamarah al-khilaf: if a safih turns 25 without rashd, Abu Hanifa returns wealth; Sahibayn do not.
5
Note the mufta bihi
The text states 'wa alayhi al-fatwa' for the Sahibayn opinion. Therefore, the operative ruling is that wealth is returned only when rashd is observed, with no fixed age limit.
This is an internal Hanafi ikhtilaf that is resolved by tarjih in favor of the Sahibayn.

والسفه، عطف على ما قبله وهو في اللغة الخفة وفي الاصطلاح ما عرفه المصنف بقوله : وهو العمل بخلاف موجب الشرع وإن كان أصله مشروعًا، وهو السرف والتبذير، أي تجاوز الحد وتفريق المال إسرافًا. فالهزل يبطله وكذلك تسليم الشفعة بعد الطلب والإشهاد يبطله الهزل؛ لأنه عن جنس ما يبطل بخيار الشرط، وكذلك إبراء الغريم بطريق الهزل يبطله الهزل حتى لو أبرأ غريما بطريق الهزل يبقى الدين على حاله. (السنبلي) إذا كان باطلاً لأن الهزل يدل على بطلان المخبر عنه فإن الهازل يُظهر عند الناس خلاف ما هو في الواقع. (القمر) والهزل: هذا قسم ثالث فيما يتعلّق بالاعتقاد لم يعتقد به ومبنى الردّة على تبدل الاعتقاد.(القمر) لا بما هزل به فإنه لا اعتقاد لمفهوم ما هزل .به (القمر) وهو أي الاستخفاف بالدين كفر سواء حصل الاعتقاد بما هزل به أو لم يحصل. (القمر) قل يا محمد للمنافقين أبالله وآياته ورسوله كنتم تستهزئون، لا تعتذروا، أي لا تقولوا العذر فيما استهزأتم به قد كفرتم أي أظهرتم الكفر بعد إيمانكم، أي بعد الإيمان اللساني. (القمر) العمل إلخ فيكون السفه من العوارض المكتسبة ولا يكون سماويًا، والمعنى الأخير وإن كان مناسبا للمعنى اللغوي، ولكنه يشمل ارتكاب المحرمات كالزنا وشرب الخمر وهو وإن كان سفهًا، ولكنه غير مبحوث في هذا المقام، والمعنى الأول يناسب المقام وإن لم يناسب المعنى اللغوي. (السنبلي) وإن كان أصله أي أصل ذلك العمل مشروعًا. وهو السرف إلخ فصرف المال مشروع بأصله؛ لأنه تصرف في ماله لكنه لما وصل إلى أحد الصرف يكون خلاف موجب الشرع، وفي الدر المختار": السفه تبذير المال وتضييعه على خلاف مقتضى الشرع أو العقل ورد ولو في الخير كأن يصرفه في بناء المساجد ونحو ذلك.(القمر) وذلك لا يوجب خللا في الأهلية، ولا يمنع شيئا من أحكام الشرع من الوجوب له وعليه؛ فيكون مطالبًا بالأحكام كلها، ويمنع ماله عنه، أي مال السفيه عن السفيه في أول ما يبلغ إجماعاً بالنص، وهو قوله: ﴿وَلا تُؤْتُوا السُّفَهَاءَ أَمْوَالَكُمُ الَّتِي جَعَلَ اللَّهُ لَكُمْ قِيَاما﴾ وفي الآية (النساء: ٥) توجيهان: أحدهما أن تكون المعنى على ظاهره أي لا تؤتوا يا أيها الأولياء، السفهاء من الأزواج والأولاد أموالكم التي جعل الله لكم فيها قيامًا؛ لأنهم يضيّعونها بلا تدبير، ثم تحتاجون إليه لأجل نفقاتهم، ولا يؤتونكم، وحينئذ لا يكون الآية مما نحن فيه، والثاني: أن يكون معنى أموالكم أموالهم، وإنما أضيفت إليهم لأجل القيام بتدبيرها، وحينئذ يكون تمسكًا لما نحن فيه، أي لا تؤتوا السفهاء أموالهم التي جعل الله لكم فيها تدبيرها وقيامها. ويدلّ على هذا المعنى قوله فيما بعده: ﴿فَإِنْ آنَسْتُمْ مِنْهُمْ رُشْداً فَادْفَعُوا إِلَيْهِمْ أَمْوَالَهُمْ﴾ (النساء : ٦) ولهذا قال أبو يوسف ومحمد رحمهما: إنه لا يدفع إليه المال ما لم يؤنس منه الرشد لأجل هذه الآية، وقال أبو حنيفة رحمه الله: إذا بلغ خمسا وعشرين سنة يُدفع إليه المال وإن لم يؤنس منه الرشد؛ لأنه يصير المرء في هذه المدة جدًا؛ إذ وفى مدّة البلوغ اثنا عشر سنة، وأدنى مدة الحمل ستة أشهر، فيصير حينئذ أبا، وإذا ضوعف ذلك يصير جدًا، فلا يفيد منع المال بعده، وذلك: أي السفه لا يوجب خللاً في الأهلية أي أهلية الوجوب والأداء.(القمر) من الوجوب له أي لنفعه وعليه أي ضرراً عليه، فيكون مطالبًا إلخ لأنه مكلّف عاقل بالغ مختار (القمر) قيامًا أي تقومون بها، وتنتعشون، وهذا مؤول بأنها التي من جنس ما جعل الله لكم فيها قيامًا، وسمّي ما به القيام قيامًا للمبالغة، كذا قال البيضاوي. (القمر) مما نحن فيه أي منع مال السفيه عن السفيه. (القمر) فإن آنستم أي أبصرتم منهم أي من اليتامى رشدًا أي الصلاح في الدين والمال فادفعوا إليهم أموالهم. (القمر) لا يدفع إليه: أي إلى السفيه المال، وعليه الفتوى، كذا قال بحر العلوم مولانا عبد العلي له. (القمر) لأجل هذه الآية: فإن الدفع معلّق بالرشد، والمعلّق بالشرط لا يوجد قبله. (القمر) فلا يفيد منع المال: لأنه لما وصل إلى هذا الحد فقد انقطع عنه رجاء الشرط. (القمر)
And safah, connected to what preceded, is in language lightness, and in terminology what the author defined by his statement: it is acting contrary to the requirement of the law even if its origin is permissible, and it is extravagance and waste, i.e., exceeding the limit and dispersing wealth excessively. So jest invalidates it and likewise handing over pre-emption after demand and witnessing is invalidated by jest; because it is of the same type as what is invalidated by option of stipulation; and likewise discharging a debtor by way of jest is invalidated by jest, so if he discharged a debtor by way of jest, the debt remains as it was. (al-Sanbali) Because it is false, as jest indicates the falsity of the reported matter, because the jester shows to people contrary to what is real. (al-Qamar) And hazl: this is a third category regarding belief: he does not believe in it, and apostasy is built on change of belief. (al-Qamar) Not because of what he jested about, for there is no belief in the concept of what he jested about. (al-Qamar) And it, i.e., mockery of religion, is disbelief whether he obtains belief in what he jested about or not. (al-Qamar) Say, O Muhammad, to the hypocrites: Is it Allah and His verses and His Messenger that you were mocking? Make no excuse, meaning do not offer an excuse for what you mocked, you have disbelieved, meaning you have manifested disbelief after your belief, i.e., after verbal belief. (al-Qamar) The action, etc., so safah is among acquired impediments and is not congenital, and the latter meaning, although suitable to the linguistic meaning, includes committing prohibitions like zina and drinking wine, and although it is safah, it is not researched in this context, and the first meaning suits the context although not suitable to the linguistic meaning. (al-Sanbali) And although its origin, i.e., the origin of that action, is permissible. And it is extravagance, etc., so spending wealth is permissible in origin because it is disposal of his wealth, but when it reaches one of the two [types of] spending it becomes contrary to the requirement of the law. And in al-Durr al-Mukhtar: safah is wasting and squandering wealth contrary to the requirement of the law or reason, even if in good like spending on building mosques and the like. (al-Qamar) And that does not cause a defect in legal capacity, and does not prevent anything from the rulings of the law from obligation for him and upon him; so he is held accountable for all rulings, and his wealth is withheld from him, i.e., the wealth of the safih from the safih at the beginning of his attaining puberty by consensus based on the text, which is His statement: 'And do not give the foolish your wealth which Allah has made for you a support.' And in the verse (al-Nisa:5) there are two interpretations: one that the meaning is apparent: do not give, O guardians, the foolish among spouses and children your wealth which Allah has made for you a support, because they waste it without management, then you need it for their expenses, and they will not give you, and then the verse is not about what we are in; and the second: that the meaning of 'your wealth' is 'their wealth', but it was added to them because of the management of it, and then it is a support for what we are in, i.e., do not give the foolish their wealth which Allah has made for you management and support. And proof of this meaning is His statement thereafter: 'Then if you perceive from them discernment, then give them their wealth' (al-Nisa:6). And for this reason Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on them) said: wealth is not given to him until discernment is perceived from him because of this verse. And Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) said: when he reaches twenty-five years, wealth is given to him even if discernment is not perceived from him, because a person becomes a grandfather in this period; since the period of puberty is completed at twelve years, and the minimum duration of pregnancy is six months, then he becomes a father, and if that is doubled, he becomes a grandfather, so withholding wealth after that is not beneficial. And that: i.e., safah does not cause a defect in legal capacity, i.e., capacity for obligation and performance. (al-Qamar) From obligation for him i.e., for his benefit, and upon him i.e., harm upon him, so he is held accountable etc. because he is accountable, sane, adult, capable of choice. (al-Qamar) 'Support' meaning you stand with it and prosper, and it is interpreted as it is of the kind that Allah has made for you support in it, and what brings about support is called support for emphasis, as said by al-Baydawi. (al-Qamar) 'What we are in' meaning preventing the wealth of the safih from the safih. (al-Qamar) 'Then if you perceive' meaning see from them, i.e., the orphans, 'discernment' i.e., righteousness in religion and wealth, then give them their wealth. (al-Qamar) 'Wealth is not given to him' i.e., to the safih, and the fatwa is upon it, as said by Bahr al-Ulum Mawlana Abd al-Ali. (al-Qamar) 'Because of this verse': for payment is conditioned upon discernment, and what is conditioned upon a condition does not exist before it. (al-Qamar) 'So withholding wealth is not beneficial': because when he reaches this limit, hope for the condition is cut off. (al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage defines safah (foolishness in financial matters) and its legal consequences. It begins by quoting the definition: acting contrary to shari'ah even if the action's basis is permissible, specifically extravagance (sarf) and waste (tabdhir). The passage then repeats some rulings about hazl that were previously discussed. The commentary notes that safah is an acquired impediment (arid muktasab), not congenital, and it is limited to financial mismanagement, not general sins. The key ruling is that safah does not affect one's legal capacity (ahliyyah) for worship and obligations; a safih must still pray, fast, etc. However, his wealth is withheld from him by consensus based on Quran 4:5. The verse is interpreted in two ways: the first interpretation says the verse addresses guardians not to give their own wealth to foolish spouses/children (not relevant to safih's own wealth); the second interpretation says 'your wealth' means the wealth of the foolish themselves, and guardians should not give it to them until they show rashd (discernment). The second interpretation is supported by Quran 4:6. Based on this, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that wealth should never be given until rashd is observed. In contrast, Abu Hanifa sets a maximum age of 25, reasoning that by then one becomes a grandfather (12 years after puberty plus six-month pregnancy doubled), indicating maturity. After 25, withholding is pointless because hope for rashd is lost. The passage concludes that the relied-upon opinion (alayhi al-fatwa) is that of the two students (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad).

Key Terms
السفه (al-safah): Acting contrary to shariah in financial matters through extravagance and waste, even if the action is based on a permissible origin.
الرشد (al-rashd): Discernment and sound judgment in financial and religious matters; the condition for returning wealth to a safih.
الإجماع (al-ijma'): Consensus of the Companions or scholars that the wealth of a safih is withheld at puberty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, at what age does a safih regain control over his wealth even if rashd (discernment) is not observed?
A) 18 years
B) 20 years
C) 25 years
D) 30 years

Key Takeaway
Safah is an acquired impediment that restricts financial control but not religious duties; the relied-upon Hanafi opinion requires rashd (discernment) before returning wealth, not a fixed age limit.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

Safah and Legal Capacity: The Quranic Foundation
Defining safah and its Quranic proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of safah, explain its effect on ahliyyah, and apply the two interpretations of Quran 4:5-6 to derive the ruling on withholding wealth.

Core Idea
Safah does not destroy legal capacity; it only restricts property disposal to protect the foolish person and society.

Safah (foolishness/prodigality) is a condition that impacts a person's financial management but does not strip them of their fundamental legal capacity. This passage from Nur al-Anwar clarifies that a safih remains fully mukallaf, obligated to perform religious duties and subject to prohibitions. However, his wealth is withheld at the onset of puberty by consensus, based on the Quranic command in Surah al-Nisa. We will explore the definition of safah, its effect on ahliyyah, and the textual evidence from the Quran, including the interpretive disagreement that leads to different rulings on when the wealth may be released.

Guided Path
1
Define safah and its scope
Safah is the condition of wasteful behavior and lack of sound financial judgment. It does not affect the core of legal capacity (ahliyyah), meaning the safih is still accountable for religious obligations.
2
Explain the effect on ahliyyah
The passage states that safah does not cause a defect in ahliyyah; the safih has both capacity for obligation (wujub) and performance (ada). He is required to fulfill all rulings.
This means the safih must pray, fast, etc., and is subject to criminal liability.
3
Identify the consensus on withholding wealth
At the beginning of puberty, the guardian withholds the safih's wealth by consensus based on Quran 4:5: 'Do not give the foolish your wealth...'
The consensus is only on withholding at the start; disputes arise later.
4
Analyze the two interpretations of the verse
First interpretation: the verse addresses guardians about their own wealth (not directly relevant). Second interpretation: it means 'their wealth' (the foolish), making it a proof for withholding the safih's own wealth. The subsequent verse (4:6) supports this.
The second interpretation is the legally operative one in this context.
5
Contrast Abu Hanifa's 25-year rule with Sahibayn's conditional rule
Abu Hanifa says wealth is given at 25 even without observed maturity, because by then the person is so old that hope of maturity is cut off. Sahibayn say it is not given until maturity is actually observed, as the giving is conditioned on maturity.
The fatwa is on Sahibayn's view.

Source Text

بيان الأهلية
٢٠٤
تعريف السفه وحكمه
وذلك لا يوجب خللا في الأهلية، ولا يمنع شيئا من أحكام الشرع من الوجوب له وعليه؛ فيكون مطالبًا بالأحكام كلها، ويمنع ماله عنه، أي مال السفيه عن السفيه في أول ما يبلغ إجماعاً بالنص، وهو قوله: ﴿وَلا تُؤْتُوا السُّفَهَاءَ أَمْوَالَكُمُ الَّتِي جَعَلَ اللَّهُ لَكُمْ قِيَاما﴾ وفي الآية (النساء: ٥) توجيهان: أحدهما أن تكون المعنى على ظاهره أي لا تؤتوا يا أيها الأولياء، السفهاء من الأزواج والأولاد أموالكم التي جعل الله لكم فيها قيامًا؛ لأنهم يضيّعونها بلا تدبير، ثم تحتاجون
بيان للسفهاء
أموالكم
إليه لأجل نفقاتهم، ولا يؤتونكم، وحينئذ لا يكون الآية مما نحن فيه، والثاني: أن يكون معنى أموالكم أموالهم، وإنما أضيفت إليهم لأجل القيام بتدبيرها، وحينئذ يكون تمسكًا لِمَا نحن فيه، أي لا تؤتوا السفهاء أموالهم التي جعل الله لكم فيها تدبيرها وقيامها. ويدلّ على هذا المعنى قوله فيما بعده: ﴿فَإِنْ آنَسْتُمْ مِنْهُمْ رُشْداً فَادْفَعُوا إِلَيْهِمْ أَمْوَالَهُمْ﴾ (النساء : ٦) ولهذا قال أي الأخير أبو يوسف ومحمد رحمها: إنه لا يدفع إليه المال ما لم يؤنس منه الرشد لأجل هذه الآية، وقال أبو حنيفة الله: إذا بلغ خمسا وعشرين سنة يُدفع إليه المال وإن لم يؤنس منه الرشد؛ لأنه يصير المرء في هذه المدة جدًا؛ إذ وفى مدّة البلوغ اثنا عشر سنة، وأدنى مدة الحمل ستة أشهر، فيصير حينئذ أبا، وإذا ضوعف ذلك يصير جدًا، فلا يفيد منع المال بعده، وذلك: أي السفه لا يوجب خللاً في الأهلية أي أهلية الوجوب والأداء.(القمر)
من الوجوب له أي لنفعه وعليه أي ضرراً عليه، فيكون مطالبًا إلخ لأنه مكلّف عاقل بالغ مختار (القمر) قيامًا أي تقومون بها، وتنتعشون، وهذا مؤول بأنها التي من جنس ما جعل الله لكم فيها قيامًا، وسمّي ما به القيام قيامًا للمبالغة، كذا قال البيضاوي. (القمر) مما نحن فيه أي منع مال السفيه عن السفيه. (القمر)
فإن آنستم أي أبصرتم منهم أي من اليتامى رشدًا أي الصلاح في الدين والمال فادفعوا إليهم أموالهم. (القمر) لا يدفع إليه : أي إلى السفيه المال، وعليه الفتوى، كذا قال بحر العلوم مولانا عبد العلي له. (القمر)
لأجل هذه الآية: فإن الدفع معلّق بالرشد، والمعلّق بالشرط لا يوجد قبله. (القمر)
فلا يفيد منع المال: لأنه لما وصل إلى هذا الحد فقد انقطع عنه رجاء الشرط. (القمر)

بيان الأهلية
٢٠٥
تعريف السفر وحكمه
وهذا القدر أي عدم إعطائه المال ممّا أجمعوا عليه ولكنهم اختلفوا في أمر زائد عليه، وهو كونه محجورًا عن التصرفات، فعنده لا يكون محجورًا، وعندهما يكون محجورًا على ما أشار إليه بقوله : وإنه لا يوجب الحجر أصلاً عند أبي حنيفة مطليه، أي سواء كان في أي السفر
تصرف لا يبطله الهزل كالنكاح والعتاق، أو في تصرّف يبطله الهزل كالبيع والإجارة؛ فإن الحجر على الحرّ العاقل البالغ غير مشروع عنده. وكذلك عندهما فيما لا يبطله الهزل، وأما فيما يبطله الهزل يحجر عليه نظرا له كالصبي والمجنون، فلا يصح بيعه، وإجارته وهبته، وسائر تصرفاته؛ لأنه يسرف ماله بهذا الطريق؛ فيكون كلا على المسلمين، ويحتاج لنفقته إلى بيت المال. أي السفية
Statement of Legal Capacity. Definition of Foolishness and its Ruling: That [foolishness] does not cause a defect in legal capacity, nor does it prevent any of the rulings of the Law from being obligatory for him and upon him; thus he is required to fulfill all rulings, but his wealth is withheld from him, i.e., the wealth of the foolish person is withheld from him at the beginning of his attaining puberty by consensus based on the text, which is His statement: 'And do not give the foolish your wealth which Allah has made for you a means of support' (An-Nisa: 5). Regarding the verse, there are two interpretations: One is that the meaning is literal, i.e., O guardians, do not give the foolish among your spouses and children your wealth which Allah has made for you a means of support, because they waste it without management, then you need it for their expenses, and they will not give it to you; in that case the verse does not concern what we are discussing. The second interpretation is that the meaning of 'your wealth' is 'their wealth', but it is attributed to them because of the management of it; in that case it is a proof for what we are discussing, i.e., do not give the foolish their wealth which Allah has made for you to manage and sustain. This meaning is indicated by His subsequent statement: 'Then if you perceive in them maturity, give them their wealth.' (An-Nisa: 6). Hence Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on them) said: He should not be given the wealth as long as maturity is not perceived in him because of this verse. Abu Hanifa (may Allah be pleased with him) said: When he reaches twenty-five years, the wealth is given to him even if maturity is not perceived in him, because by this time the person becomes a grandfather; since the period of puberty is twelve years, and the minimum period of pregnancy is six months, then he becomes a father, and when that is doubled, he becomes a grandfather, so withholding the wealth afterward is of no benefit. And that: i.e., foolishness does not cause a defect in legal capacity, i.e., capacity for obligation and performance. Of obligation for him i.e., for his benefit, and upon him i.e., for harm upon him, so he is required etc. because he is a responsible sane adult of free choice. 'Support' i.e., by which you sustain yourselves and prosper; this is interpreted as 'that which is of the kind that Allah has made for you as support', and the means of support is called 'support' by way of exaggeration, as al-Baydawi said. 'What we are discussing' i.e., withholding the wealth of the foolish person from him. 'Then if you perceive' i.e., you see, from them i.e., the orphans, 'maturity' i.e., righteousness in religion and wealth, 'give them their wealth.' 'He should not be given' i.e., the wealth should not be given to the foolish person; the fatwa is upon this, as said by Bahr al-Ulum Mawlana Abd al-Ali. 'Because of this verse': because the giving is conditioned upon maturity, and that which is conditioned upon a condition does not occur before it. 'So withholding the wealth is of no benefit': because when it reaches this limit, the hope of the condition has been cut off. 'And this amount' i.e., not giving him the wealth, is what they agreed upon, but they differed on an additional matter, which is whether he is interdicted from transactions. According to him (Abu Hanifa), he is not interdicted, and according to them (the two Sahibs), he is interdicted, as indicated by his statement: 'And it does not cause interdiction at all according to Abu Hanifa, whether in a transaction that jest does not invalidate like marriage and manumission, or in a transaction that jest invalidates like sale and lease; because interdiction of a free sane adult is not legislated according to him. Similarly according to them in what jest does not invalidate. As for what jest invalidates, he is interdicted for his benefit like the minor and the insane, so his sale, lease, gift, and all his transactions are invalid; because he wastes his wealth in this way, thus he becomes a burden upon Muslims, and needs his expenses from the treasury.'
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the legal capacity (ahliyyah) of a foolish person (safih). The author first establishes that safah does not affect the core of legal capacity: the safih remains mukallaf, required to perform worship and subject to prohibitions. What is affected is his property: at the onset of puberty, by consensus and based on the Quranic verse (4:5), his wealth is withheld to protect it from waste. Two interpretations of the verse are given: one that it addresses guardians regarding their own wealth (not directly relevant), and the second that it addresses guardians regarding the wealth of the foolish themselves (which is relevant). The latter interpretation is supported by the next verse (4:6). This leads to a disagreement: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that wealth is not given until maturity is observed, citing the verse. Abu Hanifa, however, says that if the person reaches 25 years, the wealth is given even without observed maturity, because by then (12 years of puberty plus 6 months gestation doubled) he becomes a grandfather, and the hope of maturity is cut off. The passage then notes that the disagreement extends to interdiction (hajr): Abu Hanifa denies interdiction for a free sane adult, while the two Sahibs interdict in transactions that jest invalidates (like sales) to protect his wealth, analogizing to a minor or insane person. The fatwa is reportedly on the opinion of the Sahibs.

Key Terms
السفه (al-safah): Foolishness or prodigality that leads to wasting wealth without proper management.
الأهلية (al-ahliyyah): Legal capacity, divided into capacity for obligation (wujub) and capacity for performance (ada).
الحجر (al-hajr): Interdiction: restriction from conducting transactions on one's property.
الرشد (al-rushd): Maturity in religion and financial management, the condition for releasing wealth to the safih.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis for withholding the safih's wealth at the onset of puberty?
A) Ijma (consensus) based on Quran 4:5
B) The opinion of Abu Hanifa only
C) Qiyas (analogy) to minors
D) Istihsan (juristic preference)

Key Takeaway
Safah does not impair legal capacity, but at puberty the safih's wealth is withheld by consensus based on Quran 4:5, with a subsequent dispute on when it may be released.

6 min
The Dispute on Interdiction (Hajr) of the Safih
Intra-Hanafi dispute on hajr of safih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between Abu Hanifa's and Sahibayn's positions on hajr of the safih and identify the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa says no interdiction for a free sane adult; Sahibayn interdict to prevent waste that burdens the treasury.

After establishing the consensus on withholding the safih's wealth, the passage turns to a more contentious issue: whether the safih is also interdicted (mahjur) from performing transactions. Abu Hanifa maintains that a free sane adult cannot be interdicted at all, while his two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue for interdiction in transactions that jest would invalidate, such as sale and lease. This lesson unpacks their reasoning and the practical consequence of their disagreement.

Guided Path
1
Restate the agreed point
The wealth of the safih is withheld at puberty; this is not disputed.
2
State the new question
Does the safih also lose the right to conduct transactions (hajr)?
This is an additional restriction beyond withholding.
3
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa: No hajr at all, even in transactions that jest invalidates. His reasoning: interdiction on a free sane adult is not legislated.
He considers the safih fully capable of valid contracts.
4
State Sahibayn's position
Sahibayn: He is interdicted in transactions that jest invalidates (e.g., sale, lease, gift) but not in those that jest does not invalidate (e.g., marriage, manumission). Their reasoning: qiyas to minor and insane, and to prevent him from becoming a burden on the treasury.
They distinguish based on the nature of the transaction.
5
Identify the fatwa position
The commentator notes that the fatwa is on the opinion of the Sahibayn, i.e., the safih is interdicted in such transactions.
This is the operative ruling for muftis today.

Source Text

Commentary

Key Terms
السفه (al-safah): Foolishness or prodigality that leads to wasting wealth without proper management.
الحجر (al-hajr): Interdiction: restriction from conducting transactions on one's property.
الهزل (al-hazl): Jest or joking; some transactions are invalidated if accompanied by jest (e.g., sale, lease), while others are not (e.g., marriage, manumission).
الفتوى (al-fatwa): The operative juridical opinion given by a mufti.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school, a safih's gift (hiba) is:
A) Valid, because a gift is not a sale.
B) Invalid, because a gift is a transaction that jest invalidates.
C) Valid only if the recipient is a relative.
D) Invalid according to Abu Hanifa but valid according to Sahibayn.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's mufta bihi position interdicts the safih in transactions that are invalidated by jest (like sale, lease, gift) to protect his wealth, though Abu Hanifa himself did not accept interdiction for any transactions.

Safar (Travel) as a Cause of Alleviation
Defining travel and its role as a cause for rukhsah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi legal definition of travel (safar), identify its minimum duration, and explain why travel itself—not actual hardship—serves as a cause (sabab) for rukhsah, contrasting it with illness.

Core Idea
Travel itself—not the hardship experienced—is the legal cause for alleviations in the Hanafi school.

In Hanafi usul, certain conditions trigger legal alleviations (rukhsah) that modify normal obligations. Travel is one such condition. This passage defines what constitutes legal travel and explains the reasoning (ta'lil) behind why travel itself—not the actual hardship—is considered the cause. It also contrasts travel with illness, where the cause is not the illness itself but the harm it causes to fasting.

Guided Path
1
Extract the Legal Definition of Safar
Read the passage carefully and identify the core definition: travel is a 'protracted exit from one's residence with the intention of journeying'. Note the minimum duration stated.
The minimum is three days, measured by moderate walking.
2
Analyze the Components of the Definition
Break down the definition into its constituent elements: exit (khuruj), protracted (mudid), from residence (an mawdi' al-iqamah), with intention (ala qasd al-sayr). Understand that intention is key.
This distinguishes travel from mere wandering.
3
Understand the Effect on Legal Capacity
The passage explicitly states that travel does not negate legal capacity (ahliyyah) because the traveler retains intellect and physical ability. Understand that travel is not a disability but a circumstance.
Thus the traveler remains a mukallaf.
4
Grasp the Ta'lil: Travel as a Cause for Rukhsah
The passage argues that travel is a cause for alleviation 'by itself absolutely' because it is a source of hardship. Crucially, the law presumes hardship, so whether actual hardship exists or not, the rulings apply. This is a key point.
This is why a comfortable flight still allows qasr and iftar.
5
Contrast Travel with Illness
The passage contrasts travel with illness: illness is not automatically a cause for rukhsah; only illness that harms fasting or is feared to do so qualifies. Understand why the ta'lil differs.
Illness varies, so the cause is the harm, not the illness label.
